Discussion Title: The Ethics of Eating Animals: Is Eating Meat Wrong?

1. Humans should stop eating animal meat.
1.1. Con: The taste of meat is delicious and brings many people pleasure in a manner that vegetarian food cannot fully imitate.
1.1.1. Pro: The demand for meat is rising globally. This clearly indicates its high popularity.
1.1.1.1. Con: In the USA meat consumption is actually on the [decline](https://www.fastcoexist.com/3027191/the-us-has-passed-peak-meat-the-rest-of-the-world-is-just-getting-started). It decreased from 184 pounds per person in 2004 to 167 pounds in 2014.
1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Especially, the consumption of [red meat](http://fortune.com/2015/10/27/red-meat-consumption-decline/) is on a decline.
1.1.1.1.2. Con: This citation focuses on specific dates to justify their "peak meat" claims. Other analysis has shown that 2014 was just one of many short term troughs before meat consumption jumped right back up to historic high levels  has.
1.1.1.1.3. Con: Meat consumption in the US is not declining because the taste of meat is falling out of favor, but [because of](http://www.theguardian.com/sustainable-business/sustainable-meat-vegan-vegetarian-celebrities) rising awareness about the health and environmental risks of eating meat, and rising prices.
1.1.1.2. Con: Vegetarianism has increased in a number of countries over the last 5 years.
1.1.1.2.1. Pro: The [number of vegetarians in NZ](http://www.roymorgan.com/findings/6663-vegetarians-on-the-rise-in-new-zealand-june-2015-201602080028) \(of those 14 years or older\) increased from 8.1% in 2011 to 10.3% in 2015.
1.1.1.2.2. Pro: Between 2012 and 2016, the percentage of Australians whose diet is all or almost all vegetarian has [risen from 9.7% of the population to 11.2%.](http://www.roymorgan.com/findings/vegetarianisms-slow-but-steady-rise-in-australia-201608151105)
1.1.1.2.3. Pro: In 2014, the UK reported that [a record number of British adults were following vegetarian or vegan diets](http://www.express.co.uk/life-style/health/517246/Vegetarians-are-on-the-increase-in-Britain), with numbers estimated at around 12% of the population.
1.1.1.3. Con: The raise of demand of a product does not necessarily indicate it has a higher popularity. It could indicate the lack of the product, the increase of the customer or any other factor that could unbalance the demand versus offer balance.
1.1.1.3.1. Con: Demand and supply are different, a decrease of supply is not called an increase in demand, it's called a decrease in supply, an increase in consumption and prices signals higher demand, a decrease in both, lower demand, an increase in consumption but decrease in price marks lower supply, and the opposite a shortage of supply. But a raise in popularity is literally a rise in demand.
1.1.1.3.2. Con: Not "necessarily" but a pretty good inference.
1.1.1.3.3. Pro: Meat consumption is related to living standards. This could explain the rising of demand: the more developing countries develop the more meat is demanded. [data.oecd.org](https://data.oecd.org/agroutput/meat-consumption.htm)
1.1.1.4. Pro: Steak \(beef\) and chicken are [ranked very highly](http://www.ibtimes.com/worlds-top-10-favorite-foods-551923) among the world's favorite foods.
1.1.1.4.1. Con: Just because something is ranked very highly doesn't make it ethical or justify its lack of morality.
1.1.1.5. Pro: Generally, rising incomes and urbanization in developing countries lead to a higher [demand](http://www.voanews.com/content/decapua-farm-animals-29mar12-144898655/179917.html) of animals products and meat.
1.1.1.5.1. Pro: In [China](http://www.takepart.com/article/2015/10/13/china-meat-consumption), with a growing population and a growing middle class, the demand for meat has risen and is expected to continue to rise.
1.1.1.5.1.1. Pro: The fact that economic development is correlated with increased consumption of meat indicates that many people refrain from consuming meat not because they don't want to but because of an inability to afford it.
1.1.1.5.1.1.1. Con: A correlation between wealth and consumption of meat could instead indicate that meat consumption is a status symbol, rather than something intrinsically desirable.
1.1.1.5.1.2. Pro: The [average](http://www.takepart.com/article/2015/06/29/china-insatiable-appetite) Chinese person now consumes fives times more pork than in 1979.
1.1.1.5.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.5.1.1.
1.1.1.6. Pro: As poor countries grow richer and experience economic as well as cultural change, even in vegetarian-heavy places like India meat consumption is [becoming more popular](http://www.nydailynews.com/life-style/eats/india-changing-appetites-include-meat-article-1.1255861) and vegetarianism is [falling out of favor](http://www.dw.com/en/vegetarians-developing-a-taste-for-meat/a-16490496).
1.1.1.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.5.1.1.
1.1.1.7. Pro: In [South Africa](http://gain.fas.usda.gov/Recent%20GAIN%20Publications/The%20South%20African%20meat%20market_Pretoria_South%20Africa%20-%20Republic%20of_9-15-2015.pdf), spending on meat increased from $3.5 billion US in 2005 to $12.7 billion US in 2015.
1.1.1.8. Pro: As this [model](http://www.nistads.res.in/indiasnt2008/images/it6rural/t6rur15_fig3.jpg) shows, meat consumption has been increasing in the last 30 years, in the developed world as well as in the developing world.
1.1.1.9. Pro: Across the world per capita meat consumption has been [steadily rising](http://www.who.int/nutrition/topics/3_foodconsumption/en/index4.html) and will continue to do so at least until 2030.
1.1.2. Con: Non-meat products can offer an equivalently pleasing food experience.
1.1.2.1. Pro: Soy or seitan products can exhibit a big variety of tastes because of the different spices added.
1.1.2.2. Pro: The taste of vegetables, fruits and grains is popular as well.
1.1.2.3. Con: Unless the taste, smell, texture and consistency of meat can be precisely imitated, some people would disagree. This point has not yet been reached, hence non-meat products do not offer an equivalent experience to everybody.
1.1.2.3.1. Con: Meat analogues based on soy protein or wheat gluten are [getting close](http://spectrum.ieee.org/energy/environment/the-better-meat-substitute) to imitating the taste and texture of real meat and have been part of the [food culture](http://edition.cnn.com/2014/01/15/travel/10-things-taiwan/) in places such as Taiwan for a long time.
1.1.2.3.1.1. Pro: Companies such as [Impossible Foods](https://www.impossiblefoods.com/burger/) and [Beyond Meat](http://beyondmeat.com/products/view/beyond-burger) are gaining momentum all the time elsewhere in the world as well, with the former opening its first large-scale production plant and the latter being sold in WholeFoods across the USA. Reviews of their products so far are very positive, with a 'meat-centric' celebrity chef [debuting the Impossible Burger](http://www.detroitnews.com/story/entertainment/dining/2017/09/15/michael-symon-debuts-plant-based-impossible-burger-royal-oak/105637090/) at one of his restaurants.
1.1.2.3.1.2. Con: Soy in particular but also other legumes, pulses and grains contain varying amounts of phytoestrogens. There is ongoing debate as to whether they can be consumed in quantity by males without undesirable side effects such as reduction in the production of male hormones and increasing feminisation.
1.1.2.3.1.3. Pro: Lab-grown meat is predicted to be on-offer in a restaurant within a few years. Inasmuch as the normalization of lab-grown meat lowers the bar for eating non-animal meat—thereby exerting pressure on animal-meat eaters \(all else equal\)—and inasmuch as quantified, aggregated predictions serve as evidence for the likelihood of an event, a prediction \([like this one](https://www.metaculus.com/questions/395/a-restaurant-serving-cultured-meat-by-2021/)\) that a restaurant will serve cultured meat by 2021 supports the "Eating Meat is Wrong" argument.
1.1.2.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.1.
1.1.2.5. Con: If that actually were the case, people wouldn't be eating meat.
1.1.2.5.1. Con: There has been reluctance among meat eaters to try other alternatives. Recent advancements in non-meat alternatives, combined with recipes etc. at our fingertips, could open people up to other ways of eating, if tried.
1.1.2.5.1.1. Con: While that claim is true, it is also true that many meat eaters *have* tried these alternatives, and although to many they taste good, they do not take the place of meat.
1.1.2.5.1.2. Pro: The technology on this is experiencing somewhat of a renaissance with products like [the Impossible Burger](https://www.impossiblefoods.com/burger/) creating very convincing meat substitutes.
1.1.2.5.2. Con: Increasing numbers of people are taking up vegetarianism and veganism.
1.1.2.5.3. Con: There are reasons beyond the taste and pleasure for why people continue to eat meat - authorities suggesting it \(whether parents in childhood or dieticians/dietary specialists/diet-writers\), the social acceptance of and ease of access to meat, encouragement from others to eat meat, other social factors, etc.
1.1.2.6. Con: If it were the case that non-meat products were universally as good as meat, then vegetarians would not try, and also not to such a degree fail, to replicate the taste of meat.
1.1.2.6.1. Pro: This is because vegetarians still like the [taste of meat](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/ed-coffin/why-do-vegans-eat-fake-me_b_3543316.html), despite being aware of the consequences.
1.1.2.7. Con: Meat imitation products are expensive and are not a viable option for low-income individuals and families.
1.1.2.7.1. Con: As technology advances and production scales up, they will become more affordable and available.
1.1.2.7.1.1. Con: But they are not that yet. Arguments can't be made through hypotheticals and predictions. Once they are in fact affordable you will have an argument. Until then this is baseless assumption.
1.1.2.7.1.1.1. Con: This debate suggests a future action - that we should stop eating meat. That future will not be the same as the present, both due to whatever decision we \(as all humanity\) make on continuing to eat meat, and other factors. As such, hypotheticals and predictions regarding the future are highly relevant, especially hypotheticals and predictions regarding factors which will be affected by continuing or ceasing to eat meat.
1.1.2.8. Pro: Faux meats are getting better over time as more people demand it. With more demand fake meats will taste better.
1.1.2.9. Con: The very knowledge that one is eating an animal is pleasurable to many people and cannot be imitated with non-animal products. Certain meats carry status in many cultures, such as beef in the US.
1.1.2.10. Pro: [Artificial meat](http://www.sciencemag.org/news/2017/03/artificial-chicken-grown-cells-gets-taste-test-who-will-regulate-it), which imitates the taste of real meat but is lab-grown, is being developed and could replace the taste experiences of real meat without the harm caused to animals, and with significantly less environmental consequences.
1.1.2.10.1. Pro: Memphis Meats is already producing lab grown meat from animal cells.
1.1.2.10.2. Con: Lab grown meat is not absolutely and objectively preferable to animal meat.
1.1.2.10.2.1. Pro: Previous artificial "improvements" and products have later been shown to have downsides that were not immediately apparent e.g. pollution from industry, carcinogenic substances, toxins like asbestos and lead paints which were not immediately identified before being widely used.
1.1.2.10.2.2. Pro: The production of artificial meat still costs too much energy. [7-45% less energy cost](https://phys.org/news/2011-06-lab-grown-meat-emissions-energy.html) will not be a viable solution for the growing meat demand in the world.
1.1.2.10.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.1.
1.1.2.10.4. Con: Long term studies must be done to evaluate the health impact of regular consumption of lab grown meat before it is considered a viable alternative.
1.1.2.10.5. Con: If lab-grown animal protein analogues are an acceptable resolution to the problem of eating meat, it follows that the quarrel is not strictly with eating meat but with some secondary consequence of it.
1.1.2.11. Pro: Vegetarian food offers more choices when meat is taken off the food plate. Usually there are small number of meat choices \(mostly chicken or beef with the occasional turkey, fish, and seafood\). The substitutions for this are numerous, from extra sides to faux meats.
1.1.2.12. Pro: In fact, meat itself has little to no taste, it's the texture it has and spices and flavors we add to it that makes it delicious. Other textured proteins like soy can have the same delicious taste and be almost unrecognizable.
1.1.2.12.1. Con: The fact that meat has little to no taste can be refuted by anyone who has already tasted meat directly from the producer with no spices or other additives.
1.1.2.12.2. Con: Broths from meat are often used to season foods or as a base for foods.  For example, some soups may start with a chicken broth because it has a better taste than just using water.
1.1.2.13. Pro: Taste is an acquired habit. Some cultures that eat dogs, snakes, rabbits, snails etc. also do it because they acquired those tastes even though in other cultures eating one or more of those animals is considered disgusting. Same is with vegan food. There are several cultures that promote vegetarianism and of late veganism has also grown significantly. Also, all spices and flavorful ingredients added to food to enrich taste, like pepper, chilies, garlic, ginger, basil etc are all in fact, plants.
1.1.2.14. Pro: Eating is pleasurable in general. Finding more pleasure in one food type than in another is subjective and largely determined by personal experience with recepies and cooking, family traditions, memories, habits of one's environment, etc.
1.1.2.14.1. Pro: In vegetarian cultures like for example Indian Jainism eating meat is regarded as being far less pleasurable, rather vulgar and less refined than a vegetarian meal prepared with the proper skills.
1.1.2.15. Pro: Stopping eating meat just means dropping a few ingredients. There are lots and lots of ingredients left to use and be creative with.
1.1.3. Pro: Meat is convenient and consumer friendly.
1.1.3.1. Con: Human behavior should not simply be based upon questions of convenience, as other factors weigh heavier.
1.1.3.1.1. Pro: If people were to act only based upon convenience, this would lead to a wide neglect of dutiful and/or moral behaviour \(e.g. going to work, recycling garbage etc.\)
1.1.3.2. Pro: It is sometimes difficult to be on a meatless diet, especially if you do not have the time to cook for yourself or if you eat out with friends.
1.1.3.2.1. Con: You do not necessarily need time to cook if you are a vegetarian. Most fruits and vegetables can be consumed in their raw state or with little preparation.
1.1.3.2.2. Con: Not having time to cook as a meateater is even more difficult, as meat generally \(with only very few exceptions\) has to be prepared.
1.1.3.2.3. Con: It is only difficult to stay on a meatless diet because meat is so ubiquitous under the status quo. If less people ate meat, more vegetarian options would become available.
1.1.3.2.3.1. Con: Individuals should make their decisions about whether or not to consume meat based on the situation they face, which is the status quo. The status quo therefore relevant when determining whether or not an individual should eat meat.
1.1.3.3. Con: There are many meatless foods which are also convenient and consumer friendly, such as bread, pasta, fruits, cookies etc.
1.1.3.4. Con: Not eating meat is generally [cheaper](http://www.fao.org/worldfoodsituation/foodpricesindex/en/).
1.1.3.4.1. Con: Since [1978](http://economix.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/05/20/whats-wrong-with-this-chart/?mtrref=undefined&gwh=57859188BBA6F6C85580BF7D06FEB4CA&gwt=pay) the price for fresh fruits and vegetables has been rising, while the price for meat is declining.
1.1.3.4.1.1. Con: This suggests that meat may be cheaper than fruits and vegetables in the future, yet it does not tell us whether meat is cheaper right now.
1.1.3.4.1.2. Con: Meat prices [rise](http://blogs.wsj.com/economics/2014/07/22/vegans-rejoice-meat-prices-rising-more-than-fresh-fruits-and-vegetables/) faster than vegetable prices in the recent years. This indicates a trend change.
1.1.3.4.2. Con: Since people still choose to eat meat despite the relatively higher price, this indicates that eating meat is very pleasurable for them.
1.1.3.4.3. Con: It is not plausible for some people to live solely on a diet without meats. The reason it would be impossible at the current moment is that the pricing of fruits and vegetables [costs more per calorie](https://well.blogs.nytimes.com/2007/12/05/a-high-price-for-healthy-food/) than meat and is not possible for many families with a lower budget.
1.1.3.4.4. Con: Meat is often cheaper and easier to store for low-income households
1.1.3.4.5. Pro: Unprocessed vegetarian products, which can be used as meat replacements, are cheaper than meat itself.
1.1.3.4.5.1. Con: -> See 1.1.3.4.1.
1.1.3.4.5.2. Con: Unprocessed vegetarian products, such as lentils and unprocessed soy, are bland without seasoning and taste nothing like meat; processed meatless products - those that claim to be the closest in flavour to, and therefore the closest literal 'replacements' of, their meat equivalents - are more expensive than meat.
1.1.3.4.5.2.1. Pro: The Beyond Meat Burger, which claims to look and taste almost [exactly like a beef burger](http://metro.co.uk/2017/01/09/theres-now-a-vegan-burger-so-realistic-it-actually-bleeds-6370330/), was being sold at $5.99 \(£4.93\) for two 4oz patties at the time of its launch; real beef burgers, even if gourmet, cost [the same or much less](https://www.google.co.uk/search?biw=1241&bih=675&tbm=shop&q=beef+burgers&oq=beef+burgers&gs_l=psy-ab.3..0l3.141392.144745.0.145051.8.8.0.0.0.0.188.900.2j5.7.0....0...1.1.64.psy-ab..4.2.264....0.Jy3K59uATdc) than this.
1.1.3.4.5.2.2. Con: Specialty foods like prepared veggie burgers can be more expensive than their non-vegetarian counterparts, but this is the case with most pre-prepared food, vegetarian or otherwise; buying specialty products is not necessary to lead a satisfying and nutritious \(vegetarian\) lifestyle.
1.1.3.4.5.3. Pro: When comparing the average price of non-animal protein with animal protein \(especially beef\), vegetarian products tend to [cost less](http://plenteousveg.com/cost-vegan-protein-vs-animal-protein/).
1.1.3.4.5.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.4.1.2.
1.1.3.4.6. Pro: Meat is so expensive that the [world's most expensive food comes from an animal](http://www.businessinsider.com/most-valuable-substances-by-weight-2014-9/#19-white-truffles-1).
1.1.3.4.7. Pro: The [most expensive](http://ajcn.nutrition.org/content/92/5/1181.long) element of American food servings are animal products such as meats and poultry.
1.1.3.4.8. Pro: According to [one study](http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/19320248.2015.1045675?journalCode=when20&), a vegetarian meal plan can be cheaper than a meat-based meal plan with the same nutritional value and impact on chronic disease risk.
1.1.3.4.9. Pro: As the production of meat is more expensive than a vegetarian based food industry, the market price of meatless foods is by logic cheaper.
1.1.3.4.9.1. Con: The link between production and retail price is often weak. The production costs of razor blades, for [example](http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-1191456/Sharp-practice-The-razor-heads-cost-just-5p-make-sell-2-43-each.html), is 5p while the retail price stands at £2.43.
1.1.3.4.9.2. Pro: The impact of production price on retail price depends on the [elasticity of demand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Price_elasticity_of_demand) for meat. As this is [low](http://ageconsearch.umn.edu/bitstream/162022/2/j.1467-8489.2010.00505.x.pdf) for meat the production costs can directly be burdened on the consumer.
1.1.3.5. Pro: There are many restaurants that do not offer meatless products.
1.1.3.5.1. Con: If more humans stop eating meat entirely, there will be a greater incentive for restaurants and supermarkets to develop a broader range of vegetarian food options.
1.1.3.5.2. Con: Many "classic" dishes  - such as pizza, pasta, sushi, gratins or potato bake - are in fact meatless.
1.1.3.5.3. Con: Most restaurant offer at least some forms of salads. Plus, side dishes are nearly always meatless.
1.1.3.5.3.1. Pro: The Chinese cuisine offers a huge variety of vegetarian [side dishes](http://www.vegetarian-china.info/#dishes).
1.1.3.5.4. Con: Even in a steakhouse/churrascaria you will be able to order meatless sides such as green beans, a salad or a variety of sides based on potatos.
1.1.3.5.5. Con: Even food chains like McDonald's offer meatless products such as french fries or a dedicated veggie burger.
1.1.3.5.5.1. Pro: The most popular McDonald's product is a [meatless](https://www.quora.com/What-are-McDonalds-ten-most-popular-products) one: french fries.
1.1.3.5.5.1.1. Con: French fries are only the most frequent dish because they are served with every other meal. This blurs the statistic.
1.1.3.5.6. Pro: In countries like South Korea and China restaurants that specialize in barbecue and fried chicken are among the most popular places for social outings but they usually have no vegetarian dishes on offer.
1.1.3.5.6.1. Con: If you are a non-meat eater or want to go out with a friend who is, you would obviously not choose a restaurant that specializes in barbecue and fried chicken.
1.1.3.5.6.1.1. Pro: BBQ and fried chicken joints are not the only available restaurants in countries \(South Korea, China\) with such a rich variety in its cusine.
1.1.3.5.6.2. Con: Korean barbecue comes with [many side dishes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_barbecue#Side_dishes_served_with_gogigui) such as green onion salad or a fresh vegetable dish including lettuce, cucumbers and peppers.
1.1.3.5.6.2.1. Con: As the argument states, only the side dishes are meat-free. The argument that a meatless diet comes with obstacles in certain countries is thus sustained.
1.1.3.5.6.3. Con: -> See 1.1.3.5.3.1.
1.1.3.5.6.4. Con: Typical main dishes served with BBQ include [Jamji jjigae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kimchi_jjigae), [Doenjang jjigae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doenjang_jjigae) or [Naengmyeon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naengmyeon).
1.1.3.6. Con: Meat has to be prepared, whereas most vegetables can already be consumed in their raw state.
1.1.3.6.1. Con: Tomatoes are [healthier](http://www.news.cornell.edu/stories/2002/04/cooking-tomatoes-boosts-disease-fighting-power) when they are processed with heat.
1.1.3.6.1.1. Con: However, vitamin C levels [declined](http://www.scientificamerican.com/article/raw-veggies-are-healthier/) by 10% in tomatoes cooked for two minutes—and 29% in tomatoes that were cooked for half an hour at 190.4 degrees F \(88 degrees C\).
1.1.3.6.2. Pro: Some veggies, including broccoli, are even [healthier](http://www.scientificamerican.com/article/raw-veggies-are-healthier/) raw rather than cooked.
1.1.3.6.3. Con: In certain cases meat can be eaten raw.
1.1.3.6.3.1. Pro: [Carpaccio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpaccio) is a traditional starter dish, containing raw meat.
1.1.3.6.3.2. Pro: [Steak tartare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steak_tartare) is a dish made from finely chopped or minced meat.
1.1.3.6.3.3. Pro: The [Inuit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inuit_diet#Food_sharing_in_the_community) are known for eating raw meat.
1.1.3.6.3.3.1. Con: The Inuit live in a geographical area characterized by very cold temperatures almost for the whole year. Therefore they do not have to worry about foul meat like elsewhere in the world.
1.1.3.6.4. Con: Quite a few vegetables need cooking as well.
1.1.3.6.4.1. Pro: Potatoes, a staple of lots of vegetarian diets, need to be cooked.
1.1.3.6.4.2. Pro: Leguminous plants, very often used as meat replacement, need to be cooked before eaten.
1.1.3.6.5. Pro: All salad vegetables can be consumed raw.
1.1.3.7. Pro: Not eating meat limits food options. [Four out of ten](https://faunalytics.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/Faunalytics_Current-Former-Vegetarians_Full-Report.pdf) former vegetarians state that it was difficult to stay "pure" in terms of their diet and that they were bored with the available food options.
1.1.3.7.1. Con: "Getting bored" with available food options may be a result of a lack of cooking skills, rather than specifically related to being vegetarian.
1.1.3.7.2. Con: -> See 1.1.3.5.1.
1.1.3.7.3. Con: Focusing on having meat as the central part of your diet limits your overall food options, since other non-meat alternatives, many richer in nutrients, in a variety of plant based products are overlooked as possible main courses.
1.1.3.7.3.1. Con: Not everybody who eats meat "focuses on having \[it\] as the central part of \[their\] diet". Many dishes include meat as only one component, but this is still enough to be considered "eating meat" and thus, not strictly vegetarian.
1.1.3.7.4. Con: Many moral life choices are difficult, and many immoral life choices are easy. The difficulty or ease of a choice has very little bearing on the morality of that choice.
1.1.3.8. Pro: In a more precarious context, with a small budget and little time, pleasure can more easily be found through meat consumption. The food market is still largely organised around meat consumption, making it easily accesible and cheap through mass-production. Quality cooking without meat requires more skill, more time and more fresh ingredients.
1.1.3.9. Con: Although meat is convenient and consumer-friendly in the short run, our current levels of meat consumption are harmful to [the climate](https://www.chathamhouse.org/publication/changing-climate-changing-diets), [our health](http://www.bbc.com/news/health-28797106) and thus the convenience of our existence in the long run.
1.1.3.9.1. Pro: If the externalities of meat were properly priced in, meat production would be far less economically efficient than the production of crops.
1.1.3.9.1.1. Pro: Mass produced meat is not sustainable regarding increase of CO2 and consumption of nitrogen by plants used to feed livestock. The real cost of meat is [much higher](http://www.nytimes.com/2012/04/13/opinion/the-myth-of-sustainable-meat.html?_r=1) than the current consumer price.
1.1.3.9.1.2. Pro: Meat has serious [public health consequences](http://citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/download?doi=10.1.1.365.5425&rep=rep1&type=pdf).
1.1.3.9.1.2.1. Con: This is caused by the quality of the meat. Imagine the meat production where the animal food is contaminated with poisons from the fertilizers and other farming products. These bad substances get into the animal meat in the fat and from there to our human bodies. The distinction between bad meat \(mass farming\) and good meat \(grass fed free-range\) must be made in order to draw health consequence conclusions. [PubMed: GBHs in food.](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4756530/)
1.1.3.9.1.3. Pro: Livestock farming can only be beneficial for the economy in the short term. Over the long term, the economy will be harmed by climate change induced from farm CO2 and methane emissions as well as land degradation
1.1.3.9.2. Pro: A peer-reviewed [2004 study](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/a_prospective_study_of_red_meat_consumption_and_type2_diabetes.pdf) from Harvard researchers found that eating meat increases the risk of getting type 2 diabetes in women.
1.1.3.9.3. Pro: Studies have linked heme iron found in red meat with an increased risk of colon and rectal [cancer](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10582688). Vegetarian sources of iron like leafy greens and beans contain [non-heme iron](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/nih_dietary_supplement_fact_sheet_on_iron.pdf).
1.1.3.9.3.1. Pro: The finding that red meat increases the risk of colon cancer was confirmed in an [observatory study](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8162586) of US citizens in which red meat featured as prominent factor.
1.1.3.9.3.2. Con: Studies on the effects of red meat intake do not account for the differences in processed and un-processed meat, which is unacceptable because the two have vastly different effects.
1.1.3.9.3.3. Con: A [meta-analysis](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20663065) of red meat-cancer studies found that the link is, at best, weak.
1.1.3.9.3.3.1. Pro: Further meta-analysis found that the red meat-cancer connection holds only slightly for [men](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21540747) and not for females.
1.1.3.9.3.4. Pro: When meat is cooked excessively, [carcinogens](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15199546) can be produced that are linked to cancer.
1.1.3.9.3.4.1. Con: This can be avoided by cooking meat carefully and in accordance with safety guidelines.
1.1.3.9.3.4.1.1. Con: Nobody will ever cook meat perfectly every time, and oftentimes \(e.g. in restaurants\) lay people will trust professional cooks, who may have an improper, incomplete, or out of date education/training.
1.1.3.10. Pro: Processed meat products such as hot dogs or [BiFi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BiFi) are easy to consume to-go products.
1.1.3.10.1. Con: Processed products on the basis of meat substitutes \(soy sausages etc.\) are comparably easy to consume.
1.1.3.10.2. Con: So are most kinds of fruits without a hard shell \(such as bananas, apples, oranges, grapes etc.\) and you do not even produce plastic-waste by consuming them to-go. Plus they are healthy as well.
1.1.3.10.2.1. Pro: You do not need cutlery/crockery to consume those.
1.1.3.10.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.10.2.1.
1.1.4. Con: Popularity and pleasure has no relevance to what is right or wrong.
1.1.4.1. Con: Most people live in this common situation : where the satisfaction of most of our basic needs is already distorted, where sleep is sacrificed to save time, where amusement is seen as a waste of productivity, where having hobbies gives a sense of guilt about not using the time and money for more "important" things, where human relations are an open war for understanding, stability and social recognition \(...\)
In such society, eating is the last basic need we can still take pleasure satisfying.
1.1.4.1.1. Con: There is no data to show that "most" people live in this "common" situation.
1.1.4.1.2. Con: Just because other sources of pleasure are rare or stigmatized, does not mean it becomes ethical to indulge in morally questionable sources of pleasure.
1.1.4.1.2.1. Pro: By the logic of the parent claim for this con, someone who is \(for whatever reason\) only in a position to enjoy rape or murder should indulge in those acts, and would be justified in doing so.
1.1.4.2. Con: Concepts of right and wrong are formed by societies, and thus decided by popularity.
1.1.4.2.1. Con: The concepts of right and wrong change as society changes. This changes are made possible by people who think differently to the majority
1.1.4.2.2. Con: This is a typical example of [argumentum ad populum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argumentum_ad_populum), which is a logical fallacy.
1.1.4.3. Pro: As people decide what choices are "right" or "wrong" based on how the choices serve the end goals they happen to value--be those goals the raising the quality of life of the world as a whole, just that of humans, or making more money as an individual--and those goals may not be shared by all of one's population, right and wrong are in fact concepts isolated from popular opinion.
1.1.4.4. Con: Some ethical systems are built upon the concept of pleasure as the highest good, \(hedonic morality\), so pleasure does indeed factor into judgments of right and wrong for the many subscribing to such notions, i.e., meat eaters who hold their preferences in higher regard than the suffering of others.
1.1.4.5. Pro: If popularity or pleasure had any relevance, we would never abolish slavery and could use that to justify any form of exploitation.
1.1.4.6. Pro: It is not morally justifiable to value one's own taste over an animal's life.
1.1.4.6.1. Pro: Human pleasure evaporates quickly while an animal life is lost forever. These after effects make an animal life worth more.
1.1.4.7. Con: Both popularity and pleasure are relevant to "right and wrong", or the concerns of ethics and morality. They certainly do not equate to morality on a one to one basis, not are they interchangeable with ethics or morality, but they are entirely relevant. Nearly every attempt at a cohesive system of ethics must take into account what is pleasurable to the individual and the larger society as well as the beliefs held by the majority of the population.
1.1.4.8. Pro: As the vegetarian diet can satisfy our nutritional needs, eating meat only to satisfy our taste buds is incompatible with a moral or ethical being.
1.1.4.8.1. Pro: Not only is it impossible to say that enjoying the taste of meat is universal but for many the thought of animal suffering accompanies the act and undermines any potential for "pleasure" to be derived from it.
1.1.4.8.1.1. Pro: Killing an animal can only be justified by extreme necessities, such as survival; consuming a living creature just for its taste, for convenience, or out of habit is thus not justifiable.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1. Pro: Humans are not superior to any other animal, they are simply a small part of a whole ecosystem. As such, they have no legitimate right to kill animals as they please.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1. Con: Humans are at the top of the food chain, which means that they are merely following the natural order of things when they kill and eat other animals.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1. Con: There is [no logical connection](https://jakubmarian.com/but-humans-are-at-the-top-of-the-food-chain-argument-against-vegetarianism/) between our current position in the food chain and the justifiability of eating animals. Such a reasoning is circular because what puts animals on a lower level than us is eating them.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: What puts animals on a lower level in the food chain \(and what maintains humans at the top\) are the cognitive, motor and social capabilities of the human species.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: We have used these superior capabilities to create [advanced technology](https://jakubmarian.com/but-humans-are-at-the-top-of-the-food-chain-argument-against-vegetarianism/), thereby giving us tools that help us to hunt or rear animals. This places us at the top.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: [Most people have no idea](https://jakubmarian.com/but-humans-are-at-the-top-of-the-food-chain-argument-against-vegetarianism/) how to hunt, rear animals, or make the necessary tools. Based on this argument it would thus make no sense to say that such a person is “at the top of the food chain”.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Because of the structure of human societies with division of work and other principles, not every human needs those skills. This becomes even more the case the more advanced the technology gets.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: The evolutionary advance of the human species gives them the skill to reason and enables them to rethink their behavior. It lets them decide to not kill animals for food anymore - no matter if there is a right to kill and eat any animal.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1. Pro: Unlike other animals, humans are morally conscious of their behaviour and are thus subject to [moral standards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality), meaning they cannot justify meat consumption on the basis of \(arguments such as\) convenience or their own mental superiority.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.1. Con: Simply stating that humans should be morally conscious does nothing to argue that eating meat is morally wrong.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.1.1. Con: Moral behaviour would likely not include being complicit in the slaughter of animal life for food.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2. Pro: The normalizing of killing animals for food leads to a close-minded population less able to feel empathy and emotions for other species.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.1. Con: Humans feel empathy for their pets.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.1.1. Pro: Since humans feel empathy for their pets, it can not be true that killing animals completely closes our minds, or inhibits our ability to empathize, even with non-human entities.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.1.2. Con: Cognitive dissonance is a result of this. We feel only what we want to feel, because the truth makes us uncomfortable.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.2. Con: It has not been shown that animals have emotions with which to empathize; humans should thus be reciprocal in how they consider other creatures.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.2.1. Con: Many animals will act distressed when either a human or another member of their species they care for dies, and many pets have saved their owners' lives.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.3. Pro: Care for animals and nature is necessary for human survival on this planet in a natural way.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.3.1. Pro: Species are dependent on each other in a healthy working eco-system.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.4. Pro: The exercise of true care is necessary for the human race to evolve and to grow in consciousness.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.4.1. Pro: Empathy is complex and a social skill that helped us thrive and evolutionarily assisted in the development of more complex brains.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.5. Pro: Animals have feelings and positive interaction with animals help us get more connected with nature and in turns make us way more happier beings.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.2.6. Con: This argument seem to suggest that eating meat first started in the last 50 years, or last generation.

Keep in mind humans have been eating meat a lot longer than that, and if your argument is true the issue is already lost, since the close-minded human population already cannot feel emotions.

Since you can, and you are part of humanity, you are living proof that theory does not hold.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.3. Pro: The uniqueness of humanity lies in its ability to reason beyond the forces of entropy and past the constraints of an impulse for survival. Humanity has for the most part conquered survival, and we continue to conquer the vices with which we were born as we progress towards something of a species to be proud of. We must undo these obsolete desires for pleasure as they come at the cost of life. It is in our power, our moral beliefs, and our logical perspective of life as humans to do so.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.3.1. Pro: Eating meat requires, at least for now, killing living and breathing creatures that feel pain and joy same way as we, humans, do. As the smartest species we are obligated to take responsibility for our actions regarding other species, and, especially when eating meat is unnecessary for our survival, it's clear, or at least it should be, that killing other animals only for our pleasure is cruel and despicable.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.4. Pro: Our sapience necessitates moral standard.  A similar argument can be made against homosexuality. The naturalness or temptation of an act does not immediately award permission.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.4.1. Con: Different groups define different standards all the time. Sapience does not require a common standard for all, but for groups \(consensus\).

For example: Homosexuality is being increasingly accepted around the world. Not in spite of sapience, but because of it.

Eating whales, which is common in nordic countries, and eating dogs, which is common in some eastern countries, could be considered immoral by some, but not by them.

[Gay acceptance](https://scholar.google.no/scholar?q=homosexuality+increasingly+accepted&hl=en&as_sdt=0&as_vis=1&oi=scholart&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj3u82807zYAhUGCpoKHdu9CT4QgQMIJTAA)
[Whale - Norwegian food](https://translate.google.com/translate?sl=no&tl=en&js=y&prev=_t&hl=en&ie=UTF-8&u=https%3A%2F%2Fnorskhval.no%2Ffakta%2Fen-unik-ravare%2F&edit-text=&act=url)
[Dog Meat Festival - China](https://www.wikiwand.com/en/Lychee_and_Dog_Meat_Festival)
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.4.2. Con: Naturalness or temptation does not award permission; it awards nothing. Naturalness or temptation are merely concepts, and not sapient in themselves, and as such will not affect the permission of eating meat at all.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.5. Pro: The wholesale slaughter of sentient non-human animals demonstrates that violence is an acceptable human behaviour.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.6. Con: Morality is wholly subjective, this argument presupposes an absolute moral authority counter to popular opinion. Indeed even if we were to follow the prevailing democratic subjective morality, the vast majority regularly eat meat. The idea that killing animals for food or eating meat is 'immoral' one can assume is an opinion held by [less than 10% of the global population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetarianism_by_country) with not a single major territory where it is the prevailing norm.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.7. Con: The assumption that animals are not morally conscious is just that— an assumption. Prove it.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.8. Pro: The more we learn about other animals, especially mammals, the more we learn they're intelligent, feeling beings. It is therefore morally and ethically wrong to continue farming and killing animals, and eating their meat, due to the suffering we cause them \(parent-child separation, cramped conditions, etc\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.9. Pro: We instinctively feel compassion towards animals, while carnivorous animals instinctively try to kill weaker species. E.g. Put a toddler and a rabbit in a crib, \(s\)he will hug it; put a lion cub and a rabbit in a crib, it will try to eat it.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.9.1. Con: This is an unreliable phenomenon. Whether this is an actual instinct or an instinct that are commonly warped by experience, is hard to discern. For many people the compasionate instinct described doesn't exist and the this version of compassion is a result of modern western life rather than something inherent to the human species.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.10. Pro: Empathise with animals - how would you feel if your children were taken from you, fattened and then slaughtered for the purposes of feeding another beast. Or if you were herded into an abattoir where the friends you graze with are stunned and killed before you as you wait your turn. Cattle and pigs are mammals like us and experience the world through emotions not dissimilar to our own.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.10.1. Con: One of the prerequisites for empathy to be substantiated is similar levels of sentience and cognitive capacity. It is not the case therefore there is no rational grounds for empathy
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.11. Pro: Abstaining from animal meat consumption allows one to reflect on more compassionate views of the world, and human involvement as caretakers of the ecology.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.12. Con: Morality is not absolute. While vegetarianism is a sign of moral virtue for [some Buddhists](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=RNBgCgAAQBAJ&pg=PA78&lpg=PA78&dq=buddhism+moral+vegetarianism&source=bl&ots=sdH97MDzta&sig=LZsKluIQOJ5QPhboqstbQTlePRA&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjp_7aBzoPNAhXmYaYKHQtDAQcQ6AEIMDAC#v=onepage&q=buddhism%20moral%20vegetarianism&f=false), eating meat has equally been interpreted as a [moral duty](http://animalethics.blogspot.kr/2011/06/roger-scruton-on-duty-to-eat-meat.html).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.2.1.12.1. Con: Roger Scruton, [on his duty to eat meat](http://animalethics.blogspot.co.nz/2011/06/roger-scruton-on-duty-to-eat-meat.html), exclusively refers to conscientious carnivores and their ability to promote compassionate farming. Thus, he also rejects the current state of meat production.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3. Con: Research has examined [animal cognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_cognition) in mammals \(e.g. primates, elephants, dogs, cats, horses, livestock etc.\), birds \(including parrots and pigeons\), reptiles \(lizards and snakes\), fish and even invertebrates \(including spiders and insects\). Thus humans are not unique in having a developed brain.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1. Pro: Some animals are capable of abstract reasoning.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1. Pro: Crows understand [analogies](http://www.scientificamerican.com/article/crows-understand-analogies/).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.2. Pro: Baboons exhibit [abstract reasoning](http://www.cnrs.fr/Cnrspresse/n398/html/en398a09.htm).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.3. Pro: African grey parrots have the [reasoning skills](http://www.smithsonianmag.com/science-nature/african-grey-parrots-have-the-reasoning-skills-of-3-year-olds-15955221/?no-ist) of 3-year-old humans.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.2. Con: The intelligence of other animals does not matter, since if humans are capable of hunting them, the human intellect is clearly greater. The human brain is clearly more developed than any of those listed in the pros section.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.2.1. Con: Some animals which are clearly not more intelligent than humans can successfully hunt humans. Even if the rest of the claim is true, claiming any animal which hunts any other animal is clearly more intelligent is fallacious - there are other advantages that come into play such as speed, strength, and stamina.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.3. Pro: Chimpanzees [solve problems](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=F-xFlKfmLGY) via cooperation.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.4. Pro: Pigeons are capable of making [logical decisions](http://www.natureworldnews.com/articles/2180/20130530/pigeons-capable-solving-complex-problems.htm) using problem-solving skills.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.5. Pro: Elephants can [use insight](http://www.sciencemag.org/news/2011/08/aha-elephants-can-use-insight-solve-problems) to solve problems.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.6. Pro: [IQ tests](http://news.discovery.com/animals/iq-tests-suggest-pigs-are-smart-as-dogs-chimps-150611.htm) suggest that pigs are as smart as chimps.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.6.1. Pro: Domestic pigs can quickly learn how mirrors work and will use their [understanding of reflected images](http://researchers present evidence that domestic pigs can quickly learn how mirrors work and will use their understanding of reflected images to scope out their surroundings and find their food.) to scope out their surroundings and find their food.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.7. Pro: Chickens are intelligent animals, outperforming dogs and cats on many tests of [advanced cognition](http://www.farmsanctuary.org/learn/the-someone-project/chickens/#).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.8. Pro: Cattle display [visual individual recognition](http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0004441) based on categorization capacities.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.9. Pro: Insects possess small brains, but they exhibit sophisticated behavioral performances. Various insects species have unexpected [cognitive capabilities](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/wcs.1348/epdf?r3_referer=wol&tracking_action=preview_click&show_checkout=1&purchase_site_license=LICENSE_DENIED_NO_CUSTOMER).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.10. Pro: Cephalopods are generally regarded as the most intelligent group among the invertebrates and have a variety of [cognitive abilities](http://www.cambridge.org/us/academic/subjects/life-sciences/animal-behaviour/cephalopod-cognition?format=HB).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.11. Pro: New Caledonian [crows](http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/8631486.stm) use sticks to reach their food in wild nature. So the use of tools can also be found in animality.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.2. Con: [Humans are not at the top of the food chain](http://www.pnas.org/content/110/51/20617). On a scale of 1 to 5 \(trophic level\), with 1 being the score of a primary producer \(a plant\) and 5 being a pure apex predator \(predators who don’t have any predators themselves\), ecologists found that, based on their diet, humans score a 2.21.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.1.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.4. Con: [Saying something is natural proves nothing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appeal_to_nature) unless it is elaborated on why continuing to follow the "natural order of things" is a good thing.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2. Pro: [98.8%](https://www.amnh.org/exhibitions/permanent-exhibitions/human-origins-and-cultural-halls/anne-and-bernard-spitzer-hall-of-human-origins/understanding-our-past/dna-comparing-humans-and-chimps/) of human and chimp DNA is the same, and they are so similar because they are closely related.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2.1. Con: Although humans and chimps have very similar DNA, they [often use their genes in different ways](https://www.amnh.org/exhibitions/permanent-exhibitions/human-origins-and-cultural-halls/anne-and-bernard-spitzer-hall-of-human-origins/understanding-our-past/dna-comparing-humans-and-chimps/), and therefore there are still big differences in the behaviour of chimps and humans.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2.2. Con: Our genes may be similar, but our [brain size](http://www.bbc.com/future/story/20150706-the-small-list-of-things-that-make-humans-unique) is not. That is what makes us different.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2.2.1. Con: Brain size doesn't necessarily mean more intelligence. The sperm whale for instance has a brain that weighs [17 lbs on average](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sperm_whale), where a normal humans is 3 lbs. That doesn't mean sperm whales are smarter than humans.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2.2.1.1. Con: Brain size on its own is meaningless, but brain size in proportion to body size is a consistent index of animal intellectual development
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2.2.1.1.1. Con: There is considerable ongoing debate on what markers of intelligence are important. The current strong candidate is brain wrinkling. There is behavioural evidence to suggest classes of more advanced species. For example, higher mammals such as dolphins and elephants display what appears to be funeral/burial behaviours. Other higher mammals such as other primates display adaptive problem solving. There is some evidence that elements of pain perception do relate to evolutionary advancements.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.2.3. Con: The basis of this argument is fundamentally wrong. Whenever something is placed on a scale of "closeness" to something else, based on what is used, there will always be something closer than other things. It doesn't definitively mean that one comes from, or is related to the other.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3. Pro: There is no inherent difference between animals and humans; to insist otherwise is [speciesism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speciesism), the act of discriminating against a being on the basis of their species.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.1. Pro: The line between animals and humans/nature and humans in general is a sign of humans' hubris and only exists in human minds.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.1.1. Con: Our hubris, ironically, is exactly that element which differentiates us from the rest of the animal kingdom and leads to our technological, ethical, and logical advancements beyond the rest of the animals.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.1.1.1. Con: Our reasoning capacity is more likely the driving factor.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.2. Pro: Humans and animals are indistinguishable, for they are part of the primate group \(family of the [great apes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominidae)\), thus humans are [animals](http://a-z-animals.com/animals/human/) as well.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.2.1. Con: This argument is just as flawed as saying every human on Earth is indistinguishable for we all belong to the same taxonomy.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.3. Con: It is not speciesist to point out the inherent differences in our thought processes, reasonings, technological leaps, and our huge impact on the Earth's environments, both positive and negative. We are animals, but there are no other animals like us.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.3.1. Con: While this proves we are different species it doesn't prove we are superior.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.4. Pro: Speciesism, like sexism and racism, is thinking that we as human are a superior species which leads us to slave, abuse and kill "inferior" beings. Nowadays we have advanced toward a more accepting and tolerant world and therefore we can assume that in the next 10-15 years there will be a prohibition to eat meat much like there is a prohibition to smoke in public places.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.5. Pro: Killing animals for food, clothing, experimentation or any other reason directly enforces the idea of violence perpetuated by the strong upon the weak. It is similar to how all marginalized sections of society were and still are treated. Racism, ableism, sexism, homophobia - they are all directly related to carnism.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.6. Pro: Rationally, there is no clear moral difference between a human's interests and a non-human animal's. If we are to try and justify human rights, we will see that we are unable to come up with a criterion which includes humans but excludes other animals. Sentience is the ultimate reason we think of it as wrong to harm humans; people feel pain. It is morally arbitrary to say other animals should not get the same consideration simply because they are not humans.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.4. Con: Humans are superior to all other animals, because they have the ability to make choices based on morality, and not instinct. It's what separates us from all other life known life forms.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.4.1. Con: "Instinct" is a gross oversimplification. Animals are demonstrated to perform learned behaviour on a wealth of occasions - this is not instinctual.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.4.2. Con: Many domestic animals will display guilt after behaviours or incidents they know to be transgressions.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.4.2.1. Con: While it is impossible for anyone to really know the thoughts of another being, human or otherwise, it is much more likely that in these instances we humans are projecting an emotional causation on to the learned behavior of animals. Behavior that is learned both through evolutionary symbiosis and a given animals' idiosyncratic experiences. Because we can empathize and have a tendency to anthropomorphize, we see the behavior as indicative of emotion.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.5. Con: Following that logic, animals are not superior to any other life form, they are simply a small part of a whole ecosystem. As such they have no legitimate right to kill other life forms as they please. This is inherently problematic.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.6. Con: The concept of "rights" is a creation of rational beings living in a society. The idea of "rights" seeks to transcend ecosystems and the "state of nature". If we are considering humans and other animals in their natural context of a state of nature in an ecosystem, then introducing rights is an inappropriate and anachronistic interjection.
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.7. Pro: When we look at it biologically, assigning less value to animals is a form of discrimination. It's just discrimination based on more features than within-species discrimination \(e.g. different anatomical structures or less intelligence instead of just the color of the skin\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.1.8. Pro: Human beings are not better than other animals.  An increasing amount of research is showing that they have feelings and they suffer just like humans. The literature comprises articles, books and academic papers: [www.amazon.com](https://www.amazon.com/Second-Nature-Inner-Animals-MacSci/dp/0230107818/?&tag=livescience-20); [inews.co.uk](https://inews.co.uk/news/science/animals-feelings-heres-science-prove/); [www.theguardian.com](https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2017/oct/11/elephants-animal-welfare-why-do-we-deny-ignore-feelings-other-species); etc.
1.1.4.8.1.1.2. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.3. Con: It is not the decision of one person what another puts into their bodies.
1.1.4.8.1.1.3.1. Con: The sourcing of said material can, however, be an ethical issue. For instance, all sources of human meat could be argued to be unethical.
1.1.4.8.1.1.4. Con: This argument is based off an internally judged moral system. None of the claims have hard fact behind them. Confidence brings verisimilitude but has no effect on actual truth. Proper justification is based on reality not personal preference.
1.1.4.8.1.1.5. Con: Such an act is justifiable from a hedonistic standpoint.
1.1.4.8.1.1.5.1. Con: Ethical hedonism takes into account the pleasures of all parties involved, including animals which are capable of sensation and/or emotion.
1.1.4.8.1.1.5.1.1. Pro: Ethical hedonists do not commit murder for pleasure, as this would not only end another's life \(and thus, potential for pleasure\) and cause pain, but would also cause fear in others of this being repeated. While killing an animal is not considered "murder", similar logic could be applied.
1.1.4.8.1.1.5.1.2. Pro: While eating meat may not itself be absolutely wrong from a hedonistic perspective, the structures around which eating meat in the present day is based \(i.e. factory farming\) - and which its continued consumption encourages the perpetuation thereof - are highly unethical, as they cause massive amounts of suffering to animals, as well as suffering to the humans who must work in the meat industry to sustain it. A reduction in meat consumption would reduce the prevalence of these institutions.
1.1.4.8.1.1.5.1.3. Con: Egoistic hedonism does not need to take into account the welfare of other parties.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6. Con: Plants are living as well and yet nobody seems to have a problem with harvesting them for consumption.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1. Con: Plants are not comparable to humans in the way that animals are.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.1.3.2.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.2. Pro: Plants are very different from humans and animals in that they are alive but they [are not sentient](http://www.abolitionistapproach.com/a-frequently-asked-question-what-about-plants/), which makes killing them less of a concern.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.3. Pro: Plants react merely to outside stimuli, such as sunlight or mineral composition, rather than having sentient preferences that can be described as interests.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.3.1. Con: The combination of two arguments from Singer–his 'equal consideration of interests,' and his take on 'minimal standard of decency–' allow for all organisms interests to be considered. Even inorganic matter may be considered equally as having 'interests' beyond their usefulness to me. 'Consideration' is requisite to evaluate my choices as an individual. Given that our understanding of sentience exists on a changing spectrum, what I choose to consume ideally reflects a minimal standard of decency.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.3.2. Con: "Sentient preferences", are also merely a reaction to outside stimuli, even if it is more complex.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.4. Pro: Animals and humans have individual interests and behaviours which vary from person to person and animal to animal. By contrast, plants all have the exact same, static interests. This is a morally relevant difference between the two groups.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.1.5. Con: All life forms are comparable. They all have various sets of reactions to various stimuli, which include emotions, that are also only a reaction to outside stimuli.
1.1.4.8.1.1.6.2. Pro: Research has suggested that [plants are very aware of the world around them](https://www.voanews.com/a/plants-humans-share-sensory-awareness/1637966.html) and therefore know when they are ripped  and know the difference between hot and cold touch.
1.1.4.8.1.1.7. Pro: This has less to do with right and wrong, and more to do with justice. Is it just for humans to consume the flesh of other species when it is on longer necessary? There have been times in our history when it was necessary, but this is no longer the case, so a more relevant question would be 'should it be considered torture and murder to kill sentient beings when it is not a necessity?' If not, why? Why is it ok to kill animals who think and feel, when it is not necessary?
1.1.4.8.1.1.8. Con: It is natural to eat whatever is convenient, even if it is not strictly necessary for survival. Bears, for example, are omnivores yet eat meat whenever [the opportunity arises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bear#Behaviour).
1.1.4.8.1.1.8.1. Con: Vegetarian food is equally convenient and accessible, meaning this is not a justification for a meat based diet.
1.1.4.8.1.1.8.2. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.1.1.4.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9. Pro: Killing animals to satisfy an unnecessary dietary preference creates disproportionate and unnecessary suffering.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.1. Con: If the issue is "unnecessary suffering" then the killing of the animal is not intrinsically wrong nor is eating meat. Causing "unnecessary suffering" is wrong.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2. Con: Killing can take place without suffering, for example [through gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inert_gas_asphyxiation) and in environments that do not induce stress.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1. Con: This does not change the fact that it is about satisfying an unnecessary dietary preference and not necessary for actual survival.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1. Con: Most of humans' behaviour is not necessary to survive, yet they do it if it enriches their daily lives.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.1. Pro: Many humans like to buy luxury products like fancy watches, clothes and cars.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Conspicuous consumption has been [explained](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=VCZZS6jWkRIC&pg=PA84&lpg=PA84&dq=conspicuous+consumption+evolutionary&source=bl&ots=YK_OZdJkWM&sig=wsLxBDG3twfTFwFDIeYHYi9Cifg&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjM_5KO1p7NAhVG4qYKHXOyBM84ChDoAQg9MAQ#v=onepage&q=conspicuous%20consumption%20evolutionary&f=false) in the context of humans' nature, and with an eye on sexual selection and signaling, similar to the evolutionary utility peacock's tails.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.2. Pro: Humans often enjoy partaking in alcohol, drugs, shopping and sexual intercourse for pleasure rather than out of necessity.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.3. Pro: Humans create wonderful and unique art.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.4. Pro: Humans do research and science.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.4.1. Con: Research and science does in fact assist our survival by enabling us to deal with threats that may not be apparent to a lay individual.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.5. Con: If much of humans' behaviour is not necessary for survival, it should be judged depending on the impact of that behaviour. While much of it, such as creating and and research, do not cause harm to others, eating meat is an example where extreme harm is caused, which means the behaviour is not justified.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.6. Con: Unlike consumption of meat, the vast majority of all science, art, culture and languages comes without the infliction of suffering and harm to other living beings.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7. Pro: Some of the oldest forms of human expression and art are [cave paintings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_painting) of wild game, prey of humans. The chase and consumption of meat have therefore constituted a central component of human culture since its beginning.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1. Con: Cultural components change over time: cultural transformation is a natural dynamic process.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1. Pro: Convictions surrounding different foodstuffs, and their corresponding cultural importance, change over time.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.1. Pro: In early 18th century Europe, vegetables were believed to have no health benefits and to be almost impossible to digest.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.1.1. Con: Vegetables may have had a bad reputation for some time, but this did not have a big effect on common peoples' actual eating habits.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.2. Pro: The potato can be viewed as the decisive innovation – even as a central [cultural norm](http://ieg-ego.eu/en/threads/backgrounds/food-and-drink#EarlyInternationalisationandInnovationsinthe17thand18thCenturiesPotatoesMaizeandHotDrinks) – during the emergence of the modern system of dishes and meals in the 18th century, but it only entered the dietary culture of the broad masses of central Europe during the 17th century.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.3. Pro: [Cannibalism](http://quod.lib.umich.edu/w/wsfh/0642292.0038.007/--art-of-the-table-in-eighteenth-century-france?rgn=main;view=fulltext) was, in certain times and places, preferable to vegetarianism.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.4. Con: That cultural convictions change does not imply they will change.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.4.1. Con: The rise of [vegetarianism](http://www.roymorgan.com/findings/vegetarianisms-slow-but-steady-rise-in-australia-201608151105) and [veganism](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/food-and-drink/news/number-of-vegans-in-britain-rises-by-360-in-10-years/) [around the world](https://www.riseofthevegan.com/blog/veganism-has-increased-500-since-2014-in-the-us) pretty clearly indicates that cultural values around food have the capacity to change.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.2. Pro: Humans' meat consumption patterns today are not the same as those of their stone-age ancestors. Naturally, the kind of hunting and consumption of meat practised by stone-age humanoids does not, therefore, hold the same importance in modern-day culture.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.2.1. Pro: Many of the animals hunted and consumed by our ancestors are now extinct, such as mammoths, mastodons, aurochs and cave bears.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.2.2. Con: It does not matter what kind of animal is consumed or how it has been obtained: humans' meat consumption can still constitute a significant aspect of their valued culture today.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.2.2.1. Pro: The consumption of the French-Canadian Tourtière - a meat pie - on Christmas Eve or New Year's Eve is still considered a [treasured cultural tradition](https://newengland.com/yankee-magazine/food/main-dishes/meat-pies/french-meat-pie/) by many.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.2.2.1.1. Con: There are vegetarian versions of a tourtière recipe. Here is one [example](http://allrecipes.com/recipe/97346/vegetarian-tourtiere/).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.3. Con: Cultural transformation should not be forced and attempts to do so rarely succeed, cultures only transform gradually as a result of natural processes.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.3.1. Con: If humans stopped eating meat, this would arguably be due to the natural process of meat production becoming gradually unsustainable.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.3.2. Con: In 675 AD, the use of livestock and the consumption of some wild animals \(horse, cattle, dogs, monkeys, birds\) was banned in [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_vegetarianism#Japan) by Emperor Temmu, due to the influence of Buddhism. During the twelve hundred years from the Nara period to the Meiji restoration in the latter half of the 19th century, Japanese people enjoyed vegetarian-style meals.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.3.2.1. Pro: Japan has a rich tradition of [cooking with vegetables](http://www.japan-talk.com/jt/new/vegetarian-japanese-food). As of today, [meatless dishes](http://en.rocketnews24.com/2015/09/28/10-vegetarian-foods-you-can-order-at-almost-any-japanese-restaurant/) still make up for a big part of Japanese cuisine.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.3.2.1.1. Con: Western assumptions about life as a vegetarian in Japan are being called out as [naive and unrealistic](https://thisjapaneselife.org/2011/09/07/japan-vegetarian-food/) by people struggling with it. As one writer [put it](https://kotaku.com/5484581/japan-its-not-funny-anymore): "Everything in Japan has meat in it."
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.4. Pro: The 21st century's marked by globalism and increasing interconnectivity of all cultures. In other words, a global culture is the new paradigm. The interconnectivity of our actions obligate us to behave in a way that is sustainable for all subsidiary cultures. Using one culture's norms as justification for a practice that harms the global society is not an adequate response. This debate, and Kialo in general, is the articulation of a global society working out its ethos in a dialectical process.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.5. Pro: Western \(European\) culture began to undergo rapid changes starting with the arrival of Columbus in the [New World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution), and continuing with the [Industrial Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6. Pro: Cultures around the world are undergoing [transformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformation_of_culture#Environmental_stresses_and_impacts_on_cultures) due to environmental stresses, such as [climate change](http://Cultures around the world are undergoing change due to environmental stresses, such as climate change.).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1. Pro: Eating and producing meat heavily contributes to climate change.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1. Pro: The [meat](http://shrinkthatfootprint.com/food-carbon-footprint-diet) lover's diet has the worst carbon footprint: about double the amount of a vegan diet.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.1. Con: Many vegan diet staples actually have a bigger impact on the environment and water resources than meat production, such [as almond milk](https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/shortcuts/2015/oct/21/almond-milk-quite-good-for-you-very-bad-for-the-planet).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.2. Pro: A report by Worldwatch Institute states that animal farming is responsible for [51%](http://www.worldwatch.org/node/6294) of global greenhouse gases.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.2.1. Con: And if it were replaced by vegetable farming, then vegetable farming would be the major contributor.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.3. Con: [Researchers](http://www.sciencealert.com/vegetarian-and-healthy-diets-may-actually-be-worse-for-the-environment-study-finds) at Carnegie Mellon University \(CMU\) say that a diet with more fruits, vegetables, dairy and seafood would actually be worse in terms of emissions than what Americans currently eat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.3.1. Con: The researchers did not find that producing vegetables is more harmful to the environment than producing meat. What they found, in light of the data they examined, is that producing some vegetables and other foods results in high use of natural resources – and that eating more of those foods \(as recommended for health by the USDA\) in two particular scenarios results in higher energy use, blue water footprint and greenhouse gas emissions.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.3.2. Con: "\[T\]he results showed that getting our weight under control and eating fewer calories, has a positive effect on the environment and reduces energy use, water use and GHG emissions from the food supply chain by approximately 9 percent." [cmu.edu](https://www.cmu.edu/news/stories/archives/2015/december/diet-and-environment.html)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.3.3. Pro: Shifting consumption to eating more sustainable meats like chicken and pork is a better solution than phasing out all of meats. As the source above says, chicken and pork do not consume nearly as many fossil fuels as some vegetarian alternatives. Maybe a shift away from red meat \(cow\) is what is necessary.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.4. Pro: Eating a plant-rich diet ranks as the [fourth-most effective way](http://www.drawdown.org/solutions-summary-by-rank) to combat climate change.

Universal vegetarianism would cause similar [effects](https://gnightearth.com/2014/06/26/is-your-diet-sustainable-vegetarian-trump-meat-eaters-in-terms-of-sustainability-and-greenhouse-gas-emissions/).

But in the big picture, someone who eats beef regularly will have a way bigger footprint because of its enormous chain of production required when compared with a typical vegetarian diet.

Another graphic from the same source \(reup here: [pbs.twimg.com](https://pbs.twimg.com/media/B4sAuHGCAAAe3JH.png)\) also showed that the carbon intensity of fruit is actually 20% higher than that of poultry, pork or fish

The difference is that the animal becomes inefficient. The animal have to use the energy to grow and to live, where there is a spillage of energy from what it ate. By not eating animals we exclude this factor, which is the whole reason that a vegan diet is more environmentally sustainable.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.2.4.5. Pro: Farm animals eat grass and animal feed, which took exactly as much CO2 out of the atmosphere during growing as the animals give back during digestion. Therefore animal farming does not contribute to climate change, it keeps it in balance.

1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.4.1.2. Con: We should do everything we can to reduce our damage, even if some is unpreventable - not all of it is.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.4.1.3. Con: This claim is an example of the [perfect solution fallacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nirvana_fallacy#Perfect_solution_fallacy) - it implies that just because a problem cannot be solved entirely with one solution, we should not attempt to minimize its effects until a solution can be found, or use a combination solution to ultimately solve it entirely by addressing various factors at once.

1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.8. Con: While meat production does entail production of [up to 9%](https://www.epa.gov/ghgemissions/sources-greenhouse-gas-emissions) of the world's greenhouse gases, the source of the carbon is less problematic than the other 91% of the carbon, mostly produced by fossil fuels. Cows belch methane, but this carbon originates from the atmosphere and goes back into the atmosphere in climate-boosted form. Fossil fuels take carbon formerly sequestered deep underground, and adds it to the atmosphere. So meat is problematic, but not in the same league as fossil fuel.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.8.1. Con: Plants used to feed those animals often come from intensive agriculture which needs fossil fuels directly or indirectly \(mechanization, fertilizers, pest control\). So there is a significant amount of indirect CO2 emission coming from fossil source.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.8.2. Con: That's just how you define 'league'. The source of the carbon in this case is hardly relevant, it's the transformation from carbon dioxide into methane that is. The carbon in the methane does not even out with the carbon in the carbon dioxide; [methane is a 25 times stronger greenhouse gas than carbon dioxide](https://climatechangeconnection.org/emissions/co2-equivalents/).

1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.10.2. Con: The facts aren't so simple, as shown in [this study](https://www.sciencealert.com/vegetarian-and-healthy-diets-may-actually-be-worse-for-the-environment-study-finds), switching to a less meat-heavy diet might actually cause emissions and energy consumption to increase rather than decrease. One has to keep in mind that not only the production affects the environment - to get the product from the farm to your nearest store one needs transportation. Vegetables are in general less \(calorie/nutrient\)-dense and therefore you need a bigger volume of them to feed people.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.10.2.1. Con: The [study](https://www.sciencealert.com/vegetarian-and-healthy-diets-may-actually-be-worse-for-the-environment-study-finds) is based on a "per-calorie" comparison, where broccoli \(34kcal/100g\) is compared to beef \(228kcal/100g\). While it is true that some vegetables are less calorie-dense, others are far more calorie-dense than meat, [beans](http://www7.slv.se/SokNaringsinnehall/Home/FoodDetails/874) for example. Beans are a more likely substitute for meat than broccoli, making vegetables less carbon-heavy.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.10.2.2. Con: This study did not address the fact that feeding the animals also requires massive amounts of plants and water.

1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.12. Con: Producing meat only has a substantial impact on Carbon Dioxide and methane emissions. Other greenhouse gases should be our priority as carbon emissions are reversible if re-forestation and re-greening efforts are made. [ghginstitute.org](http://ghginstitute.org/2010/06/28/what-is-a-global-warming-potential/)
