1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.2. Pro: Producing meat with traditional agriculture contributes to climate change; But producing with [sustainable methods](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rjYG4vm7MZ4) actually increases land fertility all around, to the benefit of man, plant, and animal.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.3. Pro: Reducing the amount of meat consumed by humans would have a positive impact on climate change without requiring people to stop eating meat entirely. If we all reduced our meat intake by even 50%, we would make huge strides in decreasing climate change.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.4. Con: The mere reduction, rather than elimination, of meat's carbon impact may not be enough to combat climate change.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.1.5.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6. Pro: A diet including meat can be sustainable and without negative consequences to the environment. It is not about what you eat, but about the right way of farming and keeping animals.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.1. Con: That organic production is sustainable is a [myth](http://www.nytimes.com/2012/04/13/opinion/the-myth-of-sustainable-meat.html?_r=0) because it produces relatively more CO2 emissions and requires more space.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.2. Con: All farm animals require [more water](http://news.cornell.edu/stories/1997/08/us-could-feed-800-million-people-grain-livestock-eat) per kg of food output than plants do. Therefore, it is always more sustainable to eat plant foods.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.2.1. Con: If meat production is less efficient, it only argues for moderated meat consumption, not a total prohibition on meat consumption.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.2.1.1. Con: In today's society and the current state of the world, inefficiency has a negative effect on sustainability, which may have severe impacts on the future of human existence, and even other animals and life as a whole.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.2.2. Con: A more relevant metric than food weight is food energy. Therefore, a better metric than liter/kg would be liter/kilocalorie or even breaking it down to "liter per gram" of macronutrients \(fat, protein, carbohydrates, and alcohol\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.2.2.1. Pro: Using this metric, animal sources of protein are not less sustainable than vegetarian ones. Cattle are still least efficient. However, industrially farmed broiler chickens have less of an impact than farming nuts \([Page 29, Table 6](http://waterfootprint.org/media/downloads/Report-48-WaterFootprint-AnimalProducts-Vol1_1.pdf)\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.3. Pro: Raising livestock in a responsible way is a crucial part of the nutrient cycle that supports organic farming.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.4. Pro: Meat should be eaten sparingly, and its externalities and environmental costs should be taken into account in its price. This will directly contribute to a higher price, and less meat consumption.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.5. Pro: Industrial, monoculture based, factory farmed meat is indeed bad in many ways. However, it represents only one failed model of agriculture. [Permaculture based farming](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s13412-015-0254-8) with strategic rotational grazing programs, have been shown to create many positive and vital ecological outcomes as well as improved ethics. Meat production, done in this manner, provides a very real and powerful tool in battling climate change, erosion, pollination and habitat loss, loss of bio diversity, and lack of soil health.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.5.1. Pro: Animals are present in any ecological system. [Farming systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permaculture) that emulate natural systems by integrating animals are often more holistic and resilient.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.5.2. Con: In modern western society, the majority of people eat bad, industrially-farmed meat. So, while in a vacuum eating meat might be a boon to the environment, in practice today it is not.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.5.2.1. Con: That is not a statement about eating animals as much as it is the system of agriculture that has become normalized. If we push to shift that model of farming, towards a more permaculture based agriculture system, then we also change the nature of this debate.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.5.3. Con: The farming techniques of permaculture haven't been shown to be effective for meat production on the large scale required to fulfill global need.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.5.3.1. Pro: The cost of permaculture and sustainable meat farming would make meat a luxury product and move the industry to a completely different economy.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.6. Pro: Unnatural methods of farming could be easily curbed if industrial nations consumed less meat. Everyone being on a meatless diet is not necessary.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.6.1. Con: This still suggests a need for a massive reduction in the amount of meat consumed to stop particularly unnatural methods of meat production. Even then, animals would be being slaughtered for food, such that the best ethical outcome is for everyone to stop eating meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.6.2. Pro: Industrial livestock farming results from peoples' hunger for tons of cheap meat. If people would consume meat only once a week we would not need these unethical structures.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.6.3. Con: Eating meat encourages increased meat production; not eating meat discourages it. Therefore, humans who are aware of the issues should stop eating meat, to reduce the demand for it and hence, the prevalence of unnatural and immoral farming methods.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7. Pro: We can consume meat from organic livestock farming. Organic farmers do not use antibiotics/drugs, raise more traditional breeds and aim to keep animals in conditions that are closer to their natural environment/behavior patterns, thus animals have more natural lives.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7.1. Con: Currently [organic farming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_farming_by_country) accounts for only a [small percentage](http://orgprints.org/29790/13/willer-lernoud-2016-global-data-biofach.pdf) of livestock farming and it is unrealistic to think we can provide for current levels of meat consumption via fair organic livestock farming. Thus, a massive reduction of meat consumption would be required nonetheless.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7.2. Con: Unnecessary killing of animals is cruel and thus has negative consequences even if they are not drugged and kept in reasonable conditions.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.8. Pro: According to an [Austrian study](http://www.nature.com/ncomms/2016/160419/ncomms11382/full/ncomms11382.html), it is actually possible to provide a diet similar to that of rich countries to all of the world's population without further deforestation.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.7. Pro: Not all meat consumption is equally bad for the environment: eating a cow that grazed on unfarmable grassland, is slaughtered at the farm, and is then consumed there does not contribute particularly much to climate change.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.3. Pro: An ethical diet is not one which eliminates greenhouse gas emissions or other forms of harm; if it were, the best diet would be starvation. Instead, an ethical diet strives to balance a variety of goals; health, taste, environmental impact, cultural legacy etc. In that case, a diet which includes some meat \(but perhaps less than a typical diet in a developed country\) would be morally permissible.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.3.1. Con: This is a logical fallacy of relative privation. Proposing that the better solution is to not eat at all doesn't relate to the original argument, it instead insists that not eating meat isn't a valid position, because starvation is the only absolute. A solution is an improvement, and you neglect to comment on its efficacy as an improvement, and instead try to invalidate the argument by taking the point to an extreme to misrepresent.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.4. Con: The amount of land required to produce the same amount of calories is nearly 5 times greater than is required for crops. With a growing population the consumption of meat could come at a detrimental cost. [Yields and Land Use In Agriculture, Our World In Data](https://ourworldindata.org/yields-and-land-use-in-agriculture)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.5. Pro: Through the consumption of meat that is raised by respecting the nature of ruminant animals we can regenerate land into highly productive prairie and farmland. It has been scientifically proven by the Rodale Institute and other regenerative farmers that ruminant animals and multi-specieated farms can and will regenerate land and help sequester carbon in our soil where it belongs. By mimicking nature we right the wrongs of factory farming and KAFO's.  [rodaleinstitute.org](https://rodaleinstitute.org/our-work/livestock/) [www.resilience.org](http://www.resilience.org/stories/2016-03-15/joel-salatin-the-promise-of-regenerative-farming/)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.14. Con: The net effects of climate change are not obviously bad. There's no reason to believe the climate is perfectly optimized the way it is.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.15. Con: 1 kg of chicken produces 6,9 kg CO2 eq; 1 kg of vegetables about 1.5-2 kg CO2 eq \([www.greeneatz.com](http://www.greeneatz.com/foods-carbon-footprint.html)\). However, chicken has about 3-5 times more calories and up to 10 times as much protein as many vegetables, meaning you need to consume less of it on a kg to kg basis. A single mile in an airplane produces about 24 kg CO2 eq \([blueskymodel.org](http://blueskymodel.org/air-mile)\), about the same as 2 pounds of beef - so one single domestic flight will usually offset a person's meat-related carbon emissions for a whole year.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7. Pro: Eating habits change, and meat has not always been an integral part of most cultures. Only [relatively recently](http://www.colostate.edu/Dept/GDPE/Distinguished_Ecologists/2006/Smil/Eating%20Meat.pdf) has the consumption of meat become wide-spread, for example during the mid-19th century in Europe and not until the mid-20th century in large parts of China.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1. Con: Meat was nevertheless an important cultural component before its consumption in large doses became widespread. People highly valued it, but they simply could not afford it.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.1. Pro: Henry IV, was called "le bon roi", because he advocated a ["chicken in every pot on sundays."](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France) This shows, that even though people did not eat a lot of meat, they still valued it highliy.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.1.1. Con: Meat was valued in the past because it was rare, and thus a sign of wealth, luxury and opulence. This no longer holds relevance to today.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.2. Pro: In traditional agricultural European societies many animals were [more valuable](http://www.colostate.edu/Dept/GDPE/Distinguished_Ecologists/2006/Smil/Eating%20Meat.pdf) as tools for plowing or producing fertiliser, or as a renewable resource for producing milk or eggs, rather than being killed for a one-off supply of meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.3. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.4. Pro: During the [times](http://quod.lib.umich.edu/w/wsfh/0642292.0038.007/--art-of-the-table-in-eighteenth-century-france?rgn=main;view=fulltext) of Louis XIV the rich mainly ate spicy cooked meat dishes. This shows that meat was a cultural asset, at least if one could afford it.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.4.1. Con: The king himself [loved](http://quod.lib.umich.edu/w/wsfh/0642292.0038.007/--art-of-the-table-in-eighteenth-century-france?rgn=main;view=fulltext) fruits and vegetables.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5. Con: Meat has been a rare and expensive good for most of human history, so it could not have been a strong cultural component.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5.1. Con: The availability of meat and the quantity of its consumption do not tell us much about the cultural role it played. Some goods play a role regardless of or even through their scarcity.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5.1.1. Pro: [Gold](http://www.skwirk.com/p-c_s-1_u-103_t-264_c-873/importance-of-gold-to-different-cultures-over-time/nsw/importance-of-gold-to-different-cultures-over-time/gold-/what-is-gold-), as a scarce good, has been of tremendous significance, viewed by most cultures as a symbol of wealth and prosperity.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5.2. Pro: The diet of a [farm worker](https://meatonomics.com/) in 18th century England would consist mostly of root vegetables, bread, cheese, butter, sugar, tea, and a little milk.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5.3. Pro: Up until the beginning of the 20th century, Bavarian farmers ate meat only for special occasions, about 4 - 5 times a year.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5.4. Pro: In most traditional European agricultural societies the annual meat consumption rarely went [beyond 5-10kg](http://www.colostate.edu/Dept/GDPE/Distinguished_Ecologists/2006/Smil/Eating%20Meat.pdf), which is [less than 10%](http://www.who.int/nutrition/topics/3_foodconsumption/en/index4.html) of today's per-capita consumption.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.6. Pro: Consumption of different type of meat serves to separate social classes by the price of certain pieces of meat, such as the [Tri-tip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tri-tip) \(or 'Bürgermeisterstück' in German which means 'major's piece'\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.7. Pro: Because meat was expensive it was saved for special occasions and holidays like Christmas, Easter and Thanksgiving.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.1.5.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.3. Con: The argument equivocates cultures of years past with current day cultures.  Modern cultures do, as you point out, consume meat as a central and normal role in diet.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.4. Pro: Eating meat is culturally based. There is no biological or cultural evidence that sustains an obligatory diet based on animal flesh.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.5. Pro: Cultures are changing quickly and so meat eating can be phased out without causing harm.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.5.1. Pro: Many cuisines, such as in [Persian](http://www.cultureofiran.com/persian_cuisine.html) or [Hindu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etiquette_of_Indian_dining#Beef), do have restrictions on which meat to eat and still enjoy a rich culture. Phasing out meat would work similarly.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.5.1.1. Con: Geographical differences in cuisine developed in part because of the availability of particular [game and types of grasses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guns,_Germs,_and_Steel). Thus, cultural patterns describing the phasing out of meat are not reproducible in other societies.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.2. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.2.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.3. Con: Humans in industrial nations have overcome the "hunting" part of stone-age culture; there is no reason why they should not outgrow the "consumption of meat" part as well.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.3.1. Con: Hunting in industrialised nations is no longer necessary for the acquisition of food.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.4. Con: The [species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_painting#Subjects.2C_themes_and_patterns) found most often in cave paintings were suitable for hunting by humans, but were not necessarily the actual typical prey found in associated deposits of bones. The most common animal hunting and meat consumption practices in the stone-age have not, therefore, necessarily made significant contribution to this part of human cultural history.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.4.1. Pro: It makes logical sense that cavemen would depict the animals and hunts that were most glorious, exciting, spectacular, or otherwise worthy of commemoration, rather than hunts and gatherings which would be seen as mundane and routine to them.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5. Con: In our earliest origins as a species, humans needed the high amounts of energy and protein animal meat provided to power our oversized \(compared to animals\) brains. Today, in a world where food is comparatively plentiful, there is no need to turn to meat for this intake.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1. Pro: Humans have not evolved to hunt, eat or digest meat very successfully.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.1. Con: Humans, just like [carnivores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnivore#Characteristics_of_carnivores), have comparatively short digestive systems.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.1.1. Con: Meat-eating animals have an [intestinal tract](http://www.celestialhealing.net/physicalveg3.htm) that is only 3 times their body length, so that rapidly decaying meat can pass through quickly, whereas herbivores have an intestinal tract 10-12 times their body length. Humans have an intestinal tract 10-12 times their body length, to allow [slower digestion](http://www.adaptt.org/Mills%20The%20Comparative%20Anatomy%20of%20Eating1.pdf) of plants.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.1.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.3. Con: That humans' anatomy enables them to stand upright allows for other hunting methods that do not require typical predator anatomy.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.3.1. Pro: Humans are superb [endurance](https://www.sciencedaily.com/releases/2004/11/041123163757.htm) runners - an important skill for chasing prey.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.3.1.1. Pro: Humans can even outrun [horses](http://www.slate.com/articles/sports/sports_nut/2012/06/long_distance_running_and_evolution_why_humans_can_outrun_horses_but_can_t_jump_higher_than_cats_.html).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.3.1.2. Con: This is also an important skill to run away from carnivores.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.3.1.2.1. Con: Humans' [final velocity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Footspeed) is simply not high enough to run away from most of the carnivores.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.4. Pro: The liver of a carnivore can [detoxify](http://www.adaptt.org/Mills%20The%20Comparative%20Anatomy%20of%20Eating1.pdf) the excess vitamin A absorbed from a meat-based diet. The human liver cannot detoxify excess vitamin A.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.5. Con: Humans developed anatomical features that enable them to build and utilize tools.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.5.1. Pro: The comparatively large size of the human brain [has been linked](http://press.princeton.edu/titles/6549.html) to the necessities of hunting, for example in terms of social organization.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.5.2. Pro: The evolutionary physiology of human hands [has been linked](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1571064/) to the use of tools with the specific use of hunting.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6. Con: Human evolution, physiology and behavior are adapted to hunting and the consumption of meat. Humans have thus [been called](https://www.amazon.com/Hunting-Hypothesis-Conclusion-Concerning-Evolutionary/dp/0988604388?ie=UTF8&*Version*=1&*entries*=0) a "fully evolved hunting animal".
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.5.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.5.2.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.3. Pro: Humans have unparalleled ability to mitigate heat.[ncbi.nlm.nih.gov](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nlmcatalog/101587029)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.4. Con: Compared to animals of similar size humans are among the slowest runners, thus rendering them unable to catch prey.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.4.1. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.3.1.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.5. Con: Humans lack natural weapons \(such as claws\) to kill a prey animal once caught.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.5.1. Con: Humans are endurance hunters - weapons are less necessary to kill an already exhausted prey animal.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.5.2. Con: Against smaller \(and exhausted\) prey animals, barehanded attacks \(deliberate neck-breaking, etc.\) are a perfectly viable way to kill.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.6.5.3. Con: The human weapon is his use of tools. 
Intellect derived from an enlarged brain, which itself evolved from a protein rich diet, is what allowed us to figure out how to use them.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.7. Pro: What is natural can be derived. Organisms' anatomy and physiology are good indicators for the kind of lifestyle they have adapted to - even though this does not preclude the possibility that an "un-natural" lifestyle is established.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.7.1. Pro: Anatomy and physiology are the outcomes of evolutionary processes. These are determined by the environment in which certain traits flourish while others perish. The anatomy and physiology of humans is thus an indicator for the natural environment in which they developed.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.8. Pro: Of all the anthropoid apes, man's teeth and digestive system most closely resembles the chimpanzees, gibbons, gorillas and orangutans. In captivity some of these animals will eat meat if starved, but in the wild all eat a vegetarian diet.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.8.1. Pro: Humans actually have the jaw structure of frugivores, not carnivores, and our digestive system is not built to digest meat as easy as other animals
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.8.2. Con: Since we require B12 and that cannot be found outside of animal products, i.e. meat and cheese, although we may have similarities to frugivores and other animals, ultimately humans' nutrition requirements are a better guide to what we're designed to eat, versus which animals we happen to be similar to in different ways.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.8.2.1. Con: B12 cannot be produced by either animal, not only humans. Different bacteria produce it, bacteria that are almost everywhere. In nature, we would've had enough without eating meat. Also, eating meat has many downsides to human health, but the argument seems to deliberately specify only one fact in its favour. The best choice for humans is a vegan diet supplemented with B12 \(and other missing nutrients\), which conforms to the argument's criterion of a better guide to what we're designed to eat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.8.2.1.1. Con: The necessary inclusion of the words "supplemented with B12 and other missing nutrients" to the claim that "the best diet is vegan supplemented..." directly addresses the failure of the claim. If a given diet is proscribed as best, so long as you add to it everything that is lacking and necessary for human health, then it is by definition not an effective diet.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.8.3. Con: [Meat eating and hunting among chimpanzees is normal.](http://www-bcf.usc.edu/~stanford/chimphunt.html) Meat is also used in gaining political ground in the troop and as presents when attempting to mate.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.9. Pro: Studying evolution, science and data gives a different perspective. We don't have the sharp teeth, claws or short intestinal track of carnivores. Also, our closest animal relatives are chimpanzees and bonobos which have an almost exclusively plant based diet \(less than 2% insects and animals\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.9.1. Con: When available \(but usually at least 3% of total consumption\) chimps prefer to eat meat due to the nutritional advantages. This quantity is significant when comparing the encephalization of humans, species ancestral to humans, and modern apes to their amount of consumption of proteins. For instance, humans require only as little as 15-20% of their total consumption to be protein to maintain muscle mass and brain function.[completehumanperformance.com](https://completehumanperformance.com/2015/09/11/dieting-protein-needs/) [www-bcf.usc.edu](http://www-bcf.usc.edu/~stanford/chimphunt.html)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.9.2. Con: The evolutionary growth of the human brain could only have been supported by meat consumption.[Waterlogged by Dr. Tim Noakes](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nlmcatalog/101587029)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.9.3. Con: Evolved with primates then took a sharp turn towards meat consumption with the shortening of our gut and efficient fat digestion, the loss of our ability to easily produce retinol from carotenoids, B12 from plants.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10. Pro: Humans' canines are not specially meant for processing meat. All carnivores in comparison - dogs, cats, lions etc. - have [carnassial teeth](http://www.npr.org/sections/13.7/2016/05/19/478645426/humans-are-meathooked-but-not-designed-for-meat-eating) at the back of their mouths, "blade-like and sharp and perfect for slicing meat".
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.1. Pro: Humans do not have the large mouth or long, pointed teeth of carnivores. Human [teeth](http://www.adaptt.org/Mills%20The%20Comparative%20Anatomy%20of%20Eating1.pdf) are short and flat for chewing fibrous food.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.2. Con: The presence of certain teeth does not necessarily correlate with natural dietary preferences. [Hippos](http://science.jrank.org/pages/3340/Hippopotamus-hippo-s-teeth-its-diet.html), [gorillas](http://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2015/02/150207-animals-gorillas-elephants-teeth-science-dentistry/) and [camels](http://www.fao.org/docrep/t0690e/t0690e09.htm) have canine teeth, yet are herbivores.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.2.1. Con: [Gorillas](http://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2015/02/150207-animals-gorillas-elephants-teeth-science-dentistry/) have those large canines mainly for self defense and deterrence reasons. Furthermore they chew a lot of heavy twigs and bark, which requires strong teeth.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.2.1.1. Con: This only supports the argument that there is no reliable connection between the presence of canines and eating meat. There are plenty of other reasons for their presence.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.3. Con: Humans' natural physiology [made them](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=7bdqAAAAQBAJ&pg=PT93&lpg=PT93&dq=%22Humans+can+grip+this+way+because+we+have+relatively+long+thumbs%22&source=bl&ots=dXitibmPmL&sig=iWCVFMrC88fDW6vD6OmztyuaVDY&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwim1eCGx_nMAhWHFJQKHSxiAfgQ6AEIGzAA#v=onepage&q=%22Humans%20can%20grip%20this%20way%20because%20we%20have%20relatively%20long%20thumbs%22&f=false) a tool-using species. We do not need canine teeth/claws to slice meat because we have tools for doing so.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.4. Con: We evolved with primates, then switched to eating meat later in the evolutionary path. We dont kill or hunt with our teeth. We can easily eat and digest meat and many of us do.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.11. Pro: Meat-eating animals have no skin pores and [perspire](http://www.celestialhealing.net/physicalveg3.htm) through the tongue, whereas herbivores perspire through skin pores. Humans perspire through their skin pores.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.11.1. Con: The mode of perspiration might correlate with the diet of many animals - but this does not imply a causal determination. Bears, for example, do not have skin pores, yet they can live on a plant-based diet, as pandas do.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.11.2. Con: Great white sharks, an apex predator, do not perspire through the tongue. The above claim is unfounded.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.12. Pro: Meat-eating animals, including humans, have [more acidic stomachs](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4519257/) to digest meat than herbivores.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.13. Pro: Whereas carnivores have acid saliva with no enzyme [ptyalin](http://www.celestialhealing.net/physicalveg3.htm) \(needed to pre-digest grains\), herbivores have alkaline saliva with ptyalin. Humans have alkaline saliva with ptyalin to pre-digest grains.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.13.1. Con: This merely proves that humans may be [omnivores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omnivore), able to digest grains and fruits as well.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.13.1.1. Pro: Hominidae, including [humans](http://www.vrg.org/nutshell/omni.htm), are [omnivores](https://books.google.de/books?id=CXwylbbRXvAC&pg=PA37&redir_esc=y&hl=de#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.13.1.2. Pro: Omnivores are defined as [generalized feeders](http://www.vrg.org/nutshell/omni.htm), with neither carnivore nor herbivore specializations for acquiring / processing food, and who are capable of consuming and do consume both animal protein and vegetation.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.13.1.2.1. Pro: They basically have more generalized anatomical and physiological traits. So do humans.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14. Pro: Humans, like herbivores, lack the sharp [claws](http://www.celestialhealing.net/physicalveg3.htm) of a carnivorous predator, used to hunt down and kill prey.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1. Con: Claws are not essential for eating meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.1. Pro: Claws are mostly required to catch a running animal and kill it for food. This is not a process humans have to go through to eat meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.2. Con: Carnivores use their claws not only for capturing but also for [disarticulating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnivore#Characteristics_of_carnivores) their prey.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.3. Pro: Crocodiles do not make use of their claws for eating their prey.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.3.1. Con: Corcodiles are [reptiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodile) and not [mammals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal). It is not valid to compare humans, being part of the mammal group, to non-mammal predators.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.3.1.1. Pro: There are too many features that [distinguish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal) mammals form reptiles such as the possession of a neocortex, hair, three middle ear bones and mammary glands.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.4. Pro: Pigs are omnivores and eat meat without claws.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.1.5. Pro: Meat can be prepared for humans to eat, such that it can be eaten without claws.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.2. Con: Human hands are better able to hold meat than claws. So human anatomy is superior for eating meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.2.1. Con: This only proves that human anatomy might be superior for holding meat. It does however not pove that humans are meant to eat/digest it.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.3. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.5.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.14.4. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.10.3.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15. Con: While correct, this observation does not imply a prescription. Humans do not restrict themselves to activities that their bodies are optimized to do, but rather perform a whole range of activities, that the human body is not naturally meant for.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.1. Con: Many activities that go against what our body is made for are however seen as problematic and unhealthy, for example extended sitting and diving without caution.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.2. Pro: Sitting for hours - as many office workers do - is [unnatural for the human body](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=wDB-BAAAQBAJ&pg=PA14&dq=human+body+sitting+hours+unnatural&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q=human%20body%20sitting%20hours%20unnatural&f=false) and has negative effects on overall health as well as a direct link to mortality.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.2.1. Con: This just proves that we should not be sitting for hours.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.3. Pro: Human biology points towards the benefits of polygamy - yet we are commonly expected to behave monogamously, which is [not necessarily natural](https://books.google.co.kr/books/about/The_Myth_of_Monogamy.html?id=Jl19414uE1gC&redir_esc=y) for us.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.3.1. Pro: Concerning to the Ethnographic Atlas Codebook, only 15% of its 1231 [listed cultures](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/darwin-eternity/201108/are-people-naturally-polygamous-0) live monogamously, therefore monogamy is a rather Western \(Christian\) form of relationship and the majority of cultures lived polygamously.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.3.2. Con: While polygamy as a legal form of marriage may not be permitted in many countries, it is however unproblematic to live polygamous.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.3.3. Con: Polygamy is widely [accepted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygamy) among different societies worldwide.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.3.4. Pro: Polygamy is commonly [seen as](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=-arJDCunTwEC&pg=PA182&dq=polygamy+sanctioned&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwi37srN4o_NAhUm26YKHR5tAR4Q6AEIKTAC#v=onepage&q=polygamy%20sanctioned&f=false) harmful to the Western ideal of marriage and has historically been "treated in the West as an offensive against society itself", including stigmatization.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.4. Pro: It is unnatural for human bodies to vastly go beyond the spaces and speeds they can naturally reach, for example with the help of [airplanes and spacecrafts](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=udIpBAAAQBAJ&pg=PA155&lpg=PA155&dq=%22space+exploration%22+%22unnatural%22&source=bl&ots=C-DDdRDBk1&sig=fdWW_EHDq2cQo08Cp3aw89Nvv10&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwis6IqLyfnMAhWCk5QKHezYB2QQ6AEIJTAC#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.4.1. Con: In the given examples, human bodies are largely shielded from the spaces and speeds in question. Passengers of airplanes, for example, feel neither the speed, difference in air pressure nor the cold temperatures that come with this mode of transportation.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.4.2. Con: There are limits to airplanes and spacecrafts as to how much the body can naturally endure. Thus there are restrictions set by humans' naturalness.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.4.2.1. Con: These limits can be exceeded by improving airplanes and spacecraft to travel faster while placing less strain on the body.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.4.3. Pro: Lacking wings, humans are not meant to be flying.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5. Pro: Humans are not supposed to exist under water, yet diving is a popular and widespread hobby and sport.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5.1. Con: The [mammalian diving reflex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammalian_diving_reflex) is a reflex in mammals which optimizes respiration to allow staying underwater for extended periods of time. It exists - in weaker versions - in humans, in particular babies up to 6 months old \([Infant swimming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_swimming)\).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5.2. Pro: Deep diving is only possible with special equipment such as [breathing gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas) and [swimfins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swimfin).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5.2.1. Pro: The human lung is [not able](http://scienceline.ucsb.edu/getkey.php?key=2087) to extract oxygen from water.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5.3. Pro: In contrast to animals with bodies made for diving, humans have no skin between their fingers and toes \(and thus rely on fins\) and easily suffer from [decompression sickness](http://emedicine.medscape.com/article/769717-overview).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5.4. Pro: Human skin is not made for long term stays under water. It deforms and wrinkles [dramatically](http://www.odditycentral.com/videos/what-10-days-underwater-can-do-to-your-hands.html) and finally breaks down.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.15.5.5. Pro: Divers need to wear [diving suits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_suit) for protection from the cold as well as high water pressure.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.16. Con: Humans aren't very successful at eating vegetables either \(as compare to, say, a cow\). These are the pains of being omnivores, and mean that humans cannot concentrate on only one kind of food. Thus, meat is an essential part of our diet. See [www.livescience.com](https://www.livescience.com/32435-why-cant-humans-eat-grass.html).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.17. Con: Human's digestive system is designed to eat meat therefore eating meat is fundamental to good health. [For more information here is a detailed study by Dr Weston A Price on nutrition](https://healthwyze.org/archive/nutrition_and_physical_degeneration_doctor_weston_a_price.pdf)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18. Con: The [consumption](http://www.livescience.com/24875-meat-human-brain.html) of \(cooked\) meat was crucial for the development of the human brain. Therefore you can state that eating meat is what made humans what they are today.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.1. Pro: According to [authoritynutrition.com](https://authoritynutrition.com/7-evidence-based-health-reasons-to-eat-meat/), "Humans also have canines, with big brains, opposing thumbs and the ability to make tools to hunt. Meat was one of the reasons humans were able to evolve such large, elaborate brains." It is in our nature to eat meat, seeing as we were created with the necessary attributes to efficiently hunt and eat meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.1.1. Con: Canines have nothing to do with us being carnivorous. Almost all mammals have them, herbivourous or not.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.1.1.1. Pro: Although humans have canines, the animal with the largest canines is a herbivore \(ie. hippo\)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.1.2. Con: We have the ability to make tools to hunt. The same thing that makes someone capable of making tools - a greater capacity for abstract and logical thinking - can also make them capable of getting enough sustenance without consuming meat.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.2. Pro: Consuming meat enabled the brains of our ancestors to evolve and [grow](https://www.livescience.com/24875-meat-human-brain.html) dramatically over a period of a few million years.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.3. Pro: A diet with meat helped humans develop into humans [Sorry Vegans: Here's How Meat-Eating Made Us Human](http://time.com/4252373/meat-eating-veganism-evolution/).
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.3.1. Con: As the end of the article admits, the past has no bearing on how our future development should continue.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.3.2. Pro: The brain requires 20 percent of a human’s energy when resting; by comparison, an ape’s brain requires only 8 percent. This means that from the time of H. erectus, the human body has depended on a diet of energy-dense food—especially meat. 

[www.nationalgeographic.com](https://www.nationalgeographic.com/foodfeatures/evolution-of-diet/)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.4. Con: Just because something was necessary or relevant in the past [doesn't make it necessary or relevant in the current context](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_fallacy). While eating meat did provide the caloric intake necessary for the development and evolution of the human brain, this fact holds no bearing in the modern age, where meat consumption is not tied to survival in many instances.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.4.1. Con: There are [very serious concerns about the mental](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/animals-and-us/201512/how-scary-are-the-mental-health-risks-vegetarianism) as well as the[physical risks of vegetarianism.](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/science/vegetarians-are-less-healthy-and-have-a-lower-quality-of-life-than-meat-eaters-scientists-say-9236340.html) 

[Fish are particularly important for our health](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1753-4887.2010.00287.x/full). That is true not only for the body, but [even more so for brain health.](https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jama/fullarticle/2484683)
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.5. Con: By the same logic we have not reached some kind of endpoint to this evolution, and in keeping with that one might consider that with those brains comes a self awareness, and with that self awareness comes the higher-order human traits such as compassion and empathy, and with these higher order traits come new aspirations and new appetites for self-actualisation. 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.18.6. Pro: The adoption of eating meat caused the human brain to grow and increase in power, leading to the modern human as we know it. [Eating Meat Made Us Smarter- NPR](https://www.npr.org/2010/08/02/128849908/food-for-thought-meat-based-diet-made-us-smarter)

1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.19. Con: Humans are physically created to build and use advanced tools - and [they need them](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=7bdqAAAAQBAJ&pg=PT93&lpg=PT93&dq=%22Humans+can+grip+this+way+because+we+have+relatively+long+thumbs%22&source=bl&ots=dXitibmPmL&sig=iWCVFMrC88fDW6vD6OmztyuaVDY&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwim1eCGx_nMAhWHFJQKHSxiAfgQ6AEIGzAA#v=onepage&q=%22Humans%20can%20grip%20this%20way%20because%20we%20have%20relatively%20long%20thumbs%22&f=false). 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.20. Con: Adaptation to new circumstances and opportunities is a hallmark of evolution, and thus nature in action. A changing diet that overcomes the physical adaptation to a previous diet is thus natural.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.20.1. Pro: As the environment of humans has changed over time, they have [adapted their diets](http://www.beyondveg.com/nicholson-w/hb/hb-interview1c.shtml) to fit with their surroundings and depending on what was available.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.20.2. Pro: Up until several thousand years ago, nearly all adult humans were [lactose-intolerant](http://www.npr.org/sections/thesalt/2012/12/27/168144785/an-evolutionary-whodunit-how-did-humans-develop-lactose-tolerance); however, when European farmers began to discover the nutritional benefits of dairy products from animal milk, increasing numbers of mutations in the gene that produces the lactase enzyme occurred, enabling many humans to adapt to a diet that included dairy.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.1.20.3. Pro: When Italian wall lizards were introduced to a new environment in the 1970s, they [changed their diet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_wall_lizard#Rapid_adaptation) from one heavy in plants to one heavy in insects, and accordingly adapted their morphology over generations.
1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.5.2. Pro: The strength of the human brain is that it allowed us to develop forms of social organisation and technology that have elevated the species above the whims of nature. As the dominant species on the planet, we no longer need to follow the practices of our distant evolutionary ancestors.

1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.2. 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.2.1. Con: Those activities are generally not harmful to other living things. Bestiality, for instance, is illegal and morally frowned upon.

1.1.4.8.1.3. Con: There is no data to suggest that the thought of animal suffering accompanies the taste of meat.

1.1.4.8.1.4. Pro: The term "delicious" is subjective – what is tasty to one person may be disgusting to the next.
1.1.4.8.1.4.1. Pro: A part of what we find enjoyable in food is what we are used to. If we change to vegetarian food we will become accustomed to those flavours and meat would seem less appealing.
1.1.4.8.1.4.1.1. Pro: It would be easier to grow up on a vegetarian or vegan diet than to have to learn later to like substitutes, once acquired tastes have been acquired.
1.1.4.8.1.4.2. Pro: Eventhough taste is individual and everyone experiences the pleasure of eating food, which he or she never tasted before, the sense that meat is 'good' and 'tasty' is a social phenomena. An example of the opposite direction but same phenomena could be algae, which are disliked by many people, without being tasted in the first place.
1.1.4.8.1.5. Con: People who are incapable of deriving pleasure from meat consumption can voluntarily stop eating meat. But there are many people who enjoy meat consumption despite this fact.
1.1.4.8.2. Pro: Pleasure is not a good enough reason to keep doing something if it is immoral.
1.1.4.8.2.1. Pro: Human trafficking also brings many people pleasure; however, it is morally reprehensible because the pleasure comes at a horrific cost. Eating meat merely because it is pleasurable is not a strong pro meat consumption argument.
1.1.4.8.2.1.1. Con: The value of human life comes from a mutual agreeement to not kill each other, despite the uncomfortable ways that some humans may get pleasure from this practice. However, animals cannot make such agreements since to them, we can always be reduced to being either threats or just plain food. Therefore, there is no harm in getting pleasure from the meat acquired through the killing of an animal since it's the closest we can get to a mutual agreement.
1.1.4.8.2.1.1.1. Con: Human life does not obtain its value from some form of mutual agreement. Beyond that, ethics does not consist in merely hypothesised mutual agreements. If a life is valuable, it is so as a function of some feature their life exhibits: happiness, potential for happiness, rationality, etc. And that feature needs to be applied consistently across the board when determining which lives have value and which do not.
1.1.4.8.2.1.1.1.1. Con: [Social contract](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_contract) has been one of the leading theories on ethics for quite some time.
1.1.4.8.2.1.2. Con: Eating meat is not analogous to human trafficking, except on that one minor point.
1.1.4.8.2.1.2.1. Con: Both cause undue suffering to living beings \(and animals with a nervous system and confirmed capacity for pain\).
1.1.4.8.2.1.3. Con: According to utilitarianism the cost of human trafficking outweighs the good it creates which makes it morally reprehensible. The pleasure of eating meat does not come at the same horrific cost of human trafficking and therefore the overall utility to society is increased which makes eating meat a moral act.
1.1.4.8.2.1.3.1. Con: Eating meat does in fact often cause horrific suffering to animals raised and grown in terrible circumstances.
1.1.4.8.2.1.3.2. Con: The claim that eating meat does not come at the same horrific cost of human trafficking is only true if your values are biased towards humans. Animals feel pain and emotion as humans do, and deserve to be free from suffering just as humans do.
1.1.4.8.2.1.4. Con: Human trafficking brings no pleasure to anyone other than those with psychological damage who enjoy human suffering or those who deliberately ignore the cost of the trade to reap the dubious benefits. Neither of these groups are a majority and are certainly nowhere near the same size as those who enjoy meat.
1.1.4.8.2.1.5. Con: Animals have no conscious awareness of their own death and are thus unaffected by the same human fear and dread experienced by slaves or others being trafficked for other reasons. Animals have little concept of freedom and it's opposite: oppression. Horror is a conscious, thinking reaction of humans and one not shared by any but the most intelligent animals which, as a result, we do not farm.
1.1.4.8.2.2. Pro: The pleasure gained from eating meat still does not compare to the suffering caused to animals and the environment.
1.1.4.8.2.2.1. Con: Neither does the radical switch to a no-meat diet. Both diets are riddled with inefficiencies that impact animals and the environment. Method of harvest is the issue, not the constitution of the diet itself.
1.1.4.8.2.2.2. Con: Since humans have a higher level of consciousness and experience than animals, it is possible that the pleasure of eating meat is greater than the suffering animals experience from a quick, painless death \(depending on the farm, treatment, etc.\). If we accept that humans are capable of greater emotions, then it isn't far-fetched to think that humans gain more from eating meat than animals lose from dying.
1.1.4.8.2.2.2.1. Con: Most humans aren't even focussed on the meat while they're eating, rather their social company and/or own thoughts/newspaper. Their pleasure is not only fleeting and ephemeral, it's very secondary to them. Meanwhile, an animal's death robs it of the rest of its \(potential\) lifetime of experiences entirely.
1.1.4.8.2.2.3. Con: Suffering is not a necessity in the process by any means.
1.1.4.8.2.3. Pro: If pleasure is something that makes an action right, then something which causes the opposite - a lack of pleasure, or worse, a large amount of pain - such as torturing and slaughtering animals, is wrong.
1.1.4.8.2.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.2.
1.1.4.9. Con: "no relevance" is too strong. Taking away a preference for no good reason is wrong. "little relevance" would be more precise, as other common ethical concerned associated with eating meat trump personal pleasures.
1.1.5. Con: Even if meat tastes good the experience overall is less desirable. First, the color scheme is not as colorful and pretty as plants. Additionally the processing needed to eat meat \(like cooking and deboning\) is more annoying than eating plants raw.
1.1.6. Con: The delicious taste of meat won't last forever due to [seafood](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/uknews/1533125/All-seafood-will-run-out-in-2050-say-scientists.html) and [meat](http://www.quantumrun.com/prediction/vegetarians-will-reign-supreme-after-meat-shock-2035-future-food-p2) running out in the future. It's better to get used to the taste of plants than be forced to later on.
1.1.7. Con: It is not clear that the additional pleasure \(if any\) of eating a meal containing meat compared to eating a meal without outweighs the suffering of the animal bred, raised and killed for their meat.
1.1.7.1. Pro: As humans live in more advanced societies, it becomes less moral for those humans to eat meat.  If it's "eat meat or starve," there's no moral issue there at all.  On the other hand, if eating meat is simply one more lifestyle choice, it is significantly less moral, because if you ascribe animals any moral value at all \(ask, "Do I think torturing animals for fun is okay?"\), then at some point their moral value outweighs the fleeting human desire for "tasty".
1.1.7.2. Pro: The claim seems to be that pleasure is good and therefore the act of eating meat for some people is pleasurable and therefore good. However, in the quantity of suffering vs pleasure, eating meat comes at a staggering cost of suffering at a level that far exceeds the pleasure experienced by people. If all 7 billion people were eating meat and enjoying it, that is far fewer than the 56 billion animals slaughtered every year and the billions more suffering on factory farms. [www.animalequality.net](https://www.animalequality.net/food)
1.1.7.3. Pro: There is no moral justification for eating meat that is more convincing than a justification for not eating meat while having the alternatives that there are today. The "superior taste of meat products" can not be part of a moral justification when it comes to killing living beings.
1.1.8. Pro: Pleasure is important to human quality of life, so if meat consumption is more pleasurable than anticipated, abstinence could have a meaningful negative impact on quality of life. The overwhelming popularity of meat throughout almost all cultures could be an indication that eating meat is enormously pleasurable.
1.1.9. Con: What people commonly refer to the "taste of meat" is directly linked to one of the five basic tastes: [umami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umami). This taste can also be found in vegetable foods such as miso, seaweeds, tomatoes, mushrooms and many others, thus providing an equally satisfying meal deprived of animal protein.
1.1.10. Con: That the taste of meat is "pleasurable" is very subjective, and it could be argued that taste preferences can be taught and/or untaught \(trained\).
1.1.11. Con: Many of man's endeavors are in pursuit of pleasure. However, some of these pleasures we derive have negative externalities, i.e. they negatively impact other people/the surrounding environment/the planet as a whole. It is in our collective interest to minimize and gradually eliminate the pursuit of such pleasures. Eating meat, though pleasurable has high impact negative externalities and should therefore be gradually eliminated. Unrestrained hedonism can be catastrophic to the commons.
1.1.12. Con: Eating other animals \(human beings are animals\) is not necessary for our survival, it's for our pleasure, and this pleasure has to be balanced with the cost of the victims, which is too high \(suffering and death\).
1.1.13. Pro: In the most world-renowned cuisines, meat plays a central part and is often the highlight dish.
1.1.13.1. Pro: If eating meat is too far abandoned before artificial replacements can suitably be found, culinary arts developed over centuries may be lost.
1.1.13.2. Con: Something being tasty does not justify torturing animals or destroying the environment. Jeffrey Dahmer used humans as the central piece of his meals. Protecting that culinary option for him was not more important than protecting the lives of those he would destroy.
1.1.13.3. Con: Culinary styles and traditions change and evolve over time. If the world stops eating meat, international cuisines will adapt to that fact.
1.1.13.4. Con: Most world-renowned cuisines developed seasoning and preparations to make up for the lack of meat or mask the deficiencies of poor quality scraps. What makes them world renowned is not the meat ingredients, it's everything else around it.
1.1.13.5. Pro: Bacon. Whenever there is a debate about not eating meat, bacon is quite a strong argument for the case that eating meat brings more taste and pleasure than most plant based foods.
1.1.13.5.1. Con: Bacon has become memetic in some circles. Memes do not necessarily correspond to reality, as exaggeration is socially encouraged for entertainment.
1.1.13.5.2. Con: Speaking from personal experience, when I ate meat I did not like bacon. Others, both meat-eaters and vegetarians, have said the same. It may a pleasurable taste to you but that experience is not universal.
1.1.13.6. Con: When meat is the main focus of a meal, it is often marinated, covered in sauces, seasonings, cheese, and vegetables to enhance its taste. It is those things that are delicious, not the meat itself.
1.1.13.6.1. Con: People who order their steak rare enjoy the flavor of the actual meat.
1.1.13.6.2. Pro: Meat has become [much less flavourful](http://nypost.com/2015/04/26/why-nothing-especially-chicken-tastes-like-it-used-to/) since the introduction - and subsequent rise - of factory-farming.
1.1.13.6.2.1. Pro: The flavour of meat is heavily influenced by what the animal primarily [ate](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/the-conversation-africa/its-true-what-a-sheep-eat_b_8920194.html) during its lifetime; studies show that meat of which the corresponding animal fed on natural pastures and not on man-made grain mixes is more flavourful, thus the rise of factory-farming has meant that meat is, on the whole, blander.
1.1.13.6.3. Con: The texture of meat more then the flavor is what most people value, and it's hard to replicate.
1.1.13.6.4. Con: Meat is usually not seasoned apart from salt. It is only processed meat that needs seasoning.
1.1.13.6.5. Con: Bacon tastes amazing and is very rarely seasoned.
1.1.13.6.5.1. Con: Bacon is cured. In the curing process significant amounts of salt are used negating the need to season later.
1.1.13.6.6. Con: This argument is based off an assumption. Flavour and texture of meat is something that only a meat-eater can attest to. It is opinion based and thus can't be refuted logically, merely subjectively, which can't be a basis for rational argument.
1.1.13.6.6.1. Con: This implies that claims relating to the flavour or texture of meat should become an unassailable argument in favour of eating meat. This is not good debating form.
1.1.13.7. Con: An increase in vegetarianism would generate newer and better vegetarian foods, recipes and cooking techniques, which could rival the pleasure generated from meat-based meals.
1.1.13.8. Con: Maybe it is not because it's the tastiest food, it could also be that it is the most exclusive, expensive and a symbol of power and wealth.
1.1.13.9. Con: There is no necessary correlation between a particular cuisine, restaurant or dish's level of prestige and whether it includes meat or not.
1.1.13.9.1. Con: Regardless of whether the correlation between prestigious cuisine and meat inclusion is necessary, it exists in the minds of many: chef and owner of Brighton's reputable Silo restaurant, Douglas McMaster, still cooks meat at his restaurant despite being vegetarian as meat usage is [“deeply engrained into fine dining cooking”](http://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/food-and-drink/vegetarian-chefs-who-have-to-eat-meat-silo-flat-three-a7715651.html).
1.1.13.9.2. Pro: A [study](https://arxiv.org/ftp/arxiv/papers/1502/1502.03815.pdf) suggests that it is not specific ingredients that weigh most heavily on a cuisine's reputation at all, but its combinations of different flavours at a molecular level: the study indicates that the universal popularity of cuisines such as Indian comes not from its usage \(or non-usage\) of certain ingredients like meat, but from its combining of certain ingredients whose flavour compounds do not significantly overlap.
1.1.13.9.3. Pro: The signature dish of one of the most famous chefs of all time, [Paul Bocuse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Bocuse), is a vegetarian truffle soup.
1.1.13.9.4. Pro: Maghreb cuisine is reportedly highly reputable among the upper-class of Paris, featured on culinary [blogs](http://www.saveur.com/article/Travels/Maghreb-Cooking-in-Paris) particularly for its exquisite \(and, by chance, vegetarian\) cous cous dishes.
1.1.13.9.5. Con: In a high cuisine [full course dinner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_course_dinner) fish and meat are the central courses.
1.1.13.9.6. Con: In the 2015 iteration of the "[World’s 50 Best Restaurants](http://www.theworlds50best.com/)" ranking by the British magazine Restaurant, only a single entry makes any reference to vegetarian cuisine [\(#50](http://www.theworlds50best.com/list/1-50-winners/The-French-Laundry)\).
1.1.13.9.7. Pro: The Michelin guide [recommends](http://www.therichest.com/expensive-lifestyle/food/10-michelin-recommended-vegetarian-restaurants/?view=all) plenty of vegetarian restaurants; there are more meat-serving restaurants listed simply because they appeal to a larger pool of potential guests.
1.1.14. Pro: It is because the taste of meat is so good and popular that scientists try to imitate it and create vegetarian "meat" products.
1.1.14.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.3.1.
1.1.14.2. Pro: Scientists have developed a so-called "[facon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetarian_bacon)", which is a vegetarian bacon.
1.1.14.3. Con: They do not imitate meat because of the taste, but because consumers do not want to miss out on certain dishes that usually contain meat, for example burgers.
1.1.14.4. Pro: Until you provide artificial meat at a competitive price, people will eat animals because meat is a simple and nourishing food.
1.1.14.4.1. Con: This addresses the economic question of eating meat, but not the question of whether eating meat is moral or not.
1.1.14.5. Con: Meat "imitations" are helpful in terms of transition to vegetarianism. Experienced vegetarians do not need such products, therefore meat "imitations" are not an attempt to fill in some void in vegetarian diet.
1.1.14.6. Con: If the taste is imitable there is no need to actually eat meat, as one can consume other vegetarian products with the same "fantastic" taste.
1.1.14.6.1. Pro: It is not difficult to replace meat with non-meat products that taste similar.
1.1.14.6.1.1. Pro: Tofu can be used instead of meat for example in stir fry dishes.
1.1.14.6.1.2. Pro: When making burgers, the meat patty can either be replaced with a vegetarian patty \(pre-made or homemade\) or with an equal portion \(size-wise\) of vegetables that have meatlike consistency \(e.g. mushrooms, fried zucchini, kohlrabi\).
1.1.14.6.1.3. Con: Raw or aged tenderloin beef, which is required for grilling a proper steak, can be replaced by nothing.
1.1.14.6.1.4. Con: All kinds of roasts are pretty difficult to replicate without meat, e.g. a classic "Krustenbraten" seems almost impossible without meat.
1.1.14.6.1.4.1. Con: [Seitan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wheat_gluten_\(food\)) and [tempeh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tempeh) are commonly used for vegetarian roast dishes.
1.1.14.6.1.4.1.1. Con: Neither Seitan or tempeh are able to replicate an essential part of roasts: crackling.
1.1.14.6.1.5. Con: A 'similar' taste or texture or aroma or nutrient profile would not satisfy those who desire or require real meat.
1.1.14.6.1.5.1. Con: "Real" meat is an arbitrary distinction. What we know as "meat" is the combination of a broad variety of qualities and traits, some of which are desired, others of which are neutral or even undesirable. In theory, any desirable trait can be replicated, while undesirable traits can be eliminated.
1.2. Con: Ceasing to eat meat would harm the economy.
1.2.1. Pro: Breeding livestock is necessary for many people \(particularly farmers\) to survive. Stopping this will eliminate their foundation of life.
1.2.1.1. Con: Stopping meat production would come along with an increasing production of substitutes, such as vegetables, crops and fruits. This creates new livelihoods for farmers.
1.2.1.1.1. Con: Experts in animal farming may have no relevant knowledge to put toward agricultural farming. Rather than creating new livelihood for these farmers, it would force them to rapidly become experts in an entirely new field with no time for transition.
1.2.1.1.1.1. Con: This would not be the first time an industry has been made redundant and workers in that industry have had to retrain.
1.2.1.1.2. Con: The animals currently used to farm meat will not disappear overnight. In order to immediately transition to agricultural farming, all of those animals would need to be slaughtered to make room for the vegetation. Not only would this be cruel to the animals, but it would also destroy the farmers' finances.
1.2.1.2. Con: Meat production is economically irrelevant in most national economies. Thus, impacts on farmers are easy to mitigate.
1.2.1.2.1. Pro: In advanced economies [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-sector_theory) in general is not very important. Meat production is therefore even more unimportant.
1.2.1.2.2. Pro: In underdeveloped countries meat production is marginal as illustrated by the low rates of meat consumption.
1.2.1.2.2.1. Con: [More than half](http://www.fao.org/docrep/015/i2490e/i2490e01b.pdf) of all employment in sub-Saharan Africa and South Asia is in the agricultural sector; in many of them, this produces more than a third of the national GDP.  [About one third](http://www.fao.org/docrep/016/ap106e/ap106e.pdf) of the production in this sector is livestock.
1.2.1.2.2.2. Con: Meat production in Uganda plays a significant role for the national  and rural economy. Beef production alone stands at [145000 Mt](http://www.fao.org/3/a-at589e.pdf).
1.2.1.2.3. Con: For countries like Argentina and Uruguay, [around three quarters](http://www.ers.usda.gov/media/187485/ldpm15901_1_.pdf) of their exports consist of frozen meat.
1.2.1.2.3.1. Con: In Argentina, animal agriculture is leading to deforestation and huge losses of natural capital which has a negative impact on citizens in the long term: [www.argentinaindependent.com](http://www.argentinaindependent.com/socialissues/environment/beyond-the-amazon-deforestation-in-argentina/)
1.2.1.3. Pro: Of the 880 million rural poor people living on less than $1 per day, 70% are partially or completely [dependent](http://www.worldwatch.org/global-meat-production-and-consumption-continue-rise-1) on livestock for their livelihoods.
1.2.1.3.1. Con: If rural poor people took up higher-paying jobs, they could have a higher quality-of-life and not dependent on livestock for subsistence.
1.2.1.3.2. Con: Demands for meat consumption force us into meeting that demand. If there was a big enough shift away from that need, farmers could pivot and still maintain a livelihood. Example: [Swedish drinks company helps farmer shift away from livestock farming and cut climate impact with his own oat milk brand](https://www.theguardian.com/sustainable-business/2017/aug/26/wow-no-cow-swedish-farmer-oats-milk-oatly).
1.2.1.4. Pro: Not eating meat means not farming animals, not farming animals means no money to feed them, no money to feed them means no more cattle, chicken, pigs, etc. as long as we live in a capitalist system/economy.
1.2.1.4.1. Con: This may be a benefit, as human-raised livestock is often kept in atrocious conditions, and also has negative environmental impacts. Farming also has negative impacts on humans.
1.2.1.4.1.1. Pro: Farming animals has severe impacts on the local environment due to its heavy resource use and impact upon the landscape.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1. Con: Many of the animals that we kill for meat, such as kangaroos or deer, are pests that are bad for natural ecosystems or for agriculture. Demand for their meat actually creates net benefits for the environment.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.1. Con: The above claim seems dependent on specific ecosystems.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.2. Con: The definition of 'pest' is itself a normative description that privileges human activities; e.g. kangaroos are pests because they eat crops. To hunt and kill them thus serves our own purposes, not any 'natural order.'
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.3. Con: If it is beneficial to kill pests, then we can do that without needing to eat their meat.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.3.1. Con: At the point pests are being killed, consuming their meat at least helps offset the need for other non-pest species to be raised and killed.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.3.2. Con: This literally works out to "At least we're still allowed to waste meat we kill".  Refusing to eat or otherwise consume and use this harvested meat is literally the most wasteful thing that could be suggested- even if it is not suitable for human consumption, it can still be made into pet or animal feed, or into fertilizer, etc.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.4. Pro: Humans, as apex predators who have usurped the predatory apexes of the other predators in the ecosystems we have come to also inhabit, have an ethical responsibility to keep those ecosystems in check so that, eg, rampant deer populations do not cause deforestation and subsequent ecosystem collapse.  Even where there are populations of healthy apex predators, these populations should also be checked so they do not cause problems and kill people- and it would be unethical to waste that meat.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.4.1. Con: We have already warped the ecosystem through domestication and selective breeding. We can put effort into reinstating these animals' natural habits, as animal experts sometimes do with orphaned or injured animals, and have had success with.

We also have notable success of restoring ecosystems by reinstating the natural predators that once lived there:[How reintroducing wolves saved a famous park](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NI5l8aumEWE).
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.4.2. Con: There's no reason to believe ecosystems are good the way they are. Old ecosystems are replaced by new ones. The balance of nature is a [long debunked](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/0963662505063022) ecological myth.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.5. Con: The majority of meat consumption is from cows, pigs, chickens, lamb, turkeys, not deer or kangaroo.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.6. Pro: Insects are numerous and contribute to vegetable crop destruction. Humans could have a large impact on the adverse effects of insects by eating them.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.7. Con: The morality of hunting is irrelevant to whether farming is bad for the environment.
1.2.1.4.1.1.1.8. Con: The context of this argument \(this specific sub-point\) is directly related to farming, not hunting animals. Proposing an argument of benefits of hunting overpopulated animals is a misrepresentation of the argument.
1.2.1.4.1.1.2. Pro: A 2012 study, examining the impact of a typical week’s eating, showed that plant-based diets are [better for the environment](https://www.vegsoc.org/eatingsustainably) than those based on meat.
1.2.1.4.1.1.2.1. Pro: According to a 2006 [report](http://www.europarl.europa.eu/climatechange/doc/FAO%20report%20executive%20summary.pdf) by LEAD Livestock's Long Shadow, "the livestock sector emerges as one of the top two or three most significant contributors to the most serious environmental problems, at every scale from local to global."
1.2.1.4.1.1.2.2. Pro: A 2007 study concluded that "within the same method of production, a greater consumption of animal products translates to [a greater impact on the environment](https://www.nature.com/articles/1602522#ref33)."
1.2.1.4.1.1.3. Pro: Livestock have severe effects on their immediate environment, causing issues such as  [overgrazing, compaction, and erosion](http://www.fao.org/newsroom/en/news/2006/1000448/index.html).
1.2.1.4.1.1.3.1. Con: Overgrazing and compaction are not inevitable effects of livestock, but of improper management of livestock. compaction is more dependent on the type of soil and climate in which the livestock reside, than it is upon the presence of livestock. Erosion is always happening regardless of the presence of livestock.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4. Pro: The production of meat consumes disproportionately more resources than the production of crops.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.1. Con: While the practices of meat production in high-income industrialised countries tend to be resource inefficient, meat production in other countries is [a lot more efficient](https://www.forbes.com/sites/timworstall/2012/09/03/it-does-not-take-7-kg-of-grain-to-make-1-kg-of-beef-be-very-careful-with-your-statistics/#1fc7709d5f0d). Rather than ceasing production altogether, we should ban inefficient methods of production.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2. Pro: A lot of the world's crops are currently used for animal feed, rather than human consumption.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.1. Pro: Growing food exclusively for direct human consumption, rather than using some of it for animal feed, could increase available food calories by [as much as 70%](http://iopscience.iop.org/article/10.1088/1748-9326/8/3/034015/meta;jsessionid=BE048803E5C08313A3954052670EAB15.ip-10-40-1-105), which could feed an additional 4 billion people.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.2. Pro: 36% of the calories produced by the world's crops are being used for animal feed, of which [only 12%](http://iopscience.iop.org/article/10.1088/1748-9326/8/3/034015/meta;jsessionid=BE048803E5C08313A3954052670EAB15.ip-10-40-1-105) then turn into animal products that can be eaten by the human population. That is a waste of 24% of the world's crops.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.2.1. Pro: It is more efficient to grow plants for food for people than it is to grow plants for food for animals that will be slaughtered for food for people.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.3. Pro: Corn is commonly used as a feed grain in [beef cattle](https://www.ag.ndsu.edu/publications/livestock/feeding-corn-to-beef-cattle) diets. Only [11%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corn_production_in_the_United_States#Production) of the total US corn production for 2013-14 was directly made into food for the US market, compared with 33% for livestock feed.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.4. Pro: Soybeans, predominantly in the form of soybean meal, are a major ingredient in global livestock [feed](http://wwf.panda.org/what_we_do/footprint/agriculture/soy/facts/), especially for chickens, pigs and cattle.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.5. Con: The solution isn't to stop eating meat, but rather to eat meat that has not been grain-fed \(or fed on other potential human food-sources\).
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.5.1. Pro: A benefit of this is that it lets farmers convert inedible organic matter \(grass, weeds, plant waste\) into edible organic matter \(meat, offal, gelatin, milk\).
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.6. Con: Inedible byproducts of existing plant-based food production \(e.g. soybean pods\) can be used to feed livestock.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.7. Pro: The livestock industry relies heavily on grains and oilseeds. The growing world population can not be fed if we keep using land for the production of feed for animals. [tandfonline.com](http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/03066150.2012.752357)
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.2.7.1. Pro: 40% of global grain production is fed to livestock. 
To put this in perspective, the US alone could feed 
[800 million people](http://news.cornell.edu/stories/1997/08/us-could-feed-800-million-people-grain-livestock-eat) with the grain that is fed to livestock.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.3. Pro: Irrigation systems channel a catchment's water to agricultural uses rather than lead it follow it's natural path over a landscape. This deprives natural water ways and landscapes of their water supply and degrades local ecosystems.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.3.1. Con: Provided the water use itself does not disrupt the water cycle of flowing from mountains to seas or lakes, such use would be reasonably acceptable. In addition, there must be a lot more benefits from that endeavor than just letting the water just flow right away.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.4. Pro: Agricultural use of water disrupts the water table equilibrium and leads to [desertification](https://www.greenfacts.org/en/desertification/l-2/4-causes-desertification.htm) and [salinification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salinity_in_Australia).
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.5. Pro: It takes [100,000](http://news.cornell.edu/stories/1997/08/us-could-feed-800-million-people-grain-livestock-eat) liters of water to produce one kilogram of grain-fed beef.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.6. Pro: [It takes](https://www.economist.com/blogs/feastandfamine/2013/12/livestock) two kg of grain to produce one kg of chicken, and between five and twenty kg of grain to produce one pound of beef.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.7. Con: There are countries where 99.9% of farming is grass fed. Industrial farming need not rely on grain - the nutrients are better, and the animals happier if you don't. Free range. Ethical farming practices would have one trying to replicate natural conditions. IMO, the same applies to agriculture, and recreating ecoystems/permaculture. We shouldn't I think, aim for the cheapest system - we should aim for the best system, to live on the earth, like we intend to stay here.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.7.1. Con: There is not enough land available for grazing to support our current demands for meat. Switching Western/modernized countries back to "free range" practices would require a dramatic reduction in meat consumption.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.8. Pro: Trophic levels are important to consider here. As plants are consumed to feed an animal only ~10% of the energy is available for the animal. In other words, a strictly meat only diet would require 10 times the plant matter; 100 times if eating a predator.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.9. Pro: Meat is inefficient. In growing animals for meat consumption the animal will always consume a significantly larger energy content in plant matter than can be obtained from the meat of that animal \(less than 5%\). This is due to the animal wasting massive quantities of energy in heating, digestion and movement.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.9.1. Pro: If all the grains used to feed farm animals were instead used for human consumption many people who are' starving' around the world could have a better diet.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.10. Pro: The demand for, and pollution of, water resources from farming animals is immense.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.10.1. Pro: Raising livestock accounts for roughly 23% of all [global water use](http://www.worldwatch.org/global-meat-production-and-consumption-continue-rise-1) in agriculture, equivalent to 1.15 liters of water per person per day.
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.10.1.1. Pro: It takes about 2,500 gallons of water to produce one pound of beef, and about 660 gallons to make a pound of chicken. It only takes about 220 gallons to make a pound of tofu and 180 to make a pound of wheat flour. So a vegetarian diet [conserves water](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/water_inputs_in_ca_food_production.pdf).
1.2.1.4.1.1.4.10.1.1.1. Con: These calculations are based on the most extreme situations. On average it takes about [441 gallons](http://www.wsj.com/articles/actually-raising-beef-is-good-for-the-planet-1419030738) of water per pound for US beef.

Pro: According to the Worldwatch Institute, "As populations grow, lowering meat consumption worldwide will allow more efficient use of declining per capita land and water resources, while at the same time making grain [more affordable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetarianism#Economics_and_diet) to the world's chronically hungry."
