1.2.5.4.2.5.5.1. Con: We are all humans, and individuals should not be unfairly privileged or disadvantaged due to the circumstances of their birth. Solutions should be implemented for the greatest good of the most humans and other living beings.
1.2.5.4.2.5.5.1.1. Con: The solution that represents the greatest good for most human beings and other living beings would involve control and restriction of the population in unsustainable communities and regions.
1.2.5.4.2.5.5.1.1.1. Con: Countries that implement restrictions on populations are either communist regimes or will go through a war/civil rights period in order to make it illegal. Human beings won't allow their right to reproduction to be taken away simply because someone deems their community "unsustainable".
1.2.5.4.2.5.5.2. Con: It can be debated if the first world has "earned" its luxuries, as it is built on a history of exploitation and bloodshed, and has directly or indirectly caused \(and continues to contribute to\) many "third world" problems.
1.2.5.4.2.5.5.2.1. Pro: Such 'first world countries' have only gained most of their highly developed statuses through war and dirty politics.
1.2.5.4.2.5.6. Pro: Switching to a more efficient form of food production is unlikely to prevent us from reaching a carrying capacity in the long run. Changing farming to feed a growing world population is a never-ending treadmill. Instead, we should probably focus more on the ecological stability of a system we are creating.[See Jevons Paradox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jevons_paradox)
1.2.5.4.2.5.6.1. Con: It will be beneficial and minimize damage in the short term, buying more time for and reducing the damage of finding long-term solutions.
1.2.5.4.2.5.6.2. Con: Increasing efficiency of food production may reduce the amount of labour necessary for it, allowing for that labour to be potentially allocated to more progressive jobs.
1.2.5.4.2.5.6.3. Con: Changing farming to feed a growing world population is only a never-ending treadmill if the population continues to grow. The vast majority of the world's population growth takes place in industrializing nations. Population growth tends to level off in post-industrial nations and although these richer nations often import large amounts of luxury food, most of them are capable of producing all the food they need. As economic development becomes more uniform worldwide, population growth will slow.
1.2.5.4.2.5.7. Con: We manage to produce food for far more people than that. The problem is to transport it to them as it requires expenses and the investment does not come back --- poor countries are not able to pay for it. Through correct legislation, countries could ban supermarkets from wasting food and they would have to transport it to those in need of food, manage their supplies better, and stop trashing imperfectly shaped foods and veggies.
1.2.5.4.2.5.8. Con: It is morally reprehensible to suggest the population should be reduced if you don't lead by example. Otherwise you are calling for the killing or restricted ability to procreate of others.
1.2.5.4.2.5.9. Con: We absolutely have the ability to feed all of them, which can obviously be seen by the fact that we are feeding almost all of them right now, given that very few people in the world starve to death.
1.2.5.4.2.5.9.1. Con: The statement that there are very few people in the world that starve to death is a gross understatement and incredibly false. Over 9 million people die from starvation per year as calculated in March of 2017. World Hunger is an epidemic.[borgenproject.org](https://borgenproject.org/15-world-hunger-statistics/)
1.2.5.4.2.6. Con: Moderation rather than prohibition should suffice; for any population level there is, mathematically speaking, an amount of meat that can be sustainably consumed \(e.g., each person eating meat twice per week might be sustainable for 7 billion people\).
1.2.5.4.2.6.1. Pro: From an efficacy standpoint, it might make sense to promote reduced meat consumption as a bridge instead of a cudgel toward vegetarianism. Meatless Mondays got a ton of pushback at my University - for a few weeks.
1.2.5.4.2.6.2. Con: We are already way past 7 billion people today and we need to prepare the world for tomorrow. Meat production is simply a waste of nutrients we cannot afford much longer. Limiting meat production instead of forbidding it would only make it a luxury good, thus even more desirable for the masses. Countries which once had only little meat consumption already copy the western lifestyle of eating lots of meat, because it is a symbol of wealth. Meat should be a symbol of exploitation instead.
1.2.5.4.2.6.3. Pro: It's not about the meat. The problem is unconscious consumerism. We eat far more meat than we need and buy far more stuff than we should. We need to look at the bigger picture instead of thinking that just ceasing to eat meat alone will solve the problem.
1.2.5.4.2.6.4. Pro: The population growth is predicted to flatten out in 2100. By then there will be [11.2 billion \(Page 2, figure 2\)](https://esa.un.org/unpd/wpp/Publications/Files/WPP2017_KeyFindings.pdf) people on Earth. If we reduce the consumption of beef and eat more pork, fish and chicken, then we will be fine.
1.2.5.4.2.7. Pro: [Meat is an unnecessary luxury food](https://makewealthhistory.org/2007/04/23/meat-is-a-luxury/) in a world of [food wastage](https://static5.businessinsider.com/image/56e1b879dd0895bb478b467d-960/ti_graphics_food-waste-regions-map.png) and [localized oversupply](https://assets.weforum.org/editor/KAPPoMvLpzHTC3IVCkz3T14jpvXwPAP7Z5eZubq6fr0.jpg).
1.2.5.4.2.8. Pro: We live in the 21st century and should progress out of the less civilized ways of living such as eating meat. The vegetarian movement will lead to more innovation as the meat industry ages and becomes obsolete. Humanity could advance ideas such as [feeding the future population](https://www.forbes.com/sites/ronaldholden/2017/11/04/its-called-vertical-farming-and-it-could-be-the-future-of-agriculture/#f787ccf11752) and [colonizing other planets](https://phys.org/news/2017-03-food-mars-earth-nasa-usu.html) when moving away from meat.
1.2.5.4.2.8.1. Con: Civilized people, in cultures around the world, eat meat.
1.2.5.4.2.8.1.1. Con: Just because civilization have less civilized ways \(such as eating meat or crime\) does not mean we should accept it. We should instead work on getting rid of these actions.
1.2.5.4.2.8.1.1.1. Con: You cannot compare an 'uncivilized' action such as eating meat to moral wrongdoing such as crime.
1.2.5.4.2.8.2. Pro: A desire to make vegetarian lifestyles more appealing or convenient have certainly lead to some innovations in food science, such as the development of "lab-grown" meat, or various other meat substitutes. It has also advanced the development of conventional food replacement systems, such as Soylent or Huel.
1.2.5.4.2.8.3. Con: The idea that eating meat is less civilized than not eating meat is a subjective value judgement, which is neither sufficiently justified here, nor widely accepted.
1.2.5.4.2.9. Con: Just because something potentially becomes a problem in the future does not alone require it to stop today.
1.2.5.4.2.9.1. Con: It is important to be cautious of future consequences when qualifying the morality of an action. The scarcity of resources in the future is a relevant implication of eating meat in this discussion.
1.2.5.4.2.9.2. Con: Because of the anticipation of scarce resources in the future, we ought to begin conserving resources now by stopping meat consumption.
1.2.5.4.2.9.3. Pro: There is no possible way to account accurately for how the advances of technology will be able to solve current limitations we have. You can't assume conditions will always be the same.
1.2.5.4.2.9.3.1. Pro: This was a common theme back in the 1960's perpetuated by the book "Population Bomb" in which author reasoned incorrectly that the food supply would not keep up with the then current rate of population growth and everyone would have starved by now. However, because of Norman Borlaug and the "green revolution" that never occurred. Learn more about it in this [video.](http://www.freethinkmedia.com/shows/wrong/1/were-all-gonna-starve/)
1.2.5.4.2.10. Con: The land and water supply [is so low already](http://www.worldwatch.org/node/554) that soon we will have to find food sources that do not so heavily rely on agriculture.
1.2.5.4.2.10.1. Con: This is empirically false. The article at worldwatch references United Nations Food and Agricultural Organization \(FAO\). FAO we can see that land used for wheat, most common staple, have decreased by 25% while production has increased due to much greater yield per acre. 1986 vs 2016: [www.fao.org](http://www.fao.org/faostat/en/#data/QC)
1.2.5.4.2.11. Pro: Once someone eats a plant, they can use the [scraps to grow new food](https://www.diyncrafts.com/4732/repurpose/25-foods-can-re-grow-kitchen-scraps). Regenerating food takes pressure off the food system. The same cannot be said for meat.
1.2.5.4.2.12. Con: Hunger and starvation worldwide [have been in decline even with a growing population until recently](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/global-hunger-rising-after-decade-decline-who-report/) and the recent increase is caused by war and global warming. Nothing indicates this growth to be a result of less meat production.
1.2.5.4.2.13. Con: The growing food needs of the world's population can be met whether or not we stop meat production.
1.2.5.4.2.13.1. Pro: How much meat to produce will be solved automatically by supply and demand. If food is scarce, prices will rise, and the most efficient forms of production will be favored.
1.2.5.4.2.13.1.1. Con: Waiting for the market to adapt will cause extinctions, and massive food shortages.
1.2.5.4.2.13.1.2. Con: Food shortages will primarily harm the world's extreme poor, who have very little purchasing power and are unlikely to be able to affect market trends.
1.2.5.4.2.13.1.3. Con: As long as there are wealthy consumers in high-income countries willing to purchase meat as a luxury good, even food scarcity will not eliminate meat production.
1.2.5.4.2.13.1.4. Con: In order for this to apply, supply needs to be limited. Right now the amazon rainforest is being cleared to make room for cattle. This is not efficient or sustainable.
1.2.5.4.2.13.1.5. Pro: [Historical evidence](https://ourworldindata.org/extreme-poverty/) validates this. 200 years ago the world population was under a billion and 95% of humans were living in "absolute poverty". Today we have a global population of 7.2 billion and only 10% of humans are living in absolute poverty. Overpopulation is a myth. It has been disproven time and time again since Thomas Malthus popularized the notion in the 18th century.
More humans = more innovation = less scarcity.
1.2.5.4.2.13.2. Con: The world's population will live in less ideal conditions by the continued production of meat products, compared to [plant](http://www.onegreenplanet.org/environment/facts-about-animal-agriculture-and-air-pollution/) products.
1.2.5.4.2.13.3. Pro: Starvation is due to people not having access to food, as opposed to there not being enough food to go around.
1.2.5.4.2.13.3.1. Pro: Globally, we currently produce a large food surplus; enough to provide for a growing world-wide population. Oxfam notes that "The world produces 17% more food per person today than 30 years ago." [oxfam.ca](https://www.oxfam.ca/there-enough-food-feed-world)

Undernourishment is therefore a problem of food distribution and waste; not reduced productivity from livestock farming.
1.2.5.4.2.14. Con: Eating meat allows humans to get food from a greater number of ecosystems/environments thereby supporting diversity and distributing human impact over a broader base.
1.2.5.4.2.14.1. Pro: Historically, pastoral and hunting cultures have been able to occupy areas in which agricultural societies could not survive. See for example the Inuit people, who live in areas that do not support staple crops for much of the year.
1.2.5.4.3. Con: Adequate food is produced already and output could be increased if required. Low income countries however will have no access to it because the global economy demands payment for goods and price stability for its products so production will be controlled.
1.2.5.5. Con: A lot of food produced in poorer countries is for the consumption of livestock which is then imported as meat to the west. This food could be be used to directly feed people in low income countries.
1.2.5.6. Pro: The farming of animals for meat can be problematic.  For example, when the practice involves using land to produce food for animals at the expense of food for people.  However, I stayed in poor villages in Indonesia where pigs and chickens were fed scraps or scratched for grubs.  Those chickens and pigs did not take any food that was otherwise edible for people and I felt OK to eat the meat they produced.
1.2.5.7. Pro: Countless small farmers make a living from raising chickens, goats and other animals for meat.  If artificial meat supplants that industry it will be just more wealth accumulating to the corporate techie elite.
1.2.5.8. Pro: Many bioregions are incapable of supporting one human let alone whole societies without the use of animals as a necessary part of the foodchain.
1.2.5.9. Pro: An increase in vegetarian or vegan diets could harm the economies of countries who depend heavily on their meat exports for income.
1.2.5.10. Pro: Livestock production accounts for [1.4%](http://www.slate.com/articles/health_and_science/feed_the_world/2014/05/meat_eating_and_climate_change_vegetarians_impact_on_the_economy_antibiotics.html) of the world’s total GDP. The production and sale of animal products account for 1.3 billion people’s jobs, and 987 million of those people are poor.
1.2.5.10.1. Con: If roughly 1B of the 1.3B people producing meat are poor we can assume they would benefit from undertaking more profitable enterprises if there were not the demand.  An economy that permits such poverty for our convenience would suggest, therefore, that eating meat is wrong.
1.2.5.10.2. Con: If we would base our decisions on preserving jobs, hardly any progress could be made since any change makes a certain number of jobs obsolete.
1.2.5.11. Con: Factory farming fosters poverty in the Global South.
1.2.5.11.1. Pro: In [South Africa](http://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s10806-015-9581-8) there are clear effects of meat consumption where local communities' major source of income is replaced by factory farming they cannot compete with.
1.2.5.11.2. Pro: The vast quantities of food which could feed humans is instead fed to livestock animals.
1.2.5.11.3. Pro: In developing countries, intensive livestock farming [obstructs](http://thegreentimes.co.za/negative-impacts-of-factory-farming/) poverty elimination by driving local farmers out of business.
1.2.5.11.4. Con: Not all meat eaters consume meat from factory farming.
1.2.5.11.4.1. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7.1.
1.2.5.11.5. Pro: Meat factories create a very high demand for soybeans and corn which change the production patterns of the global south.
1.2.5.11.6. Pro: Much of the world's massive hunger problems could be solved by the reduction / elimination of meat-eating, as livestock pasture needs cut drastically into land which could otherwise be used to grow food.
1.2.5.11.6.1. Pro: If everyone adopted a vegetarian diet, current food production would theoretically feed [10 billion people](http://www.uow.edu.au/~sharonb/STS300/limits/studies/articles/article2.html) \(56% more people than alive today\), more than the projected population for the year 2050.
1.2.5.11.6.1.1. Con: This would only be true, if also no food were wasted.
1.2.5.11.6.1.2. Con: The world already produces enough food for [several billions](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/eric-holt-gimenez/world-hunger_b_1463429.html) more, even when eating meat.
1.2.5.11.6.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.4.1.1.5.2.
1.2.5.11.6.3. Pro: [100 million people](http://www.vegsource.com/news/2009/09/how-to-win-an-argument-with-a-meat-eater.html) could be adequately fed using land freed if Americans reduced their intake of meat by 10%.
1.2.6. Con: -> See 1.1.3.9.1.
1.2.7. Pro: Systems-based agricultural models are often reliant on meat production, both as an ecological service and money maker. Ceasing meat production would limit those farmers from receiving both those benefits.
1.2.8. Pro: Animal agriculture is an important part of local food economies in cold climates where many crops are not available year-round.
1.2.8.1. Con: New technologies can allow plant foods to grow in artificially controlled environments, for example aquaponics. It would be more energy intensive, but with the parallel rise in renewable energy, this may curtail some of the negative effects of energy intensive processes.
1.2.8.2. Con: Traditional and contemporary methods of preserving food can be used to make sure food harvested earlier in the year is stored for the winter.
1.2.8.2.1. Con: This may not be able to provide for unexpected rises in demand.
1.2.8.2.1.1. Con: Most countries have access to global markets, and can trade non-food goods and services for food from other countries to meet any gaps on local production.
1.2.8.3. Con: -> See 1.2.8.2.1.1.
1.2.9. Pro: If subsidies related to farming animals were removed, the demand for meat would decrease due to higher prices and lower supply; allowing for reduction in meat consumption without a very unpopular and difficult to regulate law.
1.2.9.1. Con: There are just as many subsidies for the growth of plant based foods. The same argument could be made for most foods.
1.2.9.2. Con: Nobody has suggested \(in this branch of the debate\) outlawing eating meat, or that there should be governmental action to this effect, rather that it is an action we should take, as individuals or as a collective, out of our own free wills or moral imperatives.
1.2.10. Con: In the short term, yes. In the long term not ceasing to waste land and continuing to emit massive amounts of unnecessary greenhouse gasses will incur devastating economic consequences.  Beyond this, optimizing the use of water and ending subsidies for animal agriculture would encourage inevitable growth in other sectors, something which companies like Best Foods have been [compelled to accept](http://www.chicagotribune.com/business/ct-hellmanns-vegan-mayonnaise-20160202-story.html) and are now making vegan mayonnaise after losing their lawsuit over eggless Just Mayo.
1.2.11. Con: Living beings should not be treated as commodities. It would be considered to be dehumanizing if applied to humans, and I believe similar emotional disconnection and distancing even from animals is a bad idea which leads to undesirable results \(abuses, desensitization to all harm including that done to humans, etc.\).
1.2.12. Con: The economic impact may be manageable - it would not be the first time an industry has wound down, or been shut down or suppressed.
1.2.12.1. Pro: It can be compared with the need to lower the depencency of fossil fuel - in the short term there may be negative consequences, but in the longer term, the advantage clearly outweighs the disadvantages
1.2.12.2. Pro: Cultural and technological changes cause economic shifts all the time. Products and whole industries become obsolete or unacceptable. Societies and economies adapt to these changes.
1.2.12.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.3.2.
1.2.12.2.2. Pro: Industries are constantly growing and dying - they evolve with consumer demand. Though there may be additional capital involved in switching from farming animals to farming plant-based products, farmers would make the change to ensure that their crop business remain lucrative. No-one uses floppy disks or rides to work on a horse anymore. Similar principles apply here.
1.2.12.3. Pro: The meat substitutes industry can grow to replace the meat industry, taking jobs from the meat industry and creating new ones.
1.2.12.4. Pro: Meat and the meat industry would simply be replaced with the production of vegetarian foods, meaning the effects on the economy would be minimal.
1.2.12.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.1.
1.2.12.4.2. Con: Agricultural production as of today is already sufficient to cover the demand for the world. Thus, no substitute is needed and no new jobs created.
1.2.12.4.2.1. Pro: The world already produces enough food for [several billions](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/eric-holt-gimenez/world-hunger_b_1463429.html) more.
1.2.12.4.2.2. Con: Agricultural production today is not sustainable due to destructive techniques that deplete the quality of the land.
1.2.12.4.3. Con: It is extremely difficult to transition from farming meat to farming normal agricultural products, and the transitionary period would cause drastic economic harms.
1.2.12.4.3.1. Con: Other land use changes could be considered, for example, returning farmland to natural habitat and gaining revenue from recreational activities.
1.2.12.4.4. Pro: Other food production sectors would grow, meaning companies would require additional human capital to meet the new demand. As such, any jobs lost in the meat industry would simply appear in other food sectors.
1.2.12.5. Pro: We have examples of economic shift working already. In the dairy industry, for example. There are less people drinking milk now, which has caused the plant-milk and other non-dairy industries to flourish.
1.2.13. Pro: Meat keeps food prices high \(due to supply and demand\). With meat taking resources, such as land and water, the food supply is limited for consumers, which pushes the prices higher for food. [This is good for the economy because if food prices go too low, farmers run into difficulties covering their costs.](http://economics.fundamentalfinance.com/micro_price-floor.php)
1.2.14. Con: Meat raises food prices for consumers. Livestock eat grains, which drives up demand for them.
1.2.15. Pro: Many people across the world depend on meat as part of their diet, and ending meat eating would lower food security/diversity for the majority of people.
1.2.15.1. Con: Producing enough meat to provide the entire world's population with a meat-centric diet is not realistic or sustainable with current dominant farming models and a rising global population. Lowering meat consumption while shifting food production towards plant-based foods will give many more people around the world greater food security overall.
1.2.15.2. Pro: There are parts of the world still where meat is the more readily available diet for humans than vegetable products - such as tribal Greenland where fish and seal meat are still majority sources of nutrition.
1.2.16. Pro: Most of what we consume and buy today comes from animal production. It's not only about meat, it also concerns eggs, feathers, leather, but also candy. Stopping the production of meat will impact much more than the "Meat industry", and have a huge impact on global economy
1.2.16.1. Con: Disruptive innovation can increase growth in untapped markets. Tech companies are currently making large investments in the plant based sector. Having a huge impact on the global economy is not necessarily a bad thing, for example, the internet was disruptive, but it created new opportunities.
1.2.16.2. Pro: Leather products are totally dependant on meat consumption. Imagine no leather shoes, belts, jackets or shoes or bags. Other industrial products like fertilizers come from recycled waste products. Then imagine the impact of shutting down the interconnected industries and the loss of jobs and taxes for what?
1.2.16.2.1. Con: There are plenty of plant based or synthetic alternatives to animal materials.
1.2.16.2.2. Con: "Imagining the impact" of these changes is speculatory at best, and does not speak on the core ethics of killing animals for food or materials.
1.2.16.3. Con: [Modern economics teaches](https://www.mruniversity.com/courses/principles-economics-microeconomics/tariffs-quotas-protectionism-definition) that supporting production for production's sake \(protectionism\) is economically harmful, because it takes labor and resources away from production for consumption's sake.
1.2.17. Con: Ceasing to eat meat would increase the economy. Exporting the grains fed to livestock in the US would increase the trade balance by $80 billion. [news.cornell.edu](http://news.cornell.edu/stories/1997/08/us-could-feed-800-million-people-grain-livestock-eat)
1.2.18. Con: This is an advantage as financial pressure is a force for change.
1.2.19. Pro: Global meat production is constantly [rising](http://www.worldwatch.org/global-meat-production-and-consumption-continue-rise-1). Worldwide meat production has tripled over the last four decades and increased 20% in just the last 10 years. This causes more jobs as the industry expands.
1.2.19.1. Pro: Between 2001 and 2005 the employment growth in the Australian meat industry stood at [10%](https://docs.employment.gov.au/system/files/doc/other/profile_of_the_australian_meat_industry.pdf).
1.2.19.2. Con: Growth in the meat sector is simply due to growing demand for food. When people transition to other food, this demand will allow other sectors to grow instead.
1.2.19.3. Con: The idea of the possibility of constant growth is wrong. It is not possible to constantly grow the meat industry, because we live on a limited planet. Therefore what happened in the past cannot be extrapolated into the future just like that.
1.2.19.4. Con: -> See 1.2.12.3.
1.2.19.5. Pro: Poultry production is the fastest growing meat sector, increasing 4.7% in 2010 to 98 million tons.
1.2.19.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.8.
1.2.19.7. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.5.
1.2.20. Con: According to a study, less meat would come with [economic benefits](http://www.pnas.org/content/113/15/4146.abstract) due to lower [healthcare costs](https://web.archive.org/web/20080517050751/http://www.worldwatch.org/press/news/1998/07/02/) and fewer lost workdays associated with deaths from specific diseases caused by poor diet, adding up to an impressive savings of between $700 and $1,000 billion annually.
1.2.20.1. Con: 18% of USA GDP is spent on healthcare. If there was a drastic reduction in demand for healthcare it could result in a recession and a loss of healthcare jobs \(for the USA at least\).
1.2.20.1.1. Con: This claim implies poor health is desirable as it results in increased demand for healthcare. Few would agree.
1.3. Con: Eating meat is a central part of human nature, evolution, and physiology/biology and thus its consumption is inherent to humankind.
1.3.1. Con: Buying and consuming processed meat from intensive livestock farming is anything but natural.
1.3.1.1. Pro: We may only talk of a 'natural' process when observing the ways of indigenous tribes such as the Inuit, who hunt and prepare their meat themselves, and do not over-consume or waste their prey. The majority of humankind today do not share these same, natural practices.
1.3.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.4.1.2.3.
1.3.1.3. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7.
1.3.1.4. Pro: Meat requires [preservatives](http://www.foodauthority.nsw.gov.au/_Documents/industry/preservative_use_in_processed_meats.pdf) so it does not spoil.
1.3.1.5. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.6.
1.3.1.6. Pro: Chaffing male chickens right after their hatching is anything but natural.
1.3.1.7. Con: By the same logic one could argue that vegetarianism through the consumption of milk produced and food grown on large-scale farms is anything but natural.
1.3.1.7.1. Pro: Modern agriculture is neither natural nor ecologically functional as it relies heavily on monocultures, [genetically modified crops](http://www.statista.com/statistics/217108/level-of-genetically-modified-crops-in-the-us/) and chemical fertilizers.
1.3.1.7.2. Pro: The dairy and egg industries cause extreme animal maltreatment that is arguably on a par with the meat and fishing industries.
1.3.1.7.2.1. Pro: It is only true in theory that the dairy cows and laying hens are not killed in order to supply these products, but in practice, they are: these animals are usually killed at whatever point the farm considers to be the most profit-maximizing, generally when they have become too old and are used up.
1.3.1.7.2.1.1. Pro: After around two years, when their egg production stops, these “spent” hens are shipped to [slaughterhouses](http://www.peta.org/issues/animals-used-for-food/factory-farming/chickens/egg-industry/). By this time roughly 29% of those hens are suffering from broken bones resulting from neglect and rough treatment.
1.3.1.7.2.1.2. Pro: A cow’s natural lifespan is about 20 years, but cows used by the dairy industry are typically [killed](http://www.peta.org/issues/animals-used-for-food/factory-farming/cows/dairy-industry/) after about five years because their bodies wear out from constantly being pregnant or lactating.
1.3.1.7.2.1.3. Con: It is possible to implement more ethical farming methods for vegetarian products.
1.3.1.7.2.2. Pro: [In The Netherlands](https://www.cbs.nl/en-gb/news/2012/39/growing-number-of-dairy-cattle-have-no-access-to-pasture), more than half of all dairy cows have no access to pasture and more than a quarter are tied into stalls.
1.3.1.7.2.3. Pro: Many dairy cows suffer from [claw disorders](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18096964) and [infections.](https://dairy.ahdb.org.uk/technical-information/animal-health-welfare/mastitis/recordstools/incidence-rate/#.V0bPGJF96Hs)
1.3.1.7.2.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.4.1.2.6.
1.3.1.7.2.5. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.4.1.2.5.
1.3.1.7.2.6. Con: While this claim is true, it is not an argument for eating meat, but an argument against use of all forms of animal products.
1.3.1.7.2.7. Con: This is not a necessary condition of dairy and egg farming. It is possible to treat cows and chickens humanely, and many farms do so. Consumers who seek out products prepared in this way, or who even raise their own cows or chickens, do not contribute to this maltreatment.
1.3.1.7.2.7.1. Con: It is similarly possible to raise and kill animals in a maximally humane way. So if consumption of dairy is acceptable so long as it is raised in a particular way, the consumption of meat is also acceptable so long as the meat is raised in that way.
1.3.1.7.2.7.1.1. Con: Killing an animal inevitably and by definition ends its life. This could be considered to be an immoral act however it is carried out, especially as it robs the animal of whatever experiences, pleasure and/or enjoyment it may have got out of the rest of its life. Conversely, keeping animals for non-meat products while treating them humanely and well would allow them to enjoy their full natural lives while producing useful products.
1.3.1.7.2.7.1.2. Con: Unfortunately, Dairy Cows only produce milk once pregnant \(and shortly thereafter\). If a calf is male, it is often \(even on small farms\) killed, as it is more expensive to raise it. Or, it is sold to veal farming, which is inherently cruel \(I can explain further if needed\). If a calf is female, it's stolen away from the mother and not allowed to drink any of the milk, because the milk must be sold for money for humans. This process, even without overt visible cruelty, is very, very cruel.
1.3.1.7.2.7.2. Con: There is no such thing as "humane" treatment of animals when the final outcome is slaughter.
1.3.1.7.3. Con: Non-vegetarians consume these products too.
1.3.1.7.3.1. Con: Yet meat eaters are, following this argument, less hypocritical in choosing the practices they criticize and the food they do not consume.
1.3.1.7.4. Pro: Our consumption of milk is unnatural and cruel.
1.3.1.7.4.1. Con: Ants [directly "milk" aphids for their honeydew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honeydew_\(secretion\)), so while saying no other animal drinks another's milk is true, other animals do actively drink other animals secretions in a symbiotic way.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1. Con: There is nothing symbiotic about humans' consumption of cows' milk, meaning their relationship is simply exploitative.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1. Con: Humans feed, house, and protect cows as our end of the symbiosis.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1. Con: Given humans kills many cows for their meat, it is not clear that they could be viewed as protecting cows or having a particularly close relationship with them.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: An abuser is not a protector when their own actions are worse than the outside world they are supposedly "protecting" their victim from. This is true of the conditions created inside factory farms.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2. Con: Animals in the wild often endure a great deal of suffering due to violent deaths from predators, starvation, or exposure. A peaceful life on a farm is plausibly preferable to a life in the wild.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2.1. Pro: Wild animals almost invariably suffer more than domesticated animals properly farmed. Even a wild animal suffering the relatively peaceful death of kidney failure will likely be awakened when carnivores and scavengers begin eating their helpless bodies alive. There is no end to a wild life that is not brutal.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2.1.1. Con: Animals in the wild have freedom of movement and other increased choices not available to farm animals. Quality of life is not decided purely by length or absence of suffering, or how its end is met.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2.2. Con: This is contingent on the farm in fact being ethical, and depending on exactly how it is run there are still plausible reasons why a life in the wild could be better.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2.2.1. Pro: It is not just how an animal dies that matters, but how it lives. A free life, even one with a \(temporarily\) painful end, is arguably preferable to a life in a cage, especially when some of the more barbaric and cruel factory farming practices \(de-beaking, other forms of un-anaesthetized mutilation, insufficient health care to prevent diseases from spreading across the herd, etc.\) come into play.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2.2.1.1. Con: This is a claim against factory farming, not eating meat. There are many ways to humanely raise and harvest the animals.
1.3.1.7.4.1.1.1.1.2.2.1.1.1. Con: Eating meat creates the demand which drives factory farming.

1.3.1.7.4.1.2. Pro: Dairy cows are well fed, protected from weather and disease, and generally are far better off than their wild cousins.
1.3.1.7.4.1.2.1. Con: This depends on the farming method. Conditions on factory farms are often torturously unpleasant to the animals involved. \(And not much better for the human workers sometimes!\)
1.3.1.7.4.1.3. Pro: Humans are not the only animal that 'milks' another \(ants/aphids\), though it can be argued that humans are the only mammal that drinks the milk of another, only that drinks milk past weaning, this is no more 'unnatural' than much human activities. In fact, human evolution allowed for and selected for milk drinking past weaning and of another animal as in several human populations mutations arose and [naturally selected for us to drink milk](https://www.nature.com/articles/5201297) of another mammal past weaning.
1.3.1.7.4.2. Con: This argues that how we do this practice is cruel, but not that the practice itself is cruel.
1.3.1.7.4.3. Con: There is no reason to assume that a natural lifestyle is essential \(healthwise or morally\), as there are plenty of reasons for humans to follow an "unnatural" lifestyle.
1.3.1.7.4.3.1. Pro: Thanks to un-natural means such as modern medicine the lifespan of humans has [increased tremendously](https://www.nia.nih.gov/sites/default/files/global_health_and_aging.pdf). The lifespan of our closest primate relatives, who are presumed to live a natural lifestyle, is [merely half](http://bigthink.com/videos/natures-calling-how-long-should-humans-live) of ours.
1.3.1.7.4.3.2. Pro: Only through the development and wide-spread use of medical inventions, such as vaccinations, was it possible to protect humans from or even eradicate various naturally occurring infectious diseases.
1.3.1.7.4.3.2.1. Pro: Until the Mid-20th century it was natural for millions to suffer from smallpox, many of whose victims went blind and died. The disease was responsible for [300 to 500 million deaths](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smallpox) in the 20th century - but was [successfully eradicated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smallpox#Eradication) through the use of vaccinations by 1980.
1.3.1.7.4.3.2.2. Con: Vaccines are based on parts of the bacteria or the virus that make up a disease. In this sense, the working ingredient of vaccines [is actually natural](http://www.chop.edu/centers-programs/vaccine-education-center/vaccine-safety/immune-system-and-health#.V2Mvbfl96Hs).
1.3.1.7.4.3.2.2.1. Con: "Unnatural" steps are required for their production, such as interfering with disease cells to create vaccines.
1.3.1.7.4.3.2.3. Pro: The wide-spread use of un-natural vaccines was able to decrease the worldwide cases of Polio [by 99%](http://www.who.int/mediacentre/factsheets/fs114/en/) since 1988: From 305.000 to 74.
1.3.1.7.4.3.2.4. Con: Vaccines work through a [natural mechanism](http://www.newyorker.com/tech/elements/think-vaccines) and merely provoke the human immune system to produce its own, perfectly natural anti-bodies to viruses and diseases.

Many jobs that involved long hours in this position thus put a strain on the spine and the surrounding muscles, which leads to [wide-spread](http://www.nytimes.com/2011/06/25/health/25consumer.html) chronic problems.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3. Pro: Vegetarian diets generally lead to better health outcomes than omnivorous diets.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1. Pro: Scientists have concluded that vegetarian diets can in fact [provide benefits](http://freefromharm.org/featured-articles/catching-up-with-science-burying-the-humans-need-meat-argument/) in the treatment and prevention of certain diseases.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.1. Pro: Eating [plant foods instead of animal-based foods](https://freefromharm.org/featured-articles/catching-up-with-science-burying-the-humans-need-meat-argument/) can bring about health benefits including reducing the chances of high blood pressure, diabetes, stroke, and some types of cancer.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.1.1. Con: The niacin in animal protein decreases VLDL and LDL, the mostly-fat bad cholesterol that clog arteries, and increases HDL, the mostly-protein good cholesterol that removes arterial plaque.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.2. Pro: A major [study by Oxford University](http://www.oxfordmartin.ox.ac.uk/news/201603_Plant_based_diets) concluded that universal adoption of vegetarian diets could avoid 7.3 million deaths per year by 2050.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.2.1. Con: This study confounds three or four causes and conflates them with a more plant-based diet when their effects are not correlated with a more plant-based diet.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.2.2. Con: The studies that claim animal over plant diets use more resources such as fuel, irrigation, land, and fertilizer discount the fuel spent to transport crops from the climates suited to them like volcanic, tropical, and marine environments \(e.g. 9000 miles for coconuts between Oceania and America\) and the greater land and fertilizer use for human crops on soils that don't natively support staples.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.2.3. Con: India has a wide adoption of vegetarianism but its lifespan lags France, whose diet is rich in saturated fat and livestock, by 20 years.  The leading cause of death in India is heart disease.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.3. Con: There is much we do not yet understand about gut health and how the body metabolises and interacts with foods.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.4. Con: Individual studies might show advantages to a vegetarian diet, but [literature reviews](https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2014/03/science-compared-every-diet-and-the-winner-is-real-food/284595/) show no significant gains when all the various popular diets are compared to each other. Many different diets based primarily on the idea that we should eat whole food and mostly plants all show substantial health gains. We don't need to remove meat to achieve the health outcomes -- we just need to make sure we get enough plants and focus on unprocessed foods.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.5. Pro: Eating meat is no longer necessary due to the range of meat substitutes on offer.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.5.1. Con: The flesh substitutes are crumbly instead of stringy and are made from beans whose estrogens are bad for males, from monoculture sources of saturated fat like coconuts, and from starch fillers.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6. Pro: The [American Academy of Nutrition and Dietetics](https://freefromharm.org/featured-articles/catching-up-with-science-burying-the-humans-need-meat-argument/) has stated that well planned vegetarian diets are nutritionally adequate and appropriate for individuals at all stages of life.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.1. Pro: According to the [American Dietetic Association](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/american_dietetic_association_vegetarian_position.pdf) a vegetarian diet can meet protein requirements, provide all the essential amino-acids, necessary vitamins, fats and minerals.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.1.1. Con: Vegetables may contain [toxins and antinutrients](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetable#Nutrition_and_health) which interfere with the absorption of nutrients.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.1.1.1. Con: These toxins can easily be deactivated by adequate cooking.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.1.1.1.1. Con: Aflatoxin, cyanogenic glycosides, glycoalkaloids, hypoglycin, acetogenins, glucose-6 phosphate, allergens, acrylamide, PAHs, acetaldehyde, and nitrosamine are not deactivated by cooking.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.2. Con: Well planned diets are good for people who have time, and money for them, but many people just don't have that amount of time to invest, or the funds to accommodate them, so for them, a simple diet involving meat is a necessity.

1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.3. Con: Well planned diets are not always effective. Vegetarian sources of protein are not always effectively processed, leaving some people malnourished. Even when the meal contains adequate supplies of protein it won't always be absorbed.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.7. Con: In the long run \(many years into the diet\), vegetarianism makes people depressed, as stated by Lierre Keith in her book The Vegetarian Myth.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.8. Pro: The idea of a meatless diet being weak or deficient in protein is not accurate as we know some of the strongest animals on Earth are vegetarian.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.8.1. Con: The human metabolism is much [different](http://baloun.entu.cas.cz/~cizek/EkologieLesaPrednaska/InsectPlantInteractions/Allometry%20and%20Ecology%20of%20FeedingBehavAndDigestiveCapacity.pdf) from that of elephants, gorillas, and cattle. These animals spend a majority of their time eating and their stomachs are designed to process hard to digest plant matter. Humans are not designed to eat purely plants in the same way and therefore cannot subsist on the same diet and expect the same results.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.8.1.1. Con: This argument doesn't say anything about strength or protein, only metabolism - so con.

These amino acids are necessary for optimal functioning and protein synthesis. Animal proteins are closer to our protein source, providing a complete array of amino acids needed in our body
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.8.3. Con: Fishes eat plankton, some mammals eat only meat , some only vegetables. Comparing humans to other species that are not similar in their metabolism and dietary need is a fallacy at best and illogical in nature.

1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.14. Con: The same species does require very different nutrients. Diet varies by age \(enzymes and fatty acids for extremes\), sex \(saturated fat, calcium, iron for women\), and culture \(tastes and enzymes\).

1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.2. Pro: Those who eat meat are far more likely to contract cancer than those following a [vegetarian](http://time.com/9463/7-reasons-vegetarians-live-longer/) diet.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.3. Pro: [USDA researchers](https://www.peta.org/living/food/meat-contamination/) have found that eating two ounces of chicken per day \(the equivalent of a third to a half of a boneless breast\) exposes a consumer to 3 - 5 micrograms of the most carcinogenic form of arsenic, which can dramatically increase cancer risk.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.3.1. Con: There is no direct reference to the study here. Severe confounding or methodological challenges is possible.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.4. Pro: Eating meat, particularly processed meats and bacon, has been recognized by the World Health Organization to be [carcinogenic](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/24148709).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.4.1. Con: The carcinogens in processed meats come from heat and vegetal and mineral nitrites, not flesh.  The same carcinogens are present in potato chips, heated oils, prunes, and carrots.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.5. Con: Recent research implies that cancer is a metabolic decrease, which in part forms the basis of the ketogenic diet \(eating meat and good fat\). [Cancer is a metabolic disease](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3941741/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.6. Con: Most dietary cancers come from plants: PAHs from carbs; acrylamide from carbs; acetaldehyde from ferments like alcohol, soy sauce, and overripe fruit; aflatoxin from wheat fungus; nitrites from parsleys.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.4.7. Con: Studies done on negative health consequences of meat consumption are done in high carbohydrate diets. Carbohydrates are closer linked with cancer than meat consumption. 
[Starving cancer: Dominic D'Agostino at TEDxTampaBay](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3fM9o72ykww)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5. Pro: Farming meat leads to wider health risks in agriculture.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.1. Pro: [Diseases](http://theweek.com/articles/457135/5-modern-diseases-grown-by-factory-farming) such as BSE, MRSA or [bird flu](http://ecohearth.com/eco-zine/food-and-garden/865-swine-flu-bird-flu-and-bse-three-legacies-of-factory-farming-.html) are connected to intensive livestock farming conditions.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.1.2. Pro: Dirty, crowded conditions on factory farms can propagate sickness and disease among the animals. These diseases also lead to human infections.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.1.2.1. Con: In Europe the regulation of factory farming, called the [Five Freedoms](http://aldf.org/blog/u-s-lags-far-behind-europe-in-protections-for-farmed-animals/), prevents sickness and stops diseases from spreading.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2. Pro: The livestock sector contributes to human [health problems](http://www.europarl.europa.eu/climatechange/doc/FAO%20report%20executive%20summary.pdf) and the emergence of antibiotic resistance.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.6.1.13.2.6.7.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.2. Pro: Farmed animals are fed a wide variety of drugs to fatten them faster and to keep them alive in conditions that would otherwise kill them. These drugs enter the human food chain through direct consumption or through pollution of our waterways.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.2.1. Pro: 75 % of the antibiotics used on livestock are not absorbed by the animals and are excreted in waste, posing a [serious risk](http://www.worldwatch.org/global-meat-production-and-consumption-continue-rise-1) to public health.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.2.2. Pro: Meat from factory farming contains a number of [growth hormones](https://www.organicconsumers.org/scientific/growth-hormones-fed-beef-cattle-damage-human-health) that are detrimental to our health.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.2.2.1. Con: [Chicken](http://www.thepoultrysite.com/articles/2812/chickens-do-not-receive-growth-hormones-so-why-all-the-confusion/) meat contains no growth hormones.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.2.3. Pro: [55%](http://www.vegsource.com/news/2009/09/how-to-win-an-argument-with-a-meat-eater.html) of U.S. antibiotics are fed to livestock.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.3. Pro: There is [concern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antibiotic_use_in_livestock#Concerns_about_antibiotic_resistance) about meat consumption contributing to the rise in antibiotic resistant infections in humans.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.2.4. Pro: There is widespread overuse of antibiotics which creates antibiotic resistant bacteria.[Antibiotics Overuse in Animal Agriculture](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4638249/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.3. Con: This is only true of CAFO or Industrial meat production.  Organic silvopasture, permacultural, and organic intensive grazing meat production do not create the same health risks. They do not use antibiotics and animal waste doesn't build up. It is, instead, immediately turned into fertilizer. Animals are kept away from areas of the pasture long enough for the waste to be incorporated into the soil and for the plants to recover.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.4. Pro: While animals are still alive, they are normally fed antibiotics to make them larger. If you take too many antibiotics, they will be ineffective. So if you eat too many animals with antibiotics, you won't be able to take antibiotics when you are really sick, causing possible death.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.5.5. Pro: [Animals cause vegetarian foods to get contaminated, which leads to food-borne illness. Eating meat increases the capabilities of animal products \(such as manure\) to contaminate crops \(such as using manure for fertilizer or wastewater for irrigation\).](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4265071/)This could lead to people who do not eat meat \(such as vegetarians\) to be affected \(i.e. sick\) by it, even though they do not contribute to the problem.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6. Con: Meat effectively delivers important nutrients for humans.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.1. Pro: Meat is a great [source](http://www.webmd.com/diet/iron-rich-foods) of heme iron, which is important for the human body.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.1.1. Pro: Too little iron causes [iron](http://www.webmd.com/diet/iron-rich-foods)-deficiency anemia, a decline of red blood cells. Without sufficient iron, the human body is not able to produce enough hemoglobin, the important oxygen carrier. Symptoms are weakness, fatigue and irritation.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.1.2. Pro: The body absorbs 15% to 35% of the heme iron in meat, but only absorbs 2% to 20% of the non-heme iron found in vegetarian sources like leafy greens and beans. \([vegetarian.procon.org](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/nih_dietary_supplement_fact_sheet_on_iron.pdf)\)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.1.2.1. Con: -> See 1.1.3.9.3.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.1.3. Pro: [Iron deficiency is the most common and widespread nutritional disorder in the world.](http://www.who.int/nutrition/topics/ida/en/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.1.4. Con: Iron is an oxidant and can harm the DNA of our cells. Non-heme \(vegetable\) iron is safer for us, since the body can absorb only what it needs, unlike heme iron. [nutritionfacts.org](https://nutritionfacts.org/video/the-safety-of-heme-vs-non-heme-iron/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.2. Con: The human body does not require consumption of animal protein.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.2.1. Pro: All the high-quality amino acid [proteins](http://www.npr.org/sections/13.7/2016/05/19/478645426/humans-are-meathooked-but-not-designed-for-meat-eating) we require are readily available in plants such as buckwheat, quinoa and potatoes.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.1.6.1.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.2.3. Pro: There are enough [non-animal protein](http://www.health.com/health/gallery/0,,20718479,00.html) sources humans can consume.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.2.4. Con: Just because the human body can live without eating meat doesn't rationalize living without it, nor does it justify that something is unhealthy.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.2.5. Con: Eating meat or being able to live optimally without it or on alternative diets has been shown to be coded at a genetic level and this varies from one human to another. It is not always a simple moral or lifestyle choice.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.3. Con: One of the foods with the [highest](https://www.healthaliciousness.com/articles/foods-highest-in-protein.php) protein to calorie ratio is cheese, which is not a meat product.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.3.1. Con: The top four foods referenced in the article are all meat. Non-fat cheese is not commonly consumed.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.4. Pro: Meat is packed with protein. While there are other ways to get protein, lean meats are an extremely healthy and efficient way to obtain it.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.4.1. Con: Animal protein has a low pH and causes problems in our kidneys.[nutritionfacts.org](https://nutritionfacts.org/video/which-type-of-protein-is-better-for-our-kidneys/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.4.2. Con: Protein can harm the colon.[nutritionfacts.org](https://nutritionfacts.org/video/bowel-wars-hydrogen-sulfide-vs-butyrate/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.4.3. Con: Animal protein stimulates hormones such as IGF-1, which can be used by cancer to fuel growth.[nutritionfacts.org](https://nutritionfacts.org/video/animal-protein-compared-cigarette-smoking/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.5. Con: Vegetarians/vegans generally consume a diet consisting of [less](http://www.livestrong.com/article/481795-the-statistics-of-vegetarians-vs-meat-eaters/) saturated fat and cholesterol than the average meat eater.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.5.1. Con: There is next to [no scientific evidence](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nhzV-J1h0do#action=share) that a high-fat diet leads to a high cholesterol level; in fact, a high-fat diet turns out to be healthy in many ways.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.5.1.1. Pro: [Many if not most hunter-gatherer societies ate a higher fat diet than is currently recommended by Western governments](https://www.nationalgeographic.com/foodfeatures/evolution-of-diet/). Our understanding of human nutrition is far from complete. in this context, following a higher fat diet is a less risky proposition than following a low fat diet.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.5.2. Con: [A high cholesterol level](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nhzV-J1h0do#action=share) has not been finally determined to be the cause of coronary heart diseases; there has merely been found a correlation. Latest research counters the assumption that a high cholesterol level is concerning.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.6. Con: A meatless diet helps build healthy bones because vegetarians absorb more calcium than meat eaters.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.6.1. Pro: There are many sources of healthy [vegetarian calcium](http://drlisawatson.com/40-vegan-calcium-sources) including tofu, dark leafy greens like kale, spinach, and collard greens, as well as fortified cereals.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.6.2. Con: A meatless diet does not guarantee a higher absorbtion of calcium, because vegetarians can also eat unhealthy food and maintain an unbalanced diet.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.6.3. Pro: Meat has high renal acid levels which the body must neutralize by [leaching calcium](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/pcrm_protecting_your_bones.pdf) from the bones, which is then passed into urine and lost.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.7. Con: [Good fats](http://www.health.harvard.edu/staying-healthy/the-truth-about-fats-bad-and-good) come mainly from vegetables, nuts, seeds; not from meat.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.7.1. Con: It is highly debatable what fats are good and which are bad. We have been living under a lot of assumptions about fat. Polyunsaturated oils are chemically less stable than saturated fats. [What if its all been a big fat lie.](https://www.nytimes.com/2002/07/07/magazine/what-if-it-s-all-been-a-big-fat-lie.html)
[Saturated fat is safe… this is the science that says so](http://anograiner.com/fat-chemistry/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8. Pro: Without a carefully balanced diet non-meat eaters could suffer from certain deficiencies, like [protein](http://vegetarian.lovetoknow.com/Protein_Deficiency_Symptoms#Fur0di7vVrR60mUF.97) or [vitamin B12](http://www.webmd.com/food-recipes/guide/vitamin-b12-deficiency-symptoms-causes#1).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.1. Con: Non-meat eaters have enough [protein sources](http://www.bbcgoodfood.com/howto/guide/best-sources-protein) they can choose from, such as eggs, soya, beans and nuts.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2. Pro: Meat is the best source of [vitamin B12](http://ajcn.nutrition.org/content/78/1/131.long), a vitamin necessary for the nervous system and digestive system health.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.1. Con: Even if B-12 cannot be sourced directly from one's diet, supplements are widely available in many health-food stores and chemists.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.1.1. Pro: Many breakfast cereals, vegetal milks and other products are fortified with B12
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.2. Pro: Meat is the most accessible source of those vitamins, particularly in poor countries. Growing chickens is the [easiest way to get more rich in vitamins food](https://www.gatesnotes.com/Development/Why-I-Would-Raise-Chickens).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.3. Con: Vitamin B-12 is [also found](http://www.nhs.uk/Livewell/Vegetarianhealth/Pages/Vegetarianmealguide.aspx) in eggs, dairy, fortified cereals and soya products, and yeast extract.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.4. Pro: Supplements are less accessible than meat to most people.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.4.1. Con: This may change as technology, societal/moral standards, and human behaviour change and evolve.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.5. Con: There are only rare cases of vitamin B12 deficiencies and mostly this is [no problem](https://www.drmcdougall.com/misc/2007nl/nov/b12.htm) or easy to fix.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.5.1. Con: Vitamin B12 deficiency is not rare but extremely undiagnosed due to doctors not running serum tests routinely. The serum tests aren't quite accurate either and functional ranges vary between countries. There are more sensitive markers for B12 deficiency that are now available including methylmalonic acid \(MMA\), measured both in the serum or the urine...there’s another marker called holotranscobalamin II \(or holoTC\) mostly used in Europe but is way more accurate. [chriskresser.com](https://chriskresser.com/why-b12-deficiency-is-significantly-underdiagnosed/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.3. Con: -> See 1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.3.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.9. Pro: Maintaining a meatless diet in a meat-eating society is costly and requires nutrient planning.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.9.1. Pro: Many of the minerals/vitamins found in meat are not in easily digestible forms from other sources.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.9.2. Con: If society as a whole transitions away from eating meat, there will be more support structures and systems in place to make alternative sources of nutrition more viable.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.9.3. Con: Most staple vegetarian foods, like beans and rice, are very cheap. Meat is expensive. Vitamin b12, the main problem for vegetarian diets can be supplemented cheaply.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.10. Pro: Rapid evolution of humans was directly supported by the high protein diet of eating meat.  Meat diets provide more energy and nutrients that are more filling and energy efficient than plant based diets. Thus, precious time and energy is saved with the more efficient meat diet. Time and energy that can be used for different things like evolution, education, and technological advancements.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.10.1. Pro: Many scientists point to the time at which humans began to eat meat as a major event in humanity's evolution. It contributed to a drastic increase in our intelligence, according to Leslie Aiello, an anthropologist and director of the Wenner-Gren Foundation in [this NPR article](https://www.npr.org/2010/08/02/128849908/food-for-thought-meat-based-diet-made-us-smarter).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.10.1.1. Con: This does not mean that continuing to eat meat will necessarily have any ongoing positive effects on humans.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.10.2. Con: Other claims elsewhere already dispute the suggestion that meats are faster and more efficient to cook and eat in modern society.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.11. Pro: Vegetables do not sufficiently contain the nutrition needed by the human species, and additionally the much larger space requirements because of lower caloric density mean that relying on vegetation alone is not likely to be feasible, especially in comparison with the feasibility of creating ethically sound animal husbandry conditions and even changing to use less-neurologically-complex organisms as food sources, such as shrimp and aquaponics.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.12. Con: There is no one-size-fits-all regiment for optimal health and nutrition for human beings. It may very well be that some of us are more genetically wired to thrive on vegetable only diets while others need to metabolize meat.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.13. Con: Neal Barnard of the [Physicians Committee for Responsible Medicine](http://www.pcrm.org/media/experts/neal-barnard) notes that when people switch from meat-eating to plant-eating, their intake of vitamins and other nutrients improves.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.14. Con: Plant protein products are improving. You can receive the same levels of proteins and vitamins without the chemicals and hormones found in meat products. [thrivemarket.com](https://thrivemarket.com/garden-of-life-raw-organic-meal-replacement-shakes-vanilla?utm_source=google&utm_medium=pla&ccode=FIRST3&ccode_force=1&utm_medium=pla&utm_source=google&utm_campaign=Shopping_Health_Beauty&utm_content=658010116022&utm_term=google-pla_na&gclid=EAIaIQobChMIoOyxk7Oo1wIVS5V-Ch3m_gASEAYYCCABEgJkivD_BwE)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.15. Pro: It is difficult and more expensive to achieve the protein requirements for best possible health without eating meat.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.15.1. Con: If plant-based protein sources become more widely accepted and produced, they will be cheaper and easier to obtain.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.15.2. Pro: Animal proteins are complete proteins and thus a more efficient source of amino acids.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.16. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.4.2.3.7.3.4.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.17. Pro: Meat is essential for a healthy diet, especially for developing and maintaining muscles.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.17.1. Con: Meat is not 'essential'. All nutrients found in meat can be found in plants, bacteria or can be made within the human body.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.17.1.1. Con: Vegetarians and vegans are more likely to be deficient in [Vitamin B12](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5188422/).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.17.2. Con: [Many world class athletes follow a vegan diet](https://www.vegansociety.com/whats-new/blog/ten-best-plant-powered-athletes), proving that meat is not essential for developing and maintaining muscles.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.18. Pro: The bioavailability of vegetable matter is much lower than meat for human beings. Not only is meat cellular tissue far more similar in constitution to our own cells than plant cells, but it is far easier, for example, to extract the majority of iron available in red meat than it is for us to extract iron present in vegetation such as spinach, only a small fraction of which is available.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.19. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.8.2.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.20. Pro: It may be arguable that essential nutrients in meat are generally more bioavailable from those sources. For example, omega-3, choline. It is also arguable that mineral balances such as copper-zinc that are recommended for health are identical to that which one would receive from a meat heavier diet, rather than plants. Likewise saturated fats serve essential roles in the composition of hormones, in the brain, heart and liver. In other words, in the long run, a vegan diet may be harmful.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.20.1. Con: Nutrient supplements are available in today's society, and are widely used to supplement a vegetarian or vegan diet.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.20.1.1. Pro: When more people stop eating meat it will be more interesting to produce better and more affordable supplements.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.20.2. Con: The typical diets of meat eaters have a lot of [evidence showing them to be harmful](http://www.whatthehealthfilm.com/facts/) and have a particularly strong association to diseases of affluence. For example, heart disease, which is caused by atherosclerosis, the build up of plaque in the arteries. [Erectile dysfunction is an early warning sign of atherosclerosis \(by the age of 40, there is a 40% chance of ED which then goes up 10% a year\).](https://youtu.be/OVXzT_RBxFk)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.21. Pro: Meat has been shown to be an [important component](http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0309174012003385) of a balanced diet.

1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.22. Pro: Ceasing to eat meat can lead to health problems as replacing it with plant-based materials requires a plethora of different types of plants to get every nutrient needed.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.23. Pro: Eating meat is good for the brain \(check the link\), and nutrients are absorbed easier \(see how cows spend all the day chewing grass\). [www.businessinsider.com](http://www.businessinsider.com/5-brain-nutrients-that-you-cant-get-from-plants-2013-10)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.24. Con: There are more efficient and sustainable methods for putting nutrients into our body than eating meat. These include [synthesizing nutrients from chemicals](http://www.doctorsresearch.com/articles4.html), modifying existing foods to use [less resources](http://c4rice.irri.org/index.php/component/content/article/19-about/55-why-c4-rice) or [have more nutrients](https://www.npr.org/sections/thesalt/2013/03/07/173611461/in-a-grain-of-golden-rice-a-world-of-controversy-over-gmo-foods), and [individually growing food](https://www.seeker.com/food-helmet-sustains-you-with-algae-1767693118.html). Way out there is [people being genetically enhanced to become autotrophs](http://www.bbc.com/future/story/20120906-will-humans-ever-photosynthesise).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.25. Pro: There is [some evidence](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3137939/) that ceasing to eat meat would harm brains of those who are in the developmental age.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.26. Pro: A Stone Age diet is the most natural and beneficial diet to the human gut. Meat and fats and some grains and fruit. Studies have shown that those people who follow this ancient way of eating are less susceptible to diabetes, heart disease and cancers. Take a look at this article which shows how fat is very important to the human diet.[files.meetup.com](http://files.meetup.com/1463924/Homo%20Carnivorous-WAPF2.pdf)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.27. Pro: Some of the most healthful nutrients come exclusively or in greater bioavailability from animals sources: liver containing CoQ10, B vitamins, zinc, iron, chromium and other trace minerals, bone broth containing collagen supporting compounds such as hyluronic acid and glucosamine. While vegetarian diets can be healthful, they lack many nutrients that, while present in vegetables, have much less bioavailability. Humans thrive only when consuming moderate amounts of healthy animal food sources.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.28. Pro: Animals process a vegetarian diet. Meat is the effect of that process - and this is why meat packs more nutrients in than vegetables. The organs and bones of the animal are particularly high in essential nutrients.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.6.29. Pro: Eating just the cooked muscle is unhealthy. When meat is cured it increases it's bio availability and introduces good bacteria which facilitates digestion; coupled with eating bone broth and organs, eating meat in this way is extremely healthy.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7. Con: [Statistically](http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article/asset?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0088278.PDF) those who abstain from a meat based diet are exposed to higher health risk hazards.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.1. Con: The study cited has methodological flaws and therefore its results are uncertain, i.e. the number of participants \(330\) is too small to be representative and the measure of life quality is insufficient.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.1.1. Pro: The study had very [bad reviews](http://www.nhs.uk/news/2014/04April/Pages/Vegetarians-have-poorer-quality-of-life-study-claims.aspx) on health platforms.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.1.1.1. Con: This "health" platform recommends quackery like a diet with much fruits and vegetables, when the only benefit to those is the fibre which can be gotten from insects and shellfish whereas their [antioxidants](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antioxidant) do not improve health but may worsen it, and low saturated fat, when women who eat less saturated fat die earlier.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.1.2. Pro: There are [other more thorough studies](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4073139/) that conclude the opposite.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.2. Con: The study was comprised of self-reported data with very little explanation about what constituted each dietary subset. It's hard to draw any significant conclusions from self-reported data.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.3. Pro: Vegetarianism is linked to reduced physical and mental health, increased risk of allergies and specific forms of cancer. Vegetarians, who are on average more health conscious than the general population, are twice as often sick, and spend twice as much money on doctors, when compared to equally health conscious meat eaters. [journals.plos.org](http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article/file?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0088278&type=printable)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.4. Con: This relies on cherry-picked data, when there is much more data and research which concludes otherwise. A [meta-analysis](https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamainternalmedicine/fullarticle/1832195?hc_location=ufi) is a better way to get a larger spectrum of properly representative data.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.7.5. Pro: Ketosis is a state of metabolism that cannot be achieved without consuming meat.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8. Pro: Meat-eaters suffer more frequently from various types of [food poisoning](http://www.celestialhealing.net/physicalveg3.htm) than vegetarians.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.1. Pro: According to the US Department of Agriculture \(USDA\) 70% of food poisoning is caused by contaminated [animal flesh](http://www.earthsave.org/pdf/ofof2006.pdf).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.2. Con: The CDC \(Centers for Disease Control and Prevention\) published in a [report](http://www.medicalnewstoday.com/articles/255645.php) that leafy green vegetables like lettuce or spinach are among the top sources of food poisoning.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.2.1. Pro: Between 1998 and 2008, 46% of all cases of food [poisoning](http://edition.cnn.com/2013/02/01/health/vegetables-foodborne-illness-time/) in the USA were caused by leafy green vegetables.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.2.2. Pro: Leafy green vegetables cause 80% of all [E.coli](http://www.medicaldaily.com/salmonella-food-poisoning-most-common-vegetables-not-meat-325070) cases in the USA.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.2.3. Con: According to the same study, poultry was responsible for the most deaths, affecting 19% of fatal cases. Meat and poultry combined were responsible for 29% of deaths. So, despite the frequency of vegetable-related illnesses, they were not the most harmful.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.2.4. Con: Officials from the CDC have emphasized that most of the vegetable-related sicknesses came from norovirus, often passed by food handlers and cooks. Thus, contamination is more related to how the kitchen or restaurant handles the food, rather than the actual food itself.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.3. Con: Seedy vegetables \(tomatoes, zucchinis\) are responsible for more [Salmonella](http://www.medicaldaily.com/salmonella-food-poisoning-most-common-vegetables-not-meat-325070) infections than any kind of meat in the USA.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.4. Con: Food poisoning occurs in cases of poor preparation of food and poor food hygiene. There is nothing more inherently risky in eating meat than in eating vegetables.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.5. Con: In terms of severity \(hospitalizations and deaths\) vegetarian diets offer no significant advantage for avoiding food poisoning. Hospitalizations and deaths \([wwwnc.cdc.gov](https://wwwnc.cdc.gov/eid/article/5/5/99-0502-t3)\) are mostly due to listeria, salmonella, and toxoplasma gondii. None of these have any particular vegetarian advantages.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.8.6. Con: The largest food poisoning disasters \(dwarfing all others\) are chemical contamination of grain products. For example the 
[Iraq poison grain disaster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971_Iraq_poison_grain_disaster) or this case of [toxic cooking oil in spain](https://www.theguardian.com/education/2001/aug/25/research.highereducation).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9. Pro: Living without meat reduces [metabolic risk](http://care.diabetesjournals.org/content/34/5/1225.abstract) factors and thus reduces the likelihood of strokes, diabetes, and heart conditions.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.1. Pro: A compound found in red meat, called [carnitine](http://www.prevention.com/health/health-concerns/carnitine-red-meat-linked-risk-heart-disease), has been found to cause atherosclerosis, the hardening or clogging of the arteries.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.1.1. Con: It is mainly the consumption of [fresh food](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8842068) that has a positive effect, rather than whether they eat meat.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.9.2.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.3. Con: Amy Keating, a dietitian from Consumer Reports, says, "Many people replace the meat with refined carbohydrates," \([Nov. 2017 Consumer Reports](https://www.consumerreports.org/healthy-eating/eat-smarter-eat-healthier-sugar-salt-fat-gluten/)\), and these types of vegetarians have an increased risk of heart disease by 32%.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.3.1. Pro: Refined carbs/sugars are definitely not a suitable replacement for meat/dairy.  There is very little to be gained from substituting one unhealthy thing for another.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.3.2. Con: The statement that some of a group of people who are healthier because of not eating meat sometimes choose to eat unhealthy foods does not in any way make abstaining from meat a problem. Eating refined carbs or processed food is bad in and of itself regardless of vegan or not. This argument is comparable to saying that since some people who quit smoking chew more gum, then quitting smoking is bad for your teeth. In short, this is a non sequitur.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.4. Pro: Eating meat [has recently been linked with developing Type 2 diabetes.](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3942738/)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.5. Con: Alternative factors, such as that vegetarians smoke less and have an overall [healthier lifestyle](http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-2849819/Vegetarians-healthier-meat-eating-cousins-not-happy-prone-mental-health-issues.html), are strong alternative variables.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.5.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.1.1.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.6. Pro: [Vegetarians](http://time.com/9463/7-reasons-vegetarians-live-longer/) have lower blood pressure, are less likely to be overweight, and have less chance of heart diseases.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.6.1. Pro: According to a peer-reviewed study of 76,000 people, vegetarians had 24% [lower mortality](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10479225) from heart disease than meat eaters.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.6.2. Pro: A 2006 [meta-study](http://www.susanberkow.com/PDF/vegdietsandweightstatus3.pdf) that compiled data from 87 studies found that vegetarian diets are associated with reduced body weight.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.6.3. Pro: High consumption of red meats has been shown to be associated with greater risk of morbidity and mortality from cardiovascular disease [sciencedirect.com](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/B9780123739605005414).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.6.3.1. Pro: Eating animal products increases your risk for cardiovascular diseases and several other diseases, as advocated by Dr. Caldwell Esselstyn \(Cleveland Clinic\), Dr. Dean Ornish \(founder of Preventative Medicine Research Institute\), and Dr. Michael Greger. A meta-analysis of 96 studies is attached: [tandfonline.com](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/10408398.2016.1138447)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.7. Pro: A meatless diet helps prevent hypertension, and thus reduces the risk of [stroke](http://vegetarian.procon.org/sourcefiles/hypertension_and_blood_pressure_among_meat_eaters_fish_eaters_vegetarians_and_vegans_in_epic_oxford.pdf).
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.8. Pro: Doctors often suggest vegetarian diets to help with hormonal chronic conditions like PCOS and Endometriosis. While the science of why is inexact, vegetarian diets seem to help alleviate symptoms.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.9. Pro: The lead cause of diabetes type ll is eating read meat, its actually the first link and it is as toxic for our organism as cigarettes are. You can watch it on the WHO website.[harvardmagazine.com](https://www.harvardmagazine.com/2012/01/a-diabetes-link-to-meat) you can see the first fact in here by Harvard University researchers, which I consider are highly recommended
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.10. Con: Stopping eating meat can lead to more illness. It has been [shown](https://elpais.com/elpais/2014/11/26/buenavida/1417006731_060496.html) that people who don't eat meat present more allergic, carcinogenic and cardiovascular pathologies than meat consumers.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.10.1. Con: A [study](http://www.cell.com/cell-metabolism/abstract/S1550-4131\(14\)00062-X) out from University of Southern California found that eating a diet rich in animal proteins \(red meat, chicken, dairy\)  during middle age makes you four times more likely to die of cancer than someone on a low animal-protein diet — a mortality risk factor comparable to smoking.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.10.2. Con: Dr. Barnard \(president of the Physicians Committee for Responsible Medicine \(PCRM\)\) discovered that eating meat is consistently associated with an elevated diabetes risk, regardless of age. [Reference](http://www.mdpi.com/2072-6643/6/2/897)
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.10.3. Con: A [recent analysis](https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamainternalmedicine/fullarticle/1832195?resultClick=3) of seven studies by PCRM demonstrates that a vegetarian diet reduces the risk of hypertension.
1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.9.10.4. Con: Meat contains Carcinogenic compounds, leading to stomach cancer, breast cancer, Kidney, Colorectal, Prostate Cancer and pancreatic cancer. [See sources here](http://www.pcrm.org/health/cancer-resources/diet-cancer/facts/meat-consumption-and-cancer-risk)
