1.12.4.4.3.2. Pro: More resources are used to make up for what is lost. For example, another animal has to be raised for the meat that went spoiled.
1.12.4.4.3.2.1. Pro: This causes more animals to die than if the animal did not die in vain \(such as if the meat is eaten right away, another animal does not have to die to make up for the lost meat\).
1.12.4.4.4. Pro: Even waste from vegan food makes up for the loss \(that meat cannot achieve\) multi-fold. For example, not eating fruit helps the plant that wasted fruit came from. Here, the cycle of life continues because a person can plant the seeds to grow a new fruit tree that bears more fruits. This more than makes up for the one fruit that went to waste.
1.12.4.5. Pro: Many revered thinkers and most of the [collectively recognized geniuses](https://www.elephantjournal.com/2011/02/the-worlds-greatest-geniuses-are-vegetarians/) of every age followed and promoted some form of vegetarian diets \(Pythagoras, Socrates, Plato, da Vinci, Francis of Assisi, Newton, Darwin, Einstein, Tesla, Edison, Tolstoy, Franklin, Luther King… and far more recurrent among the Eastern philosophy figures. Also in modern times of every discipline: Van Gogh, Kafka, Henry Ford, Stephen Hawkins, Antoni Gaudí, Bill Gates, Carl Lewis, Matt Groening, etc\) [en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_vegetarians)
1.12.5. Pro: Conscious vegetarianism facilitates compassion towards other living beings and discourages us from viewing them as mere ingredients to a recipe.
1.12.5.1. Con: It is hard to feel sympathy for being one never sees, or interacts with, even if the alternative is only seeing them as part of a meal.
1.12.5.2. Con: Many who eat meat also feel compassion towards other animals. It is very possible to research where your meat comes from to ensure that no cruel methods were used in raising the animal, and in the case of hunting, thinning the population allows for expansion of resources, allowing the survivors a greater ability to thrive. This also allows their offspring more room to grow with less competition.
1.12.5.3. Con: Conscious vegetarianism facilitates a lack of compassion toward other living beings because they see plants as mere ingredients to a recipe.
1.12.5.3.1. Con: Plants are able to survive losing a large portion of their biomass, and many produce fruiting bodies deliberately intended for consumption by animals. Meanwhile, harvesting an animal for meat kills it 100% of the time. It is more possible to compassionately harvest \(some\) plants than animals.
1.12.5.4. Pro: Specifically, it facilitates the reduction of suffering among living beings capable of suffering. Reducing suffering is good.
1.12.5.4.1. Con: Not all moral systems are centred on the reduction of suffering.
1.12.5.4.1.1. Pro: Some moral systems \(i.e., [deontologically-based](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deontological_ethics) ones\) classify actions - or even thoughts, goals, and ideals - as right or wrong, and are effectively based around maximizing "right" actions and avoiding or reducing "wrong" ones.
1.12.5.4.2. Con: If reducing suffering is the only measure of good, the logical conclusion is that we must end all life to end all suffering. This is inherently wrong.
1.12.5.4.3. Con: If reducing suffering is good, but we do not have to end suffering entirely, then responsible farming of domesticated livestock accomplishes this end, as few domesticated animals living in these circumstances will suffer as much, or die as miserably as their wild counterparts.
1.12.5.4.4. Con: If the only moral factor is 'reducing suffering is good', then a responsible hunter who kills their prey quickly is more moral than a vegan who eats foods harvested from large fields where animals are caught and maimed by harvesting equipment. The hunter is more responsible than that same group because field crops cause animals to reproduce more quickly, only to have their food supply eliminated as winter approaches, with few natural predators nearby to bring them swifter death than starvation.
1.12.5.4.5. Con: I don't think we can say definitively that it reduces suffering. Are plants capable of suffering? I know some would say so. Are insects capable of suffering? How would you define suffering? Is one creature's suffering more relevant than another's? Which is worse, the death and suffering of a million insects, a hundred mice, or a single cow?
1.12.5.5. Con: The above claimant presumes to know what human beings "feel" when they eat meat, and how those human beings view life. It is an inaccurate representation, and therefore it is invalid.
1.12.5.6. Con: Conscious living facilitates compassion toward other living beings. Vegetarianism is not a necessary component of this.
1.12.5.7. Pro: By consuming farmed meat you are [ingesting the suffering and trauma those animal experienced in their short lives](http://sciencenordic.com/meat-stressed-animals-unhealthy) which has potential metaphysical consequences we cannot comprehend.
1.12.5.8. Pro: Eating someone or parts of someone is contradictory to compassion. Compassion involves the understanding of suffering and its reduction as much as possible. It is unlikely that there is not any suffering associated with the steps involved in eating a living being.
1.12.5.9. Pro: Love for fellow Earthlings would include the notion that our lives are precious and, therefore, we are not something to be eaten.
1.12.5.10. Pro: The thinking man must oppose all cruel customs no matter how deeply rooted in tradition and surrounded by a halo. When we have a choice, we must avoid bringing torment and injury into the life of another, even the lowliest creature; to do so is to renounce our manhood and shoulder a guilt which nothing justifies. - Albert Schweitzer
1.12.5.11. Pro: A large majority of meat eaters either have a pet, want one or watch cute cat videos with an "aww" type of reaction. That again shows the fact that we have the innate ability to think compassionately about animals and not think of them as supper.
1.12.5.11.1. Pro: It also shows, once again, that we are irrationally biased towards certain animals.
1.12.5.11.2. Con: Thinking compassionately about animals and thinking of them as supper are not mutually exlusive. In fact, the vast majority of farmers producing meat think very compassionately about their animals and ensure their well-being. Not just for economic, but for moral and compassionate reasons.
1.12.6. Con: Morality is subjective, so eating meat is not necessarily immoral.
1.12.6.1. Pro: Humans subjectively determine what has moral value, and the majority of humans place significantly less moral value on the lives of farm animals than the incomes and pleasure of humans.
1.12.6.1.1. Con: Humans subjectively determine what has moral value for humans. It is possible and probable other animals with social structures have their own sense of morality. Several animals have shown that they understand what is fair and not fair, including [chimpanzees](http://www.pnas.org/content/110/6/2070.abstract), [crows](http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0056885), and dogs. [Capuchin monkeys](https://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2003/09/0917_030917_monkeyfairness.html) have rejected rewards when they saw them as unfair or unequal to rewards given to their peers. Surely a recognition of fairness equates a type of morality. Humans are not the sole arbiters of moral value.
1.12.6.1.2. Con: Moral relativism is a weak standard of morality, with no true consideration of why things are wrong, it is only an example of [stage 4 of Lawrence Kohlberg's stages of moral development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawrence_Kohlberg%27s_stages_of_moral_development). We need a better reason, a real reason why things are right, or wrong, like [overall happiness,](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utilitarianism) [rights,](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_contract)or [good will.](https://kantphilosophy.wordpress.com/kants-ethics/the-good-will/)
1.12.6.1.2.1. Con: This position assumes out of hand that some things are definitively wrong. Yes, a strong moral system gives us a tool for "objectively" decrying actions that we disagree with, but saying that moral relativism is a weak standard doesn't affect whether or not it is real.
1.12.6.1.2.1.1. Con: We are a part of reality, and thereby can shape it to an extent. If we choose to enforce certain standards, they are "real" to an extent as they have force on our interactions with physical reality, and thereby effects on physical reality.
1.12.6.1.2.1.2. Con: By moral relativism's own measure, it is not real, but an opinion one has with no grounding, or weight.
1.12.6.1.2.1.3. Con: If one uses a what they feel is right to determine their moral system instead of using their moral system to determine what is right, they are by no measure using a moral system.
1.12.6.1.2.1.4. Con: If moral relativism is true, everything is permissible, full stop.
1.12.6.1.2.1.4.1. Con: Moral relativism claims that moral standards are relevant to a person's culture and context. This does not mean that everything is permissible, since moral standards still exist, they are simply not the same for everyone.
1.12.6.1.2.1.4.1.1. Con: But it allows for the existence of other cultures, and it is conceivable that things in other cultures are not wrong, so there is no bases by which one could object to any action. All actions must be found to be permissible.
1.12.6.1.2.1.5. Con: This assumes out of hand that nothing is definitely wrong.
1.12.6.1.2.1.6. Con: We've seen morality in it's effect on the world, and we've seen the same moral concepts pop up independently in all corners of the world. Morality exists, and there is good reason to believe it is objective.
1.12.6.1.2.1.6.1. Pro: Almost any human would agree that, for example, torturing infants for fun is immoral. The fact that there is disagreement on more complex moral issues does not imply that there is no capacity for universal agreement on moral facts.
1.12.6.1.3. Con: Majorities are not always correct, and the original subject of "humans should stop eating meat" is prescriptive, i.e., discussing what we should start doing rather than what we are. Potentially changing societal opinions and perspectives is well within the scope of this debate.
1.12.6.1.4. Con: Humans do not subjectively determine what has moral value. For example, humans could not subjectively determine that some races have fewer rights than others.
1.12.6.1.4.1. Con: Humans can determine whatever they want, just look back in history. The apartheid regime of South Africa or the Nazi German concentration camps. Or even further back to the time of the Roman Empire.
1.12.6.1.4.1.1. Con: Each of those historical instances eventually fell apart by intervention from other countries to disrupt their immorality. Thus humans do clearly \(eventually\) determine and enforce subjective moral norms.
1.12.6.1.5. Con: Animals have preferences, as frequently demonstrated through their actions, so under preference utilitarianism their demonstrated preferences should be taken into account.
1.12.6.1.5.1. Con: Taking into account preferences of different animals and trying to please all of them will eventually fail. Humans might have higher moral standards than other animals but humans still are animals that have preferences.
1.12.6.2. Pro: It is cruel, but morality is a very relative concept. In the perspective of the animal kingdom, we are part of the omnivore group, and eating meat is what our species do, as many many others. Applying morality to nature is pointless, many other species cause harm to many others. Applying the term morality to meat eating is pointless and counterproductive to the actual goal: to reduce harm to some animals.
1.12.6.2.1. Con: The very first human societies were naturally gathered tribes, so applying morality to nature is not pointless - it is in fact a significant part of how humans became and continue to be what we are today, as moral constraints to our natural state formed a significant part of shaping modern society and the modern quality of life we enjoy. They can similarly help to improve animals' quality of life.
1.12.6.2.2. Pro: The illusion of being more than nature or above nature is created by actual society. The detachment from simple things as finding our own food make us believe we are not animals but the biology says otherwise.

The comparative harm of eating say, an oyster, versus a higher plant which may, according to studies have a central nervious system depends on philosophical assumptions that are unprovable, such as that plants do not feel, or the degree to which animals feel.
1.12.6.3.1. Con: Bivalves are marginal cases which aren't really relevant to the majority of animal agriculture.  It's readily provable that a pig can feel pain and suffering in a way that a carrot cannot.

For example, some humans chose to treat other humans less morally, such as criminals or simply a person they don't like based on their ideology, therefore, it is normal for humans to be "cruel and immoral" selectively, including to animals.

1.12.6.9.1. Con: Humans are the only species on our planet with the power of sophisticated ethical reasoning. It is because of this that we can be bound by morality, which can include prescriptions about how we should or should not act on our environment and other beings in that environment.

But the author states that morality applies to humans. This is a contradiction, and therefore the claim taken as a whole is logically invalid.
1.12.6.9.2.1. Con: This argument is based on the assumption that there is only one meaning to the word "natural", whereas there clearly are at least two: natural as in encompassing the entire universe, and natural as opposed to artificial or anything derived from human thought and action.
1.12.6.9.3. Con: We already apply moral concepts to non-human animals in most societies. Forms of animal cruelty are illegal in many countries, showing that we can intuitively and practically apply moral reasoning to non-human animals.

1.12.7. Con: Ceasing to eat meat would mean that vast quantities of livestock would die without being replaced as they are unable to survive effectively outside of human agriculture.

1.12.7.4. Pro: Veganism is endangering animals. Diversity of all kinds is worth preserving. Without demand for animal products the majority of domesticated animal breeds would become extinct. Cows do not exist in the wild, they exist within the framework of supply and demand. Just because animal diversity was created by humans doesn't make it less valuable than natural diversity. Treat animals well within the supply and demand structure. Don't prevent them being born by removing the need for them.
1.12.7.4.1. Con: Bringing animals into existences which will bring them only suffering is cruel and immoral.

With many species being sustained solely to provide nutritional purpose, veganism would effectively disincentivise the further preservation of these species. Notably, cattle, chickens, and sheep come to mind.

Consuming other species is inherent to human existence; It is naive to congratulate oneself on only killing and consuming a certain variety of life.
1.12.10.3. Pro: Time is relative for each living thing. Plants/trees live for 100s of years, they just don't feel the same amount of pain as animals do because of their slow growth. However, you're still hurting them. For example, think of us as trees and mosquitoes as humans.
1.12.10.4. Pro: Increased farming to produce more plant foods will result in an increase in the amount human exploitation in countries where work regulations and workers rights are poor. Perhaps these concerns should be addressed first?
1.12.10.5. Con: We don't eat other humans. Why? Because we're so similar to them, so we feel strong empathy. Animals share much of the same DNA, biology and even emotions as humans, so we feel strong empathy for them as well. Plants, however, are from a separate biological kingdom, and work very differently from both humans and animals. Although we do have to eat some organic food to survive, we can choose the source that causes the least suffering from our human perspective.
1.12.10.6. Con: Workers can suffer in both plant and animal agriculture, so this not an argument for or against either of them.
1.12.10.7. Con: Eating botanical fruit from plants is not damaging to the plant in any way, so it is not cruel. Some vegetables are actually, in the botanical sense, fruit. Conversely, eating root vegetables, for example, is damaging to the plant. But since plants are not biologically designed to feel pain, it is not cruel to eat them.
1.12.10.8. Con: Assuming this was true, consuming meat indirectly consumes vast amounts of plants that are used as animal feed. Eating meat means indirectly contributing to the death of both plants and animals, not animals instead of plants.
1.12.10.9. Con: Cruelty suggests suffering. As plants lack any sensory system, and by observation take longer to die, it is perhaps safer to assume that less suffering means less pain. As plants do not experience physical pain, such a claim is moot.
1.12.11. Con: If everyone who cares about the ethical treatment of animals were to stop eating meat, then the only people farming and consuming meat would be those who lack compassion for the animals. Human's relationship with nature should be one of mutual respect and compassion - this will never happen if those who would put this in practice choose instead to have no symbiotic relationship with nature at all.
1.12.12. Pro: We should not rely on other lives \(such as eating animals\) to progress our own. Finding a way to not depend on others for people's existence allows for independence. Then people will not feel compelled to resort to cruelty to survive.
1.12.13. Pro: The effects of this cruel treatment are twofold. Not only does it involve the suffering and murder of billions on an annual basis but also negatively impacts the environment \(methane and phosphorous outputs, deforestation\). Ultimately hurting non-domestic animal species and ourselves in the process
1.12.14. Pro: Take the flesh that the average meat eater consumes and make them take the action of the rearing and slaughtering of the life form behind that flesh, other than letting a fish suffocate most today would find themselves unable. A wrong they can not replicate if not delegated.
1.12.15. Con: There is no part of history which would not be cruel and immoral.
1.12.15.1. Con: [Significant data](https://ourworldindata.org/slides/war-and-violence/#/title-slide) prove a decrease in cruelty and violence throughout history until present day. Animals should not be excluded from this progress.
1.12.16. Con: So many people are worried about animals but don't even think twice when walking by a homeless person on the streets. It's preposterous. How about we worry about our own kind first and then start talking about animals.
1.12.16.1. Con: This implies that caring for animals or caring for people is a binary choice. It isn't. There are those who are well placed and willing to care for people and those who prefer to serve the animal kingdom. As a species we don't just have one idea at a time and follow that to conclusion before we pursue another. It benefits all if humans divide their attentions between various issues and problems we face.
1.12.16.1.1. Con: No one said humans had one idea at a time as a species nor was it implied. It doesn't matter whether one group of people cares for humans and the other devotes to the animal kingdom. This is about individual decisions. If someone cares about another species more than helping out their own then there is a problem.
1.12.16.2. Con: Humans have freedom of choice to some extent, animals subdued by humans don't. The very intention of help urges it to go where is most needed. And so far never was [any biggest](http://www.adaptt.org/about/the-kill-counter.html), flagrant and needless cruelty and slaughter as that towards industrial farm animals.
1.12.17. Con: The statement is unclear as it is not specified what the "majority of cases" are. What delineates those from the others, supposedly not cruel or not immoral?
1.12.18. Con: Moral values are typically pertinent to particular individuals, groups, religions or schools of thought. There are no universally accepted moral values that condemn eating meat or treating animals in any particular way. Therefore the statement that eating meat can involve immoral treatment, is false.
1.12.19. Pro: The ignorance and confusion about how animals are treated may have been deliberately caused by the meat industry [lack of transparency](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2016/10/09/magazine/meat-industry-transparency-fight.html) and [misleading advertising.](https://www.ecowatch.com/dairy-industry-facts-2525727633.html)
1.12.20. Pro: For those who eat meat, it may also mean that they neither have a developed empathy nor a developed compassion - leaving farm animals out of their [circles of compassion](https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/28/einstein-circles-of-compassion/), or just that they don't have [reliable sources of information](https://www.viva.org.uk/blog/meat-myths). \(e.g. ["suicide food".](https://suicidefood.blogspot.com/)\)
1.12.21. Pro: Relating to the standards of good behaviour \(not killing / not imprisoning\), fairness \(not profiting on others pain / not imposing artificial insemination to females or robbing them their byproducts -eggs or milk\), and honesty \(not enslaving entire species -farm animals / not robbing other intelligent and sentient beings offspring to subdue them as well\), [i.e. morals](https://dictionary.cambridge.org/dictionary/english/moral), eating meat is wrong, especially when there are [alternatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_meat_substitutes).
1.12.22. Con: Not eating the meat of animals killed for other purposes would be a waste and thus morally wrong.
1.12.22.1. Con: There are very few opportunities to eat animals killed by non-human causes. Eating only those animals would be very similar to not eating any meat at all.

Given that they animals are already being killed their meat should not be wasted.
1.12.22.3. Con: Selling meat from animals that have been killed anyway creates a demand for meat, which then encourages people to kill more animals than otherwise would have died.
1.12.22.4. Con: Since a lot of institutions and professionals sustain that a diet that contains meat will necessarily cause a lot of health problems for the eater, not eating meat is not a waste. If someone doesn't want to drink poison, we would not say that they are 'wasting' poison.
1.12.22.5. Con: Most of us wouldn't like the idea of eating a pet, regardless of its cause of death. Moral wrongness can vary depending on a person's view of how a dead body ought to be treated, and this subjective moral view varies wildly throughout culture, and from person to person.
1.12.22.6. Con: We don't consider the food we feed to our pets "wasted". Every organism eventually "feeds" the ecosystem in which it dies \(including humans\), thus it's invalid to call organic matter objectively "wasted" simply because humans aren't the ones eating it.
1.12.22.7. Pro: Many societies, admittedly, less that are around today, [cannibalized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocannibalism) their dead for religious purposes, out of reverence for them.
1.12.22.8. Con: Many animals that we eat or commodify were brought into existence by humans and would otherwise not exist. By reducing the demand for meat, we reduce the animals that are killed for any reason. Therefore, it is only a waste because we have created something we do not need.
1.12.22.8.1. Con: Never existing is worse than dying because if you exist you at least were able to experience some form of life.

1.12.22.10. Pro: In practice, yes, but to be precise, eating the flesh from dead bodies is not cruel nor immoral if the act can be shown to never create demand for the murdering of animals. A free-range animal that dies from natural causes could have its body eaten without causing any suffering. Anonymously eating murder meat purely from others' leftovers also causes no suffering. Necessarily cruel and immoral are the various acts of torture and finally the murder, not the flesh-eating part which has exceptions.
1.12.22.10.1. Con: This is not a practically viable method of sourcing meat. Who would watch for such incidental deaths?

1.14.4.5.1. Con: There are many meat eaters which have certain food preferences and will not ever eat certain dishes. However noone would say they are insociable because of that.
1.14.4.5.1.1. Con: Few other food preferences are as widely exclusive as is a meatless diet. Being on a meatless diet is thus on a different level than merely disliking certain ingredients.
1.14.4.5.1.1.1. Con: A [gluten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gluten)-free diet is as exclusive as a meatless diet, as one could not eat anything including wheat and related grains.
1.14.4.5.1.1.2. Con: There are far more staple ingredients in cuisine around the world than meat. Onion, for example, is the world's [most ubiquitous](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/magazine-30549150) foodstuff, "the only truly global ingredient"; eating an onion-less diet would come as a much more major and daily obstacle than a meatless one.
1.14.4.5.1.1.2.1. Con: Onions rarely carry cultural importance, [as opposed to eating meat.](https://meatonomics.com/2016/04/20/hooked-on-meat-how-cultural-beliefs-and-attitudes-drive-meat-consumption/)
1.14.4.5.1.2. Pro: Many people do not like raw fish and would never eat sushi.
1.14.4.5.1.3. Pro: Some people hate the lingering odor of onions and especially garlic and would not eat any meals including these ingredients.
1.14.4.5.1.4. Pro: Some people dislike the \(hot\) spices used in Asian cuisine and thus avoid food from e.g. Korea, Thailand, China etc.
1.14.4.5.1.5. Pro: Quite a few people consistently avoid meals including gluten, lactose or sugar for dietary reasons.
1.14.4.5.1.5.1. Con: These people may have allergies or intolerances and are thus forced to avoid certain meals.
1.14.4.5.1.5.1.1. Con: -> See 1.14.4.2.1.1.1.
1.14.4.5.1.6. Con: Some people overcome their personal food preferences when custom, politeness or necessity require it.
1.14.4.5.2. Con: -> See 1.1.3.5.3.
1.14.4.5.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.5.6.
1.14.4.6. Pro: In many countries - for example [China, Japan and Korea](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=uMnubkF5HjAC&pg=PA3&dq=vegetarianism+concept+korea&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q=vegetarianism%20concept%20korea&f=false) - the very concept of a meatless diet is not widely popular and recognized, hence maintaining a meatless diet can come with obstacles.
1.14.4.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.14.4.1.1.
1.14.4.6.2. Con: There are a lot of vegetarians living in China, Japan and Korea. Thus, it cannot be that difficult.
1.14.4.6.2.1. Pro: Vegetarianism in Korea is becoming a [new trend](http://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/news/nation/2015/04/654_176353.html) with online communities sharing information.
1.14.4.6.2.1.1. Pro: There are [50](http://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/news/nation/2015/04/654_176353.html) purely vegetarian restaurants in Seoul and [150](http://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/news/nation/2015/04/654_176353.html) across the country.
1.14.4.6.2.1.2. Pro: The Korean Vegetarian Union believes [1 percent](http://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/news/nation/2015/04/654_176353.html) of the population are vegetarians.
1.14.4.6.2.2. Pro: According to a 2014 survey [4.7 percent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetarianism_by_country#Japan) of the Japanese population are vegetarian. This is only a bit lower than in Western countries.
1.14.4.6.2.2.1. Pro: And these are only the numbers on strict vegetarians who not only do not eat meat, but also do not eat fish and seafood. The number for non-meateaters should thus be even higher.
1.14.4.6.2.3. Pro: Estimates suggest that  [4 or 5 percent](http://www.pri.org/stories/2013-06-27/vegan-lunch-going-meatless-beijing) of Chinese could be vegetarian.
1.14.4.6.2.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.14.4.6.2.2.1.
1.14.4.6.2.4. Con: These numbers tell us very little about the circumstances and difficulties these non-meat eaters face.
1.14.4.6.2.4.1. Pro: By the same logic, the estimated [5%](http://time.com/3508291/china-underground-churches-catholicism-catholics-christianity-christians-kevin-frayer/) of China's population that are Christians would not face many problems. Yet more than half of them are organized in semi-legal underground churches, which exemplifies the difficulties they face.
1.14.4.6.2.4.1.1. Con: Vegetarianism is in no way legally prescribed in Korea. Thus, the comparison to Christians in China is flawed.
1.14.4.6.2.4.1.2. Con: Roughly [5%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_vehicles_per_capita) of Indonesians do own a car and they do not face problems. Selecting any 5% population to show non-meat eaters statistics are flawed is, at least, equally flawed.
1.14.4.6.2.4.1.3. Con: The difference between Christianity and Vegetarism is that one is an optional thing of belief, whereas the other concerns the intake of food, which is necessary for surviving. The two cannot be compared.
1.14.4.6.2.4.1.3.1. Con: They can certainly be compared, as the original claim compares them on the grounds of both being minority and sometimes persecuted opinions and factions.
1.14.4.6.2.4.2. Con: If many non-meat eaters are living in a place it can be assumed that it is easier than if fewer non-meat eaters live in that place.
1.14.4.6.2.5. Pro: There is an own vegetarian subculture active in Seoul that expresses itself in [magazines](https://www.10mag.com/vegetarian-restaurants-vegan-restaurants-seoul/) and connects in this way.
1.14.4.6.2.6. Pro: The main staple dishes in Korea, rice and kimchi, are produced without meat.
1.14.4.6.3. Pro: In [Korean schools](http://www.koreatimes.co.kr/www/news/nation/2015/04/654_176353.html) there are no meatless dishes offered for children.
1.14.4.6.4. Con: The Buddhist cuisine in East Asian countries is meat-free. This means that traditionally their food is not necessarily including meat.
1.14.4.6.4.1. Pro: A meat based diet is seen as a westernized cuisine while a plant based diet is indigenous.
1.14.4.6.4.1.1. Pro: In [Japan](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=gQcAAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA25&lpg=PA25&dq=vegetarian+statistics+japan&source=bl&ots=NSERwM1wkK&sig=NpnlBLFTKkfCXMt2UBbep2BRsss&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj5-b_hzajNAhUFqJQKHV1cCc84ChDoAQgZMAA#v=onepage&q&f=false) the Americanization of the indigenous diet caused a strong rise in meat consumption.
1.14.4.6.4.1.2. Pro: In [Korea](http://english.yonhapnews.co.kr/n_feature/2012/04/05/21/4901000000AEN20120405001700315F.HTML), it was only with modernization that meat consumption increased drastically.
1.14.4.6.4.1.3. Con: -> See 1.2.5.4.2.3.7.4.1.
1.14.4.6.4.2. Con: Barely anyone outside of Buddhist temples and monasteries lives according to a Buddhist diet.
1.14.4.6.4.2.1. Pro: Buddhism's basic code of ethics for laypeople - the [Five Precepts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Five_Precepts) - does not contain any dietary restrictions but merely prohibits the [active participation](http://www.buddhanet.net/e-learning/qanda08.htm) in killing. Outside of temples and monasteries a vegetarian diet is thus not required from Buddhists.
1.14.4.6.4.3. Con: Buddhism [does](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist_vegetarianism), depending on the school, not advocate a vegetarian diet, and generally not expect laypeople to refrain from eating meat.
1.14.4.6.4.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.14.4.6.4.2.1.
1.14.4.6.5. Pro: At celebrations for the Chinese [New Year](http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/world/china/Chinas-vegetarian-population-touches-50-million-Report/articleshow/29725767.cms) and Korean [Chuseok](http://www.foodrepublic.com/2013/09/19/today-is-korean-thanksgiving-heres-what-you-should-eat/) it is traditionally necessary to offer meat dishes as ritual foods.
1.14.4.6.6. Con: Korean cuisine hosts a variety of non-meat dishes that are widely available, such as Kimchi, Bibimbap, Gimbap, Mandu, Bam, Gamja Jon, Doenjang Jigae, Jap chae, or Jamchi Jigae.
1.14.4.6.7. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.3.2.1.
1.14.4.6.8. Con: -> See 1.1.3.5.3.
1.14.4.6.9. Pro: Traditional restaurants in these countries oftentimes focus on a single, meat-containing dish and offer nothing besides, for example in [Japan](http://www.ibukimagazine.com/focus_on_the_tokyo_food_scene/).
1.14.4.6.9.1. Con: Many of such single-dish restaurants focus on dishes like sushi, tempura, okonomiyaki or noodles \(udon, soba or ramen\), which are generally meatless.
1.14.4.6.9.2. Con: -> See 1.1.3.5.6.2.
1.14.4.6.10. Con: -> See 1.1.3.5.3.1.
1.14.4.7. Con: -> See 1.14.4.5.1.
1.14.4.8. Con: People with certain food allergies / intolerances \([Coeliac disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coeliac_disease), [lactose intolerance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactose_intolerance), histamine intolerance, nut allergies etc.\) will not ever eat certain dishes, but noone would say they are insociable because of that.
1.14.4.8.1. Con: -> See 1.14.4.2.1.1.
1.14.4.9. Pro: It's nearly impossible to live off a vegetarian diet in some areas, like Tibet. [Finding Vegetarian Meals in China](http://liuzhou.co.uk/wordpress/2013/11/27/vegetarian-or-vegan-in-china/)
1.14.4.10. Pro: Not eating meat could be construed as prejudicial against meat eating cultures. For example, the Inuit of the Canadian Arctic, the Chukotka of the Russian Arctic, the Masai, Samburu, and Rendille of East Africa.
1.14.4.10.1. Con: Slavery is banned despite some cultures still practicing it today.
1.14.4.10.2. Con: Not eating meat could be therefore construed as prejudicial against non-meat eating people.
1.14.4.11. Con: The solution to this would be to minimize stigmatization and increase availability of meatless diets, not embrace eating meat.
1.14.4.12. Con: Among all cultures there are people who do not eat certain kinds of meat for [religious reasons](http://www.chewfo.com/philosophical-reasons-for-food-choices/religious-dietary-restrictions/) and they do not seem to be stigmatized as insociable.
1.14.4.12.1. Pro: You cannot prepare pork or meat that is not halal for your Muslim friends for example.
1.14.4.12.2. Pro: You cannot prepare any meat for your Hinduist friends.
1.14.4.12.2.1. Con: The ancient and medieval [Hindu texts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diet_in_Hinduism) do not explicitly prohibit eating meat.
1.14.4.12.3. Pro: You cannot prepare pork or any meat that is not kosher for your Jewish friends.
1.14.5. Con: -> See 1.1.4.8.1.1.9.2.1.1.7.1.7.
1.14.6. Pro: Many religions explicitly permit or encourage eating animals.
1.14.6.1. Pro: According to Mormonism, God [created animals for our use, to eat sparingly](https://www.lds.org/scriptures/dc-testament/dc/89).
1.14.6.1.1. Con: Eating or abusing someone is harmful to their life experience. If any living beings were created with the intention of being eaten and abused, this would indicate that God did not consider their lives to be precious. There is no purpose to the creation of living beings whose lives are not precious.
1.14.6.1.1.1. Con: Life, including animal life, is sacred. The Creator permits the sacrifice of animal life in order to save human life, but [He will require the lives of beasts at our hands.](https://www.lds.org/scriptures/jst/jst-gen/9.10-11.html?lang=eng)
1.14.6.2. Con: Biblical citations and religious assertions alone are not reasoned evidence.
1.14.6.3. Pro: As this is a moral statement, with no declarable moral code defined, the Bible even from a atheistic view is valid here. For example,  \(Romans 14\): "As for the one who is weak in faith, welcome him, but not to quarrel over opinions. 2 One person believes he may eat anything, while the weak person eats only vegetables. 3 Let not the one who eats despise the one who abstains, and let not the one who abstains pass judgment on the one who eats, for God has welcomed him."
1.14.6.3.1. Con: By many forms of moral reasoning \(e.g. utilitarianism\), God is amoral or even sometimes commits evil acts. As such, the Bible does not provide an unambiguous view of goodness.
1.14.6.4. Con: No religion mandates eating animals.
1.14.6.5. Pro: In the Bible, God granted the animals to Noah and his family after the flood, saying "The fear of you and the terror of you will be on every beast of the earth and on every bird of the sky; with everything that creeps on the ground, and all the fish of the sea, into your hand they are given. Every moving thing that is alive shall be food for you; I give all to you, as I gave the green plant. Only you shall not eat flesh with its life, that is, its blood."
1.14.6.6. Pro: Meat was created by God for the righteous use of all of us, his children. The scriptures are eloquent, clear, and common sense on this topic. [1st Timothy Chapter 4 Verses 1-16](https://www.lds.org/scriptures/nt/1-tim/4?lang=eng)
1.14.6.6.1. Con: Meat is, by one definition, the organs or tissues of animals considered to be food. Organs and tissues of living beings were created for the functioning of an individual's living processes, perceptions and actions and not for the nutritional purposes of other animals, including humans.
1.14.6.7. Pro: In the Bible, God tells Adam and Eve not only to have dominion over all animals, but he also gives instruction in the mosaic law as to what types of animals you can and can’t eat. There are dozens more religions that promote certain diets that include meat.
1.14.6.7.1. Con: -> See 1.14.3.4.
1.14.6.8. Con: Jainism encourages vegetarianism on the basis of ahimsa which is the principle of nonviolence and noninjury and is, in the case of Jains, applied to all beings.
1.14.6.9. Con: If God created some living beings subservient to others, this would indicate God doesn't care about the welfare of some of his creations.
1.14.6.9.1. Pro: -> See 1.14.6.1.1.
1.14.6.10. Con: An omnibenevolent God would not create living beings that have the capacity to suffer with the purpose of being eaten and abused which results in suffering.
1.14.6.11. Pro: If the temple in Jerusalem ever gets rebuilt, there will be a need of sacrifices there. That involves killing animals.
1.14.7. Pro: People from rural areas will be ostracized if meat consumption falls because it is far more easy to raise animals than to plow the land.
1.14.7.1. Con: Society is not static. There have been other societal changes that have put pressure on various subsections of society to change their practices and lifestyles \(e.g. the growth of automation in manufacturing, and subsequent fall in manual manufacturing labour\).
1.14.8. Con: A deliberate cultural evolution away from meat will overcome many current cultural issues with not eating meat.
1.14.9. Con: Once a culture has the resources and technological knowhow to live in a way that avoids harms it previously needed for survival, that culture permanently progresses. Other cultures may have a valid argument for consuming meat or other [ESS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionarily_stable_strategy) such as raids involving murder of rival tribes' members. Western culture, with its great abundance and alternate foods, does not.
1.14.10. Pro: -> See 1.1.13.
1.14.11. Con: Culture explains behavior but does not necessarily justify it.
1.14.11.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.8.2.
1.14.11.2. Pro: "Culture" is not important. Cultural behaviors can be positive or negative. The practice of female genital mutilation is not something we should strive to protect simply because it is part of the culture. Slavery was our culture once. People fought and died to preserve that culture, yet the culture was wrong, just as the culture of eating animal products is.
1.14.11.3. Pro: Culture should not dictate morality.
1.14.11.4. Pro: -> See 1.3.8.2.5.
1.14.11.5. Pro: -> See 1.2.3.3.1.1.
1.14.11.6. Pro: Not all cultural or religious values should be respected.  They are not equally valid.
1.14.11.7. Pro: People live traditionally and rarely stop to ask whether our traditions are blinding us from the reality of the cruel way we indirectly treat certain animals. At the root of their treatment is discrimination, which leads to exploitation and abuse. Eating animals in the modern world is cruel because it is no longer necessary to eat animals to survive and live a healthy life. If these animals we not bred into existence, there would be no need for them to exist in the wild.
1.14.11.8. Pro: Eating meat was necessary for survival. Many meat-eating cultures have some inherent respect for the animals they eat. If there is no longer a necessity to eat meat to survive, the slaughter is purely for gratification; we should reduce our consumption, and develop other ways of fulfilling our recreational eating desires.
1.14.11.9. Con: More humans eat meat than choose to abstain from eating meat, and most abstention is poverty based. Whilst non-meat eaters are the more vocal and empassioned cohort on this issue, this does not make them the majority and societal intersubjective truths are generally determined by majority thought constructs. In other words, eating meats is okay because most humans believe it to be okay.
1.14.11.10. Con: It's not ethically wrong since the definition of "Ethical" is "A set of moral values and principles that guide the human conduct in the society". Knowing that, the most part of the society eat meat and don't see any problem in this. We can declare it not ethically wrong.[Ethical Definition \( Brazil Website \)](https://www.suapesquisa.com/o_que_e/etica_conceito.htm)
1.14.11.11. Pro: The argument that something is part of a dominant culture was used to justify numerous evils of human history, from racism to corruption and the suppression of minorities.
1.14.11.11.1. Pro: In the past people were presented to gods as [human sacrifices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sacrifice) or held as [slaves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery). However, these cruel features were eventually abandoned in most cultures.
1.14.11.11.1.1. Con: [Slavery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contemporary_slavery) and [human sacrifices](http://www.mirror.co.uk/news/world-news/human-sacrifices-still-taking-place-5999139) exist as of today.
1.14.11.12. Pro: According to [moral absolutism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_absolutism), particular actions are intrinsically right or wrong.
1.14.11.12.1. Con: According to [cultural relativism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_relativism), judgement of right and wrong are determined by one's own culture and are thus not absolute.
1.14.11.12.1.1. Con: Cultural relativism contradicts itself by arguing that moral principles are culturally dependent, and that we should therefore not impose our morality on others, because, the principle "we should not impose our morality on others" is not culturally dependent.
1.14.11.12.1.2. Con: There are moral systems which can exist and be applied independently of culture, e.g. utilitarianism.
1.14.11.13. Con: As there are no absolute standards for judging right and wrong, good and bad, as these terms are products of social agreement, individuals can only use their culture and the values / attitudes it has created for moral guidance. From this point of view, the dominant culture thus explains and justifies behavior.
1.14.11.13.1. Con: Moral relativism is self-defeating in this case. Suppose all cultures should follow their own ethical codes. It then follows that if our culture's code says that eating meat is unethical, then we should condemn everyone who eats meat, no matter what culture they are from.
1.14.11.13.2. Con: Some cultural practices are obviously wrong. For example, slavery and torture are wrong, even if most people once thought they were right. So there are some universal moral standards that exist independently of cultural opinion.
1.14.11.13.3. Con: -> See 1.12.6.1.2.
1.14.11.13.4. Con: The fundamental moral truth, that pain and suffering in living beings should be minimized as much as possible, has to be the foundation of any discussion and has to supersede cultural values. Otherwise things like slavery and ritual killings would need to be considered morally OK, just because they are part of a certain culture. This would make argument-/logic-based discussions about what is morally right/wrong pointless. Thus, if such a discussion shall take place, culture can't be an argument.
1.14.11.13.5. Pro: According to meta-ethical [moral relativism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_relativism) in such disagreements, nobody is objectively right or wrong.
1.14.11.13.5.1. Pro: Because nobody is right or wrong, we ought to tolerate the behavior of others even when we disagree about the morality of it.
1.14.11.13.5.2. Con: -> See 1.14.11.12.
1.14.11.13.5.3. Pro: According to the epistemological position of "[fallibilism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallibilism)", absolute certainty about knowledge is impossible.
1.14.11.13.6. Con: According to [moral universalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_universalism), a system of ethics applies universally, that is, for all individuals, regardless of culture.
1.14.11.13.7. Pro: All humans are a part of a certain culture and society, which fundamentally characterizes their values and attitudes. Thus behavior of a certain culture can only be judged in comparison.
1.14.11.14. Con: The amounts of culturally-prescribed meat, for example at rituals, are limited and thus come with marginal negative effects. There is nothing to justify.
1.14.11.14.1. Con: Justification is not a question of amount. If something is wrong, it is wrong regardless of the quantity in which it occurs: murdering one person is wrong, as is murdering five people.
1.14.11.14.2. Pro: There are only several occasions per year, such as on [Eid al-Adha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_al-Adha), that eating meat is culturally induced.
1.15. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.7.4.3.3.3.
